O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, my very dear children, I have completed this book which is the end of the science of medicine, its full understanding, and I have concluded it through its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I completed this with a treatise, which is the part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And since the work of hands is highly specialized in our region and foreign to all, the knowledge is lost and cut off, and there is no longer any memory of its strength except for small descriptions in ancient books about what the hands have done.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes error and vanity, and intentions are closed, and knowledge is estranged.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I will revive this treatise by ordering its content according to the method of exposition and explanation, and the brevity; I will bring together the forms of cautery tools and other instruments used in the work, with adjustments to their declaration and preparation as needed.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine has declined.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who wants to excel in the art of anatomy, as Galenus says, must know the judgment of the members, their forms and conjunctions and separations, have knowledge of bones, nerves, muscles, and the number of them, and understand the action and rest of veins and arteries, and from where they originate.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And Hippocrates says that the name without action is meaningless, and the action without knowledge is poor; especially in the art of healing.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the beginning of this book that he who is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned above, risks error and mistaking people; as I have often seen many of those who engage in this science without knowledge or experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a most wondrous sight, which infected the abscess of scrofula in the neck of a woman, and affected the arteries of her neck; so much blood flowed out that the woman died in her hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another wonder: a stone was removed from an elderly man's bladder, and the stone was large; it took away with it a piece of his bladder, and he bled internally for three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone; if it were not removed, he would surely die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another marvel that took in hand the care of a duke from our land who had broken his leg, and with the break, there was an open wound; and all the ignorant healers bound the break over the wound as if by strong magic, leaving no trace of healing to the wound, and left it thus until the leg was entirely gangrened and the pain became unbearable, and it led to his perdition.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	They called me to come to him, and I hurried to free the leg; and when I freed it, he was at peace and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But every way of corruption was already confirmed in the member, and it could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member until the member was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another wonder: the abscess became worse, and then it was inflamed because of the evilness of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For the ulcer, when it is pure of melancholic humor, one should not use iron if it is not in a part that can be entirely removed what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, dear child, it is necessary that you know that the art of medicine is divided into two parts: namely, the work of the hands, which involves great danger in many positions; and I will show each part in this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Therefore, hold fast to this, so that the foolish gaze cannot speak ill of you. If you take up your weapons in courage and undertake your patients gently yet firmly, and use the best means, through the grace of God, you will attain salvation and be happy; and banish the diseases of sorrow from your mind, and lay down your weapons, those which make you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can pass from this world to the other with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen says in none of his warnings: "Do not take too much care of a bad disease, lest you be called a fool.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatment according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter deals with fire cautery and the cautery of medicine (ague), and it is ordered from the head to the feet; and about the forms of instruments, and the tools for cautery, and everything that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and of ventouses (suction cups) and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and this chapter is ordered and includes the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar conditions; and it ordains the use of the main instruments from the head to the feet, and the forms of the tools.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Furthermore, remembering the work, it is necessary that I describe the qualities of aid and the harm of each condition.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid and their harms are the most extensive knowledge and subtle science, and these secrets are revealed; and many sages have spoken about them and agreed on this; and I will be content with little of their words, as I fear the lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery helps universally for all complexes where it has matter, whether hot or dry complexes: that is to say, a hot complex with matter, and a dry complex without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In both hot and dry complexes, matter is present, some say that cautery is great help, while others say the opposite: that cautery is useless for ailments arising from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For nature of fire is hot, and should not be treated with heat for hot ailments, neither by heat nor dryness; and he who says the contrary states that cautery provides great help to hot and dry ailments that come upon the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of a man and its moisture with the hot complexion of fire, you perceive the body is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in any case, no one should attempt this except he who has tried it himself, and knows through long experience the chapter of cautery, the diversity of human complexes, the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the remedies according to time; for the rest of complexes, we have only fear, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all agreed and consented to the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that cautery brings together fire in a way that is the essence of healing, and indeed far greater kindness than the burning cautery of medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and brings no force but to the member that is hot, and does not harm any other member.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The burning medicines travel from one member to another by going away, and they bring to the member diseases of sorrow that have no cure; and sometimes the fire causes the patient pain because of its warmth and the goodness of its substance, if there is too much of it.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And if you have found me through experience and the length of service and study that I have put into this art, and it is about the truth of things; and for this reason I excuse the length of my words, because I do not like to take away from you the secret that lies within fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives diseases from the body, as the philosopher demonstrates; then consider it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on the times when cauterizations should be done and carefully chose the instruments.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is appropriate in all times, because the pain-relieving effect of cauterization removes the damaging influence; and especially when cauterization is for necessary and urgent pains that cannot wait until a greater ill comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear child, as they do who are ignorant; for to the illness that is healed by cautery there is no relapse; and it should be so; but it is not like what they care for, because cautery is only a medicine that alters the complexion, dries up the humors that cause pain, and moves more quickly than other medicines because of the virtue of its work and authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And another thing that is possible: the illness comes according to the complexion and the nature of the malady and its virtue; and excesses accumulate in it with the acquisition of foods and similar things, except when cautery is administered to reduce excesses and moisture, as in the cauterization for pain and similar conditions, where this pain does not return; but it happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand at all why cautery is called the last resort of medicine; it is true; but they do not believe that cautery has any value after medicine, because when we administer methods of cure for any illness and they are ineffective, then we use cautery, and it is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it becomes clear that cautery is indeed the last resort of medicine, not at all according to the opinion of learned people.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that gold cautery instruments are better than iron ones, and they only spoke of fire for its quality of gold and the high value of its substance; they said that the heat of cautery does not cause putrefaction, but it is not true, as I have experienced it, and I have found that it has no effect on any man; gold cautery is more effective than iron.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet when you heat an instrument of gold, you are not certain if it is heated through by the color of the gold, and as soon as it cools; and if it is overheated, it will burn; thus there is ample obstruction.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason, we use fire cautery because we have made it suitable for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or, I have ordered this chapter in a logical sequence, so that the way may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	Cyst cautery is applied to moisture and cold on the brain, and it is effective for various conditions caused by illness, known as "soda," and by numerous humors that descend from the head to the ears, and due to excessive dreaming, toothache, throat pain, and especially for diseases arising from cold such as paralysis, soddenness, apoplexy, and similar ailments.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient be purged with a solvent medicine, purifying the third or fourth (part of the brain), according to the virtue and age and habituation of the patient; and then the head should be allowed to dry out again.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him sit with his back between your hands, and place his hands on some weight; afterwards, put the root of your palm on the root of his neck between his two fingers; and there where your two middle fingers meet, if he bleeds, immediately heat up the cautery called 'olive', which has this shape:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	Mark the location with an ink sign, and repeatedly descend and stretch your hand while twisting; then gently release your hand, and assess the bone; if you do not see it, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you. Afterwards, take a small amount of string, place soft, melted cotton inside, and apply it to the location; leave it for three days. Then put clean, moistened cotton on top, and continue until the burning is gone; finally, treat the wound with 'tetrafarmacon' ointment while ensuring it remains clean.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients say that the longer an injury remains open, the more it purifies itself; for this reason, it is helped to heal.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say that one should not leave the cautery for so long that part of the bone is burned, and then remove what is burned from the bone, and it will be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And another says that one should leave the cautery for so long, and pull so hard that part of the bone is removed as wide as a woman opens her womb to let humor flow out; and the wound should remain open for a long time; after that, it should be cleaned and dressed.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cautery do not seem good to me in all cases, except for those who have no hope; and I think I should leave them; for the joint is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we testify in other members; and also when the patient's joint is weak by nature, and the initial appearance of cauterization seems safer and more mobile to me, and from this I act together for the good.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When chronic pain in the head comes and lasts for a long time, patients should use herbs and pills called "cough drops," and purgatives for the head and eyes, and bandages; and if one performs the cauterization that we have mentioned above, it is of no avail.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's condition is of a strong nature and not too severe; then cauterize deeply, as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After cauterizing each horn of the skull just below the bone, as we have previously said, and cauterize the one called "vasselz" (vessel), which is where suction cups are placed; hold your hand slightly away so that you do not see the bone. The patient experiences much greater pain from this cautery than from others, which I will discuss later. It is necessary for the cautery of the horns to be more precise than that of the middle part of the skull, and this is its shape.
dou cautere dou chief	For fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When there is a sudden intense pain in a part of the head, and the disease extends as far as the oil (or possibly referring to inflammation/fever), and the symptoms are purged with medicated remedies, and all other treatments mentioned in the division of illnesses have not helped, then perform cauterization according to two methods, that is, using heat or fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauterization with heat (or fire) involves pricking a sweet-smelling herb and applying it to the skin where the pain is located, in such a way that you can push the sweet-smelling herb beneath the skin; then tightly wrap and leave it for 12 hours. After this, unwrap it and treat the area fiercely with honey, leaving the wound like this for 2 or 3 days, then apply cotton soaked in butter until the pus is gone.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment with medication as long as it is healed; and if you see that something similar to any of the burning medicines I have written about or the dosage for treating them has been done.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery is done according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery instrument with this form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "closed" because the head is shaped like a cap with a small opening, and in the middle there is a little appearance; then place it on the painful part, hold your hand, and turn it slightly so that half of the thickness of the heart is burned; remove your hand when the artery stops burning, which is when it ceases to pulse, and abundant blood flows.

After placing cotton in awe of the wound, and covering it with cloth for three days; then he immerses the cotton in butter, and then dresses the wound with medicine until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called 'cultellare', be sure not to cut the artery in this migraine which is not old.
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre. de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of fistulas by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have discussed in the sections on diseases, and your treatments are not helping, then it is necessary that you perform cauterization according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place his head on a healthy surface, and hold the affected limb between your hands in such a way that it does not move or shift its position. Afterwards, apply moist cotton or persil juice over the wound. Then, heat the cauterizing iron until it is hot. Position the iron over the injury, shaping it like a quill, or like a tent. However, whatever shape you find most suitable for your work, that is how it should be.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula, open it, and drain the pus and dry it; if it is closed, repeat the operation, and use hot cautery; hold your hand over the cautery at the affected area above the oil, so that your hand does not cause harm; place the cautery on the fat of the oil, and corrupt (it).
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you start the cautery near the bone, that would be better.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If no, repeat the cautery again, and if necessary, do it a third time, leaving it for three days; then apply moistened butter cotton to cure the drying dressing as long as it is healthy; and if forty days pass and it is not healed, apply corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and the remedy should be according to what comes in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cautery for a fistula, which no one from the past mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understand the fistula, and fix its position; then place a fine, sharp instrument into the gap, which thus forms the shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and they make it in the quantity of a drop of rain; and hold your hand firmly, so that the patient does not move at all, until the liquid flows out on its own; and one should put clean cotton over the wound, either with a poultice or in any other way: the liquid will gently leave the fistula and heal it miraculously.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the ulcer is healed by the cauterization we have described, that is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If that does not happen, it is necessary to administer warmth or cold, and bring the ulcer back to the body according to what is appropriate for its own place.
des crevaices en levres	cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times, cracks appear in the lips that are called "pox," especially on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	As you treat these wounds of which we spoke in detail, and the treatment is not effective, then heat a small surgical blade according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	and insert it into the wounds until it reaches the bottom; after that, treat the area with wax until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess forms in the throat's root or in the uvula, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, it causes putrefaction and swelling and becomes a fistula; then you treat it as we described in detail, but it is not effective. In this case, you should perform cauterization according to the size of the fistula; after that, remove or close the fistula opening, and keep your hand on it until the heat from the cautery reaches the bottom, and do this once or twice, following the treatment we described for wounds, until it is healed; if treated in this way, it will heal well. If not, you must expose the area and remove the rotten bone, as you will find described in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	no movement of the joints
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and treatment with medicine is ineffective, then place the patient's aching tooth in a healthy place; afterward, apply the hot cautery to the area where the shape will come as if you were placing a candle on the tooth; and insert the hot cautery firmly, holding your hand until the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; then release your hand and repeat the cauterization according to your desire; afterward, have the patient fill his mouth with salty water and leave it for an hour and a half burning.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way, the tooth that was moving becomes firmly set, and the soft gums are restrained, and the moisture is dried up.
de la dolor des dens	about the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain comes from cold, either from being cold or swollen, and medical remedies are ineffective, then it is necessary to use cauterization according to two methods: butter cauterization and fire cauterization.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Butter cauterization is done by pressing warm butter onto the affected tooth, using the tip of a metal spoon or arrow, and wrapping cotton around it. Moisten it with melted butter, place it on the aching tooth, and hold until it cools; repeat this several times until its effectiveness reaches the root of the tooth. If you don't have moistened wool and cotton in butter, apply the warm butter directly to the aching tooth and hold a hot iron to it until the heat reaches the gum around the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	He uses fire cautery if it is such that you can insert a piece of iron or steel, and it is thick enough that the heat does not reach the patient's mouth; after heating the cautery, from which the shape will come, place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools; do this often, for the pain will be lessened that day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter in the haste of that cautery, and then quickly remove it; and this is the shape of the cautery.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make cautery on the upper lip where you wish, and according to what you are able to do; and this is the shape of the instrument.
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrofula is of cold moisture, and is not obedient to digestion with medicines, then heat the cautery knife with this after which comes the shape, and it has openings for the fumes to escape from the cautery in another part; and place the hot cautery on the abscess once, as it is necessary, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, apply cautery according to its quantity, and leave it thus for three days; and then cover it with moist cotton and butter until the burning is removed; after that treat the wound and bandage it until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the bone:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture defeats the channels of the body, and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be drained first by solvent medicines; afterwards, apply cautery to the root of the throat, and beware not to go up to the throat, and only use a little heat.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, apply another cautery to the joint of the collarbone near the top of the spine, and these cauteries that are called 'claves' which we have described above; and treat the limb as we have said before until it is healed.

de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	Of the dislocation of the shoulder joint.

dou cautere de pleuresin	the cautery of tears

de la menoison	of the joint
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When abdominal pain arises from cold and moisture, the retentive and digestive virtues in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by normal means; you see the patient suffering greatly with strong vital force, so perform a great cautery on the stomach as he has spoken of before, to the circulatory cautery; and three cauterizations around the anus using subtle cautery claws, and two cauterizations on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	If you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, perform a cautery on the wrist, and one cautery on each part, and two small cauterizations on the stomach to alleviate the great pain, for the cure is profitable when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	On the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are of long standing and consist of corrupt, cold, moist humors, they are treated as we have said in the previous sections, but they do not benefit from cauterization.  Make three incisions along the spine of the back, starting from below and moving up in a triangular pattern; make one incision above the anus (two incisions deep); if you think the stomach is chilled, the meat does not cook, and bloating is observed on the face, then apply a strong cauterization on the stomach as mentioned before, and another on the liver, and yet another on the heart (the whole body with cautery). Leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treatment, reset the joint as long as it is healthy.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	from the fleshiness called "thelul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you deal with the fleshiness (thelul), if the cautery appears too sharp, then cover it entirely with hot embers over the entire flesh; and leave it until the cautery reaches the vein, thereby sealing it; do this once or twice, and if there is much flesh, cauterize each part as we have said; afterwards, treat the wounds profitably as long as they are healthy; and if you cauterize with a great cautery on raw (fleshy) skin, it will be of greater help.
de plaie mal curee	From the poorly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, as we shall relate, a certain illness comes about that can only be healed by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a vein forms a fistula, and becomes inflamed with putrefaction and corrupt moisture, you must try all subtle remedies, and be sure to know at every step how effective they are.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heating the cautery instrument to a sharp degree, insert it into the fistula according to the amount that the attempt has entered, and repeat the cautery once, or twice, or three times, depending on the quantity required; be careful not to burn the sensitive nerves and large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	He will puncture the bladder and intestines if you are not careful with these joints, and do not make too deep a cut in fleshy parts, and think that it is not dangerous; then treat the joint until it is healthy, and if the joints are intact and the matter has been removed for a long time, then know that the joint is completely healthy; but if the matter remains, know that the joint is weak and the bone is corrupt at its base, just as we will say of these joints.
de la maladie des reins	regarding the illness of the kidneys

When kidney pain and severe constipation comes, and it prevents a woman from doing her duty, then you must perform cautery on the kidneys from both sides using the cautery clamp that we have mentioned before; and if we apply the cautery in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a row, and it will bring greater relief.
de la vessie	from the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from pressure and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then it should be cauterized in the upper part of the bladder where the hairs begin to grow, both on the right and left sides, and each cautery should be as long as a finger; and also cauterize behind the back if necessary; and make the cauteries in the shape as mentioned above.
de la marris	of the marriage

de la hainche	de la hainche" translates directly from Old French to English
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous moisture descends into the chest of the hinch (a term for a lung or breathing difficulty), and because of this it remains in its place, and the symptoms are that one leg is longer than the other when measured together; and there is found a weak pulse in the affected area, it is necessary to cauterize the patient above the chest of the hinch with a circular cautery, marking in front of the joint around the chest so that it stays within the circle, and if necessary, the cautery should be done as one does for the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present for you, perform three cauterizations from the large olive, and let these cauterizations be just as effective as all the others; and treat until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	for the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain arises in the back, caused by cold and moisture, and the patient's condition does not improve with the treatments we mentioned in the previous section, then it is necessary to cleanse the patient of the bad humors using foul-smelling pills or other similar good pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After making the incision, there are two ways to cauterize: with burning medications and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery has many methods, of which I will describe two: first, cauterizing the breast in a triangular shape, making sure it is deeply and widely done, with each cauterization spaced apart by about the thickness of a finger, and they are olive-shaped. Never should cauterization be performed in the middle of the chest, as this creates three (or) four shapes according to this method.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	If you see that the cautery is in a circular shape as we have previously described in the dislocation of the chest, make it in such a way that the circle encloses the entire chest, and all the spaces around the heart are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the method used for sciatica, when the pain is in the hip and does not reach down to the thigh or leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if the pain reaches down to the thigh and leg, perform a cautery on that part where the patient feels the pain, starting from just above the ankle, on the left side a little; it can be a cut cautery or a burning of the thick tissue; and if the patient feels that the pain extends up towards the knee or near it, cauterize there where he feels the pain, three times or four times with a cautery known as 'point'.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if the pain is so intense in the knee towards the thigh, make a cut with a sharp or circular instrument, and be very careful in all your cauterizations that you do not leave them for too long, lest you burn the nerves and large arteries, and cause the patient greater harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who have made cauterizations on the ankle of the foot, and left them until the leg was completely swollen, and the foot as well, and it became pierced and corrupted throughout the foot.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After an abdominal solution, he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, apply cautery to one and the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise ones say about the cautery of the spine, which is how it should be done: take a piece of iron, as thick as a new date palm or slightly thinner, and make it twisted and interwoven from one side to the other, at a distance equal to that of a thumb's nail; twist it over both sides, making it straight like a bow, and have a skilled blacksmith forge it. This is its form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And heat it until it is entirely red and exudes bubbles, then place it on the affected spine of the patient, and turn to the healthy side; apply cautery once more and leave it for three days. Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use this cautery little because of the danger of its regard, and we should see few who use it; nevertheless, these are good cauteries, which one can endure, and where it is firm.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The burning cautery of medicine is made by creating a tool with a thin, descending edge, either of iron or steel, attached to a long handle. Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After placing the board of the couch over the patient lying on their side, and quickly covering your hand with the board, pour between the two circles of hot ash, which is heated over the fire, and leave it for an hour while the patient endures the heat and burn from it.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it causes a severe burning just like fire; and when the burns have passed, lift your hand with the instrument and raise the affected area gently, leaving it for three days, and apply butter until the blackness from the burn is gone; and leave it for another three days as pus drains out; and this would be the final aid after treating the wounds until it is healed.

And if the pain extends to the thigh or leg, use the instrument to draw the awl according to what you did with the hip, increasing the pressure; and this is the method of hot awl, which I have written about in the treatment of rectifications of medicine.

ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	If there is a small opening, make it larger with a point of a needle so that the alkali and lime can enter; then place this pot into another well-sealed pot, and add more alkali and lime on top, stirring gently until there are two layers of powder at the surface as you hold it in your hand. Leave it thus until the liquid inside becomes clear and evaporated. Then take all that remaining liquid, pour it over the lime and alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And therefore it will be very useful and beneficial in many medical operations and other cautery treatments, for it acts like fire, and it is used in other medicines such as fomentation and myrrh and anacardium and chalk with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a case where a nobleman was cured of the pain in his hip and sciatica, and he says that no other treatment was done, and he was completely healed once this cure was performed, and he bathed as he is instructed below.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And prepare it in such a way that you press the litargire (alum) with fresh and dry herbs, grind them finely with a bit of fat, apply it to the hip, thigh, and leg where the pain is, and wrap it; leave it for three hours or according to the amount, until the patient no longer feels the burning.

Then make them take a bath or a warm drink until their body is slightly warmed, and have them lie down in bed, and the pain will disappear entirely and they will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use such cautery with these medicines unless it is after evacuating the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dyscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's hair fire, it provides great aid; and the cautery should be done in this manner.

Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After that, take dry goat hair, ignite it until it becomes charcoal, and place it on the wool, leaving it until it is stained; and repeat this process again and again, without stopping, until you believe that it has reached the hinch (a possible reference to a specific body part, perhaps the hip or lower back) and the pain has ceased; and this method of cauterization is called "goat hair cautery.
de la dolor dou dos	From the great pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from strain or impact, or due to excessive blood evacuation, or from what appears to be a cold, expanded substance, none of these signs should be treated with cautery, except for that which arises from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary that after the patient has been voided of foul pills or other similar substances, one should apply to their back, where the pain resides, three lines marked with a sign of a cross, and on each line perform five cauterizations or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can endure; and the cauterization should be done using a instrument called 'a point'; and if you see fit, make three or four cauterizations at the medium cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees. de la dolor des jointes	joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of joints is caused by moisture that has spread to each limb deeply, and when the pain comes on suddenly, they call it "gout" properly speaking, and when it is due to a cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, then cautery is the remedy in this manner: make several cauterizations around the joint of the foot, and let the cauterization be olive-colored according to this form.
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary to pierce the face with a pin, make the cautery completely around with a claim of "no point.

And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, this often happens, make cautery on each knee with three or four cauterizations from every part, completely olive-colored; and if you need more, do so, but don't hold your hand too tightly until the heat of the heart is gone.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and back, administer the cautery as we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make points inside the bones with two lines; and if there is no pain in the middle finger, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to the fingers or shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good care to the patient and apply medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give good care to him and purge the flu, he will be healed by God's grace.
de la routure dou syfac	of the fracture of the thigh bone
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a rupture occurs in the bowels, and the intestines descend into the coils, it is important that, when you see the cure take place, they do not move at all during the day; and he should use things that leave the belly empty, so that the intestines return to their proper place. After this, have him lie on his back between your hands, and command him to keep his breath until the bowels are healed, and arrange them in your hands, and mark the rupture on the bone of the wrist, and at every sign, it should look like half a circle above the body; then take the fire cautery whose shape is described here:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as it is white and exudes scent.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the bones to their proper places; and have the minister place his hand so that they do not return backwards; and carefully open the legs of the patient, and place a cushion and a support under the legs, and another on the anus which holds his hands; then apply the cautery to the sign over your entire hand, holding it straight and firmly until you reach the bone, and if you do not touch it the first time, repeat it again until you reach the bone; and be careful that the bone does not jump when applying the cautery; that you do not burn it; and that the patient does not die or suffer any other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that if you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your efforts are in vain.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And the cauterizer of children should be subtle according to their size, and of tall people as great according to their measure; after three days, treat the wound with butter until the burn is healed; after that, treat other injuries until they are healed, and have the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is well sealed; and it is necessary that his movements be limited for a long time, so that the boils do not appear when he goes to bed.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wants to stand up, apply a well-made compress and leave it for another forty days; and have good rest, that he works little and guards himself from too much drinking and eating, and from loud laughter; and when he follows this instruction, he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will now describe the treatment for cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the abdomen
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other parts of the abdomen and are recognized, and you see that they do not grow larger, it is treated with cautery according to its quantity, and sometimes it is burned with hot iron; after this treatment, follow the method as we have said; and no one among the ancients has said that it should be cauterized at three angles in this way.
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the place with a sign of lightning and make a line across the width above the rupture; then another one from the opposite side, and hold your hand steady over the entire cautery area.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterization is lighter and easier.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain arises in any member, whether from strain or injury, and this pain persists for a long time, and the cure of medicine is ineffective, then it should be cauterized with the cautery called "point," and the cauterization should be according to the length of the member and its smallness and weakness, and its virtue and location of twists and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If the first cauterization is successful, that's good; if not, recommence with another cautery on the same member, for it is customary for it to move towards the nearest member, so you should perform cauterizations until the patient is free of pain.
de meselerie	From illness
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The medicines are aided by cautery no less than by great help, especially the illness that arises from the putrefaction of fluids and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	You must learn to cauterize, take care if the illness is in its beginning, and cure it according to what we have said in the previous division, so that it does not linger or remain, and doubt lest the corruption spread throughout the patient. Then perform cautery on the head: first, make a new wound on the crown of the head, and another towards the front at the end of the hair; then on both temples, and behind on the nape; and leave your hand so that the cauterization goes down to the bone, and the skin parts outward so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape. Cauterize the mouse according to what is indicated above.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the disease is widespread throughout; and it appears manifestly, then you must cauterize with these cauteries that we have mentioned in the beginning, cauterizing in some places, and cauterizing on the spine of the neck, and cauterizing on the spine of the back, and greatly on the crupie and another delicate place, and two on each shoulder; and two on the elbows, and two on the tender parts of the pis, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the fossae of the hands; and beware of the nails that are on the last toe, that you do not burn them; and never make a cautery on the bone of the wrist, or on the bone of the stomach, or on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more you perform cautery, the greater the aid and benefit it brings, and move it for the better; and know that the patient feels no pain from cautery as the healthy do, because the body is already corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cautery be great and small according to the members and joints, as you will find in the manner of iron.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treatment, cover the wound with flour of times (a type of plant) mixed with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling appears in any member and is cured by medicines, oils, and bandages, but it remains unhealthy, then make cautery on the member according to its size and shape; and let the cautery be slightly inside the hope of the heart; then cure with poultices until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.
