And never should cautery be performed on the hand, foot, or back, at the point of the nerve that causes the limb to move, and thus if swelling is removed; nevertheless, no one should intervene unless they are knowledgeable about the members and the passages of the moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	of albara (or perhaps "from blisters")
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is afflicted, and the medical art has no effect, then cauterize with a hot iron slightly, according to the depth of the wound, until the white is removed, and the color changes; then apply a cure of meal, lentils, rose oil, plantain leaves, collicon (a herbal remedy) and alder bark, each in a portion; mix all together, wrap it in a cloth, and keep it at the fire until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the treatment of ulcers with cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a wound appears at the beginning, and you wish to stop it, cauterize it with the cautery that seems like a circle around the entire wound.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	However, wise people say that cautery should also be done in the middle of the wound; yet, I don't find this good, as I fear it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have never seen it work effectively before. A more proper thing is to cauterize around it, with a cautery called a "circle," as we have said in many cautery practices.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	from the swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	If anyone has a disease called "adubelati," and it is slow to die, either because of the excess it produces or because of the old age of the patient when he is debilitated (that is, too much) and has little blood, or because of the time; then you see that it hastens to die: at this point, cauterize it with many small cauterizations by poking; then leave it alone.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	Because it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierce through all the cauterization, make the cautery so hot that...
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of this illness called 'adubelati' until the cauterization has reached the heart, and it is done like the cauterization that the patient feels relieved in this way that the course of decay is stopped.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	Heal the fire with iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of illness is called 'corrodens', which is nothing other than a wasting away of the members, as it attacks the limbs just as fire does the dry branches.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a limb that can endure fire cautery, then heat the cautery instruments slightly and thoroughly, according to what is suitable for the limb or the disease; afterward, cauterize all parts until you have eradicated all the corruption, leaving nothing from it, so that everything that is corrupted be removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	Then leave it for three days, and apply oil to the cauterized limb, grinding it, until all the burns from the fire are healed, and all the corruption is gone.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of wounds that generate heat.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if after three days a healthy character does not appear, it is good; and if not, the cautery should be repeated on that which remains delayed from the corrupted joint.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this mixture is sometimes cured with a hot medicinal drink instead of fire cautery; but nevertheless, the fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already mentioned the cure with a cold medicinal drink in the previous section: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	from the vessels that come as pieces
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that a pain arises from a defect which we call "close" according to our intention, and it is a great wrong that hurts the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery for this illness is according to two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cautery, and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is when you heat the cautery tool to a fine point with a forge, making sure it has sharp edges; then apply it to the nail, turning your hand around the nail until it reaches the bottom; leave it like that for three days so that it starts to rot; then make an ointment from crushed wild mallows, and apply it over the cautery mark, leaving it on all night. The nail will fall off and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the shoulder with a healing ointment, making it as clean as possible.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are affected by fire and the skin is burned, often both hands or feet, it is necessary to apply hot water cautery; and it is done thus: take a rod of iron or steel, or a needle from a bowstring, and attach the nail and the glue, that is, the putty, to the burn; then place the rod on it so that it covers everything around it, and pour some hot water over it, and hold your hand firmly, and twist it so that the edge of the rod reaches the root of the nail, and find the hot water deeply into the root; allow the patient to bear the sting of the hot water for an hour; then leave it as it is, and it will come out at the roots entirely.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	First, do one after another, until you have loosened all those that are in the body, then treat the ulcers that cause pain.
li cure dou trembler	It cures the trembling.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When anyone trembles from cold or quartan fever or any other, it is necessary to make four cauterizations or five on the spine of the back, one cauterization between each spine; and one cauterization on the fish, and one on the stomach with an olive cauterization; if this stops the trembling and hastens the healing from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	from pus-filled blisters
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Never is it apparent through external defects or pus-filled blisters that come from highly corrupt matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	it is necessary to act at first when they appear, performing cauterization on each head of the pustule: a delicate cautery with a stick of myrtle, from which the point is taken to the fire, or with a long root of aristologist, or with a lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And never should cauterization be performed at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, nor can it grow worse in progress, but it breaks off the superfluities from which it comes, and becomes healthy; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut off
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many serious consequences often arise from the blood of an artery that is cut during a wound, or in the case of a vein opening, or incision of an abscess, or cautery on a limb, and similar situations; and it is a very sad thing to experience.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet, if this happens to anyone, hurry and place your index finger on the wound of the vein, pulling it firmly until the pain subsides from your finger, and no more blood flows; then take several small and larger olive oil cauteries, as hot as they can be, and apply them, depending on the size of the wound and where the artery is located, placing the cautery on the vein where you hold your finger, and holding it there until the pain subsides.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if a sudden jump occurs when you remove your hand from the vein, and the cauterization is complete, then quickly take another cautery tool from those that are on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And continue to perform this one after the other until the wound is completely healed; be careful not to damage the nerve that lies nearby, and ensure no further harm comes to the patient; and know that when the flow from the artery cuts off, it cannot be properly healed, especially if the artery is large, except through one of the four methods we have mentioned: either by cauterization, or extraction when it has not been treated, or tightly tying it with strong thread, or applying medicines that have the power to stop the flow of blood; and it should be bound and tightly wrapped.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever administers relief from pain by binding tightly with cloth or placing hot things, or other similar things, will not succeed unless it is done properly.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and they have no good medicine at hand, then they should put their two fingers on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press hard until all pain from the wound and the vein has subsided; and they must not move it, but apply moist cold often, as much as is very cold, until the limb is frozen and engorged and free of pain. And prepare in advance everything that is needed for cautery and medicine.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	We begin the second book of surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about every illness where it is necessary to cauterize with fire or burning medicines, and about the herbs, causes, instruments, and forms of cautery; I have placed that chapter primarily before this one, so that whoever wishes to find these things more easily can follow this same path.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, before we begin, it is important for you to know that this chapter involves more danger and fear than the first one on cautery; therefore, greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	Because many ways of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come from such who have become so affected by their illness that they die quickly because of the severity of their condition and the magnitude of their suffering; of these one must be afraid.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And there are those who, in their weakness, say: "Wait, I am bleeding," and the illness is malicious.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	You should not consent to those who come to you with such methods, but place more emphasis on your honor than on their greed, and act prudently, not foolishly, regarding what you are certain of, and what you can safely acquire; and use prognosis and treatment in the care of your patients, so that health may be restored; and this will help you gain good repute, glory, and lasting fame.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Most precious child, Our Lords grant you good understanding and integrity, and if you desire the holy inspiration from His hand, so be it.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I have ordered this chapter for you, devising it according to chapters about cautery, as it is before or the chapter on dislocations, which I have devised from the head down to the foot, so that you may find it easier to understand what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	chief filled with water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	You know that this illness often comes to children at birth, when the child's head is too tightly bound, and it never happens for a reason that one cannot fathom.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease except in children, and to all those that I have seen, death comes quickly; and for this reason, it seems to me that it is better to leave the work in part for some cures.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose joints were filled with water, and the head swelled each day so that it could not be supported; and due to the moisture, it became infected, and this moisture gathered beneath the bone next to the lymphatic vessel, between the heart and the bone; and the work is such that the moisture is located between the heart and the bone, and the abscesses are small, so you must make a wide cut across the head where the moisture is present, as deep as possible, until the moisture flows out; and see the shape of the spatula.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper, and the abscess larger, then make two cuts in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and you see the openings of the commissures of each side wide open, and there is a sharp, strong discharge when you press with your hand from within, and it does not return to normal, then you must make three cuts in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all the moisture completely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After loosening the cracks of the bandages and powders, he applies wine and oil and leaves it for up to five days; then he unwinds it, treating the wound with bandages and poultices, and stretches the head equally, and gives the patient dry meat from a pouch of moisture until the limb is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you observe or measure the size of the abscess and the arrangement of the fluid; for it never appears in front, nor behind, nor on the right, nor on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Measure then the abscess and the quantity of fluid, and make the cut according to your ability; be careful not to block the artery; then comes a flow of blood, so that the patient dies due to the slow progression of blood and moisture evacuation.
de reume	Of the root
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When someone has a disease called "cataract" either in one eye or both, and the disease is old, and medical treatments are not helping, then the final remedy is cauterization by sealing the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you see the patient turn their head, rub the affected area with a rough cloth until the arteries open, then gently pull the skin away from the eye using all the cloth; observe where the vein is located, and its branches behind the ears, which should be visible; mark these spots with a sign, then cauterize both with a sharp spatula, going deep into the tissue up to the bone, making sure it's wide across the forehead.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, turn the spatula away from the artery and cut the coagulum on top, also cutting as it should go through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, it bleeds continuously from above unless stopped.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open when pressed, it is necessary to measure the quantity of space in three parts, then tie it with string and make it extend to the bone; and this should be done with blood, about six parts, or perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the state of the artery; then examine the wound: if there is no discharge from the sinus that forms at the point where it was cut, and if the coagulum does not prevent healing, then press and bind the wound, and apply treatment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old migraine comes with a severe catarrh due to moisture in the eyes and sockets and other similar symptoms, and all medical treatments fail to help, then we drain the arteries of the eyes and apply heat, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method for extracting them is that the patient pulls out the hairs from his temples and listens to the artery opening in the temple, as it opens clearly due to its beating, and it is tightly closed, except in no one who is too frail; and if it is closed, he tightens a piece of cloth around it from some thin fabric, then rubs the area with hot water until the artery appears manifestly open. Then take the instrument (spatumile) shaped as follows:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	then scrape the skin lightly as you approach the artery, then grasp it with pincers and free it from the webs that bind each part; and if the artery is delicate, twist it to the tip of the hook, then cut off that part according to the number of joints.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, it will not heal without great pain throughout.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And incise the blood with a sharp tool from the sixth to the third; and if the artery is large, tie it in two places with a strong double thread of silk, so that putrefaction does not come before the wound heals and complications arise; then cut off the excess between the two threads at that very moment, and, if you see fit, cauterize the patient with a cutting instrument until the joints are cut through; and this is the moving part, if the patient does not have fever and has a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cauterization is a help to end moisture: therefore it is of greater aid against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or for the extraction of arteries, it is necessary that one fills the wound with fine cotton and covers it with well-made bandages; and when they are loosened, take care to apply dried medicines that produce heat, and new bandages, as long as the wound is healed; and if you see any sign of an artery, be quick to cover it with cauterization, or use vitriol and press with your hand so that the wound becomes clean; and if you do not have this at hand, put snow on the wound until it freezes, and keep applying cold water until the bleeding stops, and pull gently as necessary. The warmer and lighter the artery is when extracting, the better it is to cauterize the vein with this cautery, cutting from both sides, but the cuts should be well-spaced to maintain heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too tight, they hold the heat less.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it must have between the two blades a good space, and then when you have marked with a sign the two joints, and put the hot iron until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two joints; and they should be separated between the two parts because this cautery is not fully sealed everywhere; and this is the form of the cautery.
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes descend into the veins that are under the skin of the head, and no medicine can help, you see the face of the patient contort, and feel their forehead twitching as if with tremors; and the eye is inflamed and moist, so much so that the eyelashes fall out, and the eyelids are scorched by the heat of the tears, then this cure is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it the "old cure" (li cure contuse); so for the patient with this condition, you should shave the hairs on their forehead, then make three cuts (fendures) on the forehead evenly according to its length; one of these cuts should go all the way across the front from ear to ear, and the others should be two on each side of the bones above the eyes, avoiding the incision of the arteries that are next to the bones; also, keep your hand away from the joint of the lower jaw. Each wound should be about three fingers wide. Have a piece of sponge and clean cloth to wipe the blood, then mold the spatula with one part as follows:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is made on the temple down to the second incision; scrape all the flesh that is between the two cuts to the full satisfaction that is on the bone, then make another from the middle incision down to the other second, and then extract this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you insert the instrument called 'cultellaire' into the first cut, it should be very sharp on one side and slightly soft on the other; this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the sharp side towards the far edge of the cut, and the soft side towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the joints as long as the incision is continuous until it opens the heart, and then make another cut in the middle until the other side is open; and then extract the blood equally, and press out the blood with a cloth, and put in each wound a piece of old cotton, and place on top moistened cloths in wine and oil and ash, and be careful that no abscesses form; and on the third day, loosen the bandage, and administer a strong infusion of water, then apply basilicon treatment with rose oil, and other treatments to cure wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	the joints
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When any catarrh comes that is usually accompanied by thick and small veins, weakening sight, burning papers, hair falling out, and intense pain in the head, the patient sneezes; then know through these symptoms that this matter and catarrh do not come from a single cause but are rather the result of many veins, and the movement cure that is necessary.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And instruct the patient to bend their forehead backwards, then make a deep cut across the forehead, and another one wide enough.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And starting from the cut in the left temple to the right temple, make the incision down to the bone; and keep your hand away from the muscles of the temples that move when you blink. When the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood away with a sponge, then separate the two edges of the cut and insert old cotton, and cover it with linen. Then place moistened cloth soaked in wine and oil on top and protect it from infection; once the bone heals, rub the bone gently until new skin begins to form, then apply a drying agent that promotes healing.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of rye flower and three parts of chalk, mix them to make a paste, and apply it to these wounds to promote healing throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	from ear infections
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Anything that causes pain in the ears is one of four things: grains or seeds, animals or creatures, hard rocks or similar objects, or fluids such as water or mucus; like seeds, beans, peas; or flowing things like water and mucous-like substances and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a piece in the ear or any other object that does not adjust itself to the ear, does not enter the ear, then place the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see a foreign object, and some violet oil or oil of sisament drips from it, then proceed with extraction; and as the condition permits, make the patient sneeze, and when sneezing occurs, stop their nostrils, and place pieces of cloth or wool inside the ear; and pull the ear gently upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often, this treatment works; and if it does not work, then extraction with fine tweezers should be performed, in the following manner:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If she jumps out of the pincers, that's good; if not, apply a subtle, thin extraction at the base; and if she doesn't jump out, make a hook of iron and twist the head of the hook or the perforation of the ear tightly, and stop what is around the hook with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter with the hook; then treat it firmly, as it often comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, take a lot of care to catch it, and use a sharp instrument suitable for this purpose, and put some cotton around; then press the pressure on the stone or something, and extract.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not jump out of all the things we have said, hurry to split the ear so that the abscess hardens and relaxes; and the way to split it is that you first make the patient from the cephalics, and extract blood according to its strength, then place the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the base of the ear where the fat or tissue depends; and let the cut be as thin as a moon, until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your ability, and suck it vigorously with your mouth; and cure it as long as it is healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is embedded and swollen, then perform extraction; and if it cannot be extracted, then apply a thin, delicate spatula according to this form.
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and perform an incision on that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not attempt this if you think the grain is moist from earwax, until you have made many attempts; then extract it with fine tweezers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is gentle.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case where something has entered the ear, it is advisable for the patient to use a light sneeze and cover the ear with thick cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let them lie on that same ear where the pain is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If she jumps out of fear, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If she does not jump, take many small, thin stones according to the length of your thumb and index finger, warm them slightly in the fire, and insert one into her ear, then from another side, insert a larger stone over the stone in her ear; continue this process with stones, one after another, until all the water has run out, and thus she will jump out entirely. And if you see that she is trapped, take a thin bone, and push one of the joints into her ear, while pulling the other end with fire until the thinner joint is burned; then make other joints in the same way until all the water is gone, as we have said before.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	During the removal of an animal, if it is a small core, like a pest or similar thing, treat it as we have said in the previous section; but if it is a large core that one can feel, then use pincers for its extraction; and it is the lighter thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When extracting worms from the ears, if you treat it as we have said in the previous section and you treat the distillations, but the cure is not effective, then you should examine the ear in sunlight. If there are no visible worms, use fine pincers to remove them, and if they are still not visible, take care to extract the worm from where it has taken shape.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it should be tight from below and wide from above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And then insert the most subtle tube into the ear according to the amount of suffering of the patient, then suck until all the water is drawn out; do this often until all the truth is revealed.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, then stop up the canal with cotton as I have said in the stone; and if they do not protrude as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have tried in the extraction of worms, and you will find them or treat them through distillations; and distil your oils and medicines into the ear using all these instruments, forming them as you see.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And take a thin piece of silver or gold and insert it into the small opening to distill; and over it place an instrument made of good iron to press down on the distillation; then take a razor and wrap it tightly around the tip with soft cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever you wish from your medicine in the kettle, and let the kettle be in the ear; then put the razor entirely into the cotton and press your hand firmly until the oil is distilled or barely enters the ear; and let the patient feel it within, and the distillation should be warm as if it were distilled in the ear; but beware that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	From ear inflammation
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born with any perforation in the ears; and the same thing occurs in adults due to a wound or a foreign object inside the ear, and this blockage never completely closes in the ear unless one can see it; and sometimes the perforation becomes permanently closed, and no one can see it.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	When the blockage completely closes, if one cannot see it, it is due to poor healing in various dispositions, and in this case, you must place the patient's ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see the wax visible, check if it has taken on this shape:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And make cuts and incisions all around and behind, so that the ear is not wounded; if the pain arises from the cartilage or the flesh of the ear, hold it with delicate pincers and gently cut, until that part is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the incision is completely in the ear, take a thin, sharp razor and heat it slightly over fire, then apply it to the cartilage of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the incision causing the patient great pain in the ear, make a slight perforation, and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then insert into the ear a plug according to the size of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Keep the bandage on for as long as the wound is fresh, or take a cloth and soak it in rose water, and sprinkle vitriol powder on it; and if you see the ear swelling, it is necessary to remove the bandage and apply another moistened cloth made of rosin oil and wax until the swelling subsides; then treat it while it is still clean.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, immerse a sponge and cloth in cold water, place it on the ear, and use other remedies to stop the flow of blood, which include treatments using distillation.
de la char des papieres	from the matter of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Gather all the papers that come from the eyes when they are moist and dry; it is necessary to stretch them with pliers and pincers, and cut off the top of a spatula at its roots; then place it on the vitriol paste.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if, after removing the skin, the lenticular cautery is performed with a delicate cautery, and the cauterizer moves after incision; often they heal, but nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized with fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the frost (or ice)
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come before us strange things that appear grainy in their form and hardness, and for this reason this illness is called "frost," and it's a gathering of great moisture on the paper from above and below; the work is as follows: be vigilant if the frost becomes silent on one side or the other, and this is a slight thing to know; then make them wide, scrape gently from each part, and pin them up and cut.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover it without piercing the paper slightly, it causes no harm to the patient; and if the gathering is great, with a stitch, treat it as long as it remains healthy; and if it's small, do not use much force, because the stitches will soon reopen and cause pain.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the pain is descending within the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper inside out, and the pain will tighten in pinches, pressing from one side and the other; and if the paper is removed by incision, it causes no harm; and when the pain is cut away, pour clean salt water and heal the place where it was causing trouble until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	from the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	The condition is a fat that forms in thin layers on the eyes, and it occurs more often in children than in adults, causing great discomfort to their eyes. It leads to frequent watering of the eyes, preventing them from bearing the light of the sun. Due to this, they rest their faces, sleep with their eyes closed, and their paper-thin eyelids become moist, showing signs of inflammation that have opened up in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the joint with your fingers and feel the pain between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the procedure is that the patient places his head in a healthy position; then he takes a linen cloth and prepares a tent-like structure according to the amount of blood from each part, placing it on top; and he presses with his fingers on both sides so that the blood collects within the circle; then, using a sharp spatula, he makes a groove not wider than the wound made in the vein, and completes the incision until he reaches the blood; and he continues to cut the skin in a perfect manner until he comes to the blood; and depending on the various arrangements, blood will come out from the groove in the form of a white fat piece.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Take then a whole piece of cloth soaked in fire between your fingers and move your hand to the right and left as long as it is glowing; and be careful not to insert anything into the wound, do not go all the way to the oil, do not touch it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the wound does not open at the beginning of the cut, gently widen the wound slightly until it opens; then take it out as we have said, and moisten the cloth with water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and hold it tight.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And for such men who grind and apply it to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat him as long as he is sane.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the hot abscess, treat it with cauterization as long as he is sane.
des poilz des papieres	hairs of papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow in papers (or abnormally), they become entangled, causing harm similar to the problems caused by ragged papers and albugine, as long as it is due to the destruction of the hair follicles; and the cure is according to four methods: either with cauterization using fire, or with medicine according to what is mentioned in the preceding chapter on cautery, or through incision and stitching, or with binding, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the patient's head in a healthy position, then turn the paper from the oil in your left hand; if it rotates, that is good; if not, insert an needle along all the thread above; and this should be done either along the edge of the paper or where the hairs grow along those hairs, and pull the thread above all the paper, turning it against the razor; then cut into the skin below the hairs, close to the root, from the large scar to the small one; then extract the thread, and place below the paper a small piece of cotton and cloth, and sign on the paper with an image of a cross, as if it were a fir tree, but the image should be according to the amount you raise the paper, which is marked at all points.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if you take a tool with which to cut great quantities of paper according as the paper is softened; then make incisions throughout all two lines that you have marked, and begin from a large tear as far as it extends; and let one of these cuts be near the natural hairs, in thickness equal to a root, then turn the oncin (scissor) into one of the two angles at heart, and scrape off everything; then bring together the two lips with a single stitch of fine thread, and wipe away the blood, and dry off any superfluity of thread on both edges with something non-adhesive if you can do so; and if not, leave the stitch and thread for three or four days; then cure the wound without stitching it up, using drying and constricting things, for the paper revives at the healing of the wound and its joining together, but the stitch moves (as they say in old times), and this is a work full of danger; and if another way: mark on the paper a figure like a fir tree, as we have told it, at three oncin distances according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut off what overcomes the small forces equally according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the pincers equally, and the matter is not equal, take a needle where there is thread, and tie it around the shape; then take another thread beneath the large lip, and the second thread beneath the small one, and tie them together equally between your fingers; then gently let go of your hand equally, and remove all the skin you have marked, as we have said, then sew together the two edges of the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healed; and if an abscess forms at your incision, soothe it with wax and similar remedies that relieve; and sometimes the paper-like tissue becomes converted. It is necessary to use what we have said about the incision; but sewing in one direction or another is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for the broken arm is as follows: and it is that you convert the paper and make it inside according to what I have said, then make two bands by art, also very thin long like the paper and the width with the spatumile; and fasten as much of each part where you hold the bones; then assemble them both delicately on top of the paper from the oil, and stretch the two bands from the formed parts; and leave it thus for several days, and the flesh that is squeezed will die and wither and rot until it comes out by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays and the patient has strength, then cure it as long as it is healthy; and when the wound is dried, and if lifting the paper does not hurt anymore, and the hair does not grow back; this is the shape of the two bands that you will make according to this figure and this quantity of length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work involves piercing the skin with a fine needle and threading it with soft, delicate silk thread; then joining the parts together very gently, making the length of the threads one palm's length. Next, arrange another thin thread of silk quickly and tie the ends delicately; place the patient's head on your healthy side, and let the sun dry the wound so that the work is revealed, as it is a delicate and small task. Then push the needle through all the skin at the root of the hair neatly, and make the paper pierce it gently until you remove it from above the natural hair; then pull out the hair up to the thread in the paper, and put back into the thread any hair that remains such as one, two, three, or more. Finally, withdraw your hand once all the hairs are pulled through the thread in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hair does not come out with the pulling, pull the hair root out completely along the entire thread that you have ordered; until the hair comes out from the opening and you see it through the eye of the needle; then you will pull the hair and the thread, and close the wound and leave it for two or three days, until the new hair grows in its place; and if the hairs are small, accompany them with a long natural horsehair, and raise it along with that, as long as it is elongated and then release it.
de la porriture de l’oil	regarding the impurity of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this illness called "aleacrati" or putrefaction comes in the body, it has two manners: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs suddenly from a wound, or cutting, or cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of working on it is that you open that wound, separate the lips of it, and put inside several pieces of linen, and bind them until they are healthy; and it does not suit that you use in the treatment of it things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness returns worse than before; but it uses softening agents, such as fenugreek; and rosewater of water or oil and flaxseed are cooked, and the diaquilon (a type of ointment) is melted in one of the eyes, and it envelops a cloth, and treats it accordingly.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the true power of your cure lies in ensuring it does not follow the same form as before; and these works that we have spoken are only correct measures for this illness so that it does not return in the same way again.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the grease that comes to the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness which is dislocation, truly called "axacti," is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Accidental dislocation arises from wounds, cuts, cauterization, and similar actions; the manner of its occurrence in this chapter is such that if you pierce a needle with a thread, it should go through both sides of the flesh, starting from the left eye socket towards the right, so that the thread comes out at two places on the shoulder; then the muscle is above the entire needle, and the scar tissue is wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the shape of the muscle returns to its proper position, it is good; if not, take a razor and insert it into the gap, turn the muscle, and make two cuts on either side inside the muscle; let the angles of these cuts match the angles of the incision you made, creating an angle so that when they are brought together, the shape resembles a letter with a curve (not 'griesche'); then remove the excess muscle, according to how much is above and below the skin, from where you turned the muscle; then adjust the two mismatched parts, stitching them with a thread of wool; finally, apply the curative treatments we mentioned for mollifying medicines and bandages until it is healed.

And if the disease comes from cutting or stitching or cauterizing, it is necessary to make a clean cut under the skin between the hairs, and according to what has been said before; then separate the two books of a joint, as I have mentioned; and one must perform the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and skilled doctors use various devices from all possible means to restore the natural shape; and the patients themselves, according to what they need for treatment and instruments in different arrangements.

de l’ungle de l’oil	from the nail of the finger

de la bowe de l’oil	of the vein (or artery)
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. des aigues de l’oil	the waters of oil

Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the patient lie between your crossed hands, away from the light for the sun, and bind him tightly with pure oil; then place the paper of oil in your left hand if his toes are on the left, or in your right hand if his toes are on the right; then take in your right hand, if his toes are on the left, the instrument called "almagda," or in your left hand, if his toes are on the right; then place the tip of the instrument into the crown through the thickness of a single strand at the bleached part of the oil to the smaller end of the tear, and turn the instrument called "almagda" skillfully, and twist your hand until it pierces the bleached part of the oil, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the almagda be exactly the same as the measure of the space from the plum to the end of the darkness; and this is the crown of the oil; you will see the bone on the paper due to the clarity of the horny cloth, and then place the instrument up to where the water is, and express it through one path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he lets it descend now, then he must see the patient before him and hold the instrument in his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After a brief rest, he should then attempt to raise it again along the second path, applying force with the instrument, and when it is fully inserted and does not rise, gently extract it by turning your hand back and forth; then reset it again using a string of the finest silk, and remove the instrument from inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply heat to the affected area using a hot poultice or any other moistened oil mixed with plenty of egg yolk, and bandage it with clean oil.
