Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, put a fine grind with much heat onto it.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if it cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, as there are many people with very hard eyes, it is necessary that you press the instrument called "alberit", which has this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then pierce only the conjunctiva gently, and do not cut too deeply, but make it subtle, then press the almond-shaped object as we have said; and after completing the work, prepare the patient for sleep with a warm place, on his back in a dark room; and be careful of all movements, and feed him light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and bind him according to his condition for three days. Then release him in the same dark room, test his vision, and make him see no objects, and then put the bandage on again for seven days; and it is not appropriate that you do this during the treatment or after the incision now, but you should gently ease him, because sharp pain rises suddenly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If an abscess appears, you should loosen the oil on the seventh day and apply the remedies for a soothed abscess; once it is soothed, loosen the bandage and place an edge on your face to cover it for some time, and thereafter remain in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then he should leave the house little by little and recover from his condition; and know that no disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And then one came to us from Iran who told us that in their peaceful land they use a device to suck out water, but I have never seen one in our land, nor do I read about it in the books of the ancients; perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of magics, for he who does not know them will see them as if they were made of gold.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the tip of this same tool be very sharp, and the rear in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	on the wound near the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	No wound ever appears with diverse adjustments, from which there is none that seems like a scorpion full of pain; and if there are such where the wound is enriched with bright color, or the flesh is soft and of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In this case where the wound is sore and not yet healed, you should place the patient between your hands facing the sun; open their nostrils, and pour ointment onto those parts, and treat them fiercely; cut what you can hold with the delicate blade on one side, as long as you know that part of the wound is completely healed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If there remains anything that cannot be covered, cut it with all the delicate and light instruments until nothing is left; and without delay, perform the incision as needed; and if it is a malignant abscess, hurry and cauterize it until the blood is completely drained and all parts are healed, then apply heat or cold and wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If he opens his mouth and moisture comes out until the wound is healed; knowing that it is healthy, and if the moisture does not come out as it should, knowing that there is a chip in the upper bone, preventing the instruments from cutting: then you must insert a thread of linen somewhat thick, using your hands, and allow each thread to have some space or little; and place the patient's toe in the thread at his power, pulling it by smelling until it comes out through the wound inside the mouth; and often children do this at school, and it is a light task for those who want to do it. Then hold the head coming through the wound with one hand, and the other head coming through the mouth with the other hand, knowing each after the other as we who are in thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do as you know, purify the infected wound, treat the child, dry up the blood, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment, then put it back to its place; do this for three days or more, until the ointments have corroded everything that remains of the infection. Then place a bandage around the neck for no more than a day while ensuring it is clean; if medicine is needed, use it; and this is the form of the instrument used to purge the head, with which one distills oils and medicines into the wound.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or gold, resembling an open lamp, like a candle, and lead it thus; and if you see fit, make a closed candle, and let the instruments be full to purge the head; and have many around the head to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	Of the pain near the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often, near the nose, a pain appears called "telul," which grows and becomes very large, so much so that it is a thing to behold; and for this reason, you must catch it at the beginning, and clean it thoroughly, then apply cautery or the burning medicine; and if you delay covering it until it becomes large, be wary if it turns hard, of poor color, and losing sensation: do not touch it with iron, because it is a deep abscess, and when you cover it for the first time, great harm comes to the patient. If the abscess is sensitive to gentle touch, there is no turning back, and the patient must be cured by completely emptying it without pain, using dry and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and seared
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Knowing that when a continuation of one of these important cartilage structures is broken, it benefits no one.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore important for no one to delay, if the wound is fresh and filled with blood; then close the two lips with a single stitch, and treat it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated on both sides, it is necessary to scrape all parts of their heart while they heal, then bring the two lips together with a stitch and tighten them, and apply dragon's blood powder and incense ground; and place a piece of plaster from strong or other adhesive plaster over it, leaving it until it falls off by itself, then treat it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is such that you bring the wound together: either with needles, as we have spoken of in abdominal stitching; or with thread, as I have informed you.
des apostemes des levres	abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home, the abscesses on the lips appear hard, resembling small grains, both smaller and larger; then you must turn the lips, cut each one open, and take out the pus with tweezers, applying it to each part; then use vitriole (a caustic substance) after making an incision, until the wound is clean; then apply oil from a light plant, and cure the lip by keeping it moist until it heals.
de la char des gencives	Of the work of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, a growth appears on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus"; it is necessary that you hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root, allowing the blood to flow or the pus to drain; then place upon it vitriol powder, or other restrictive and desiccant powders; and if the growth returns after the incision, this happens often, especially if the piece is cut a second time, and cauterize it: if it does not return after cauterization; these are the shapes of the tools for cutting.
des sordens	from disorders
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	No teeth are ever aligned at the head of the jaw, within the gums, which are ugly and rough; and no tooth is black and yellow and rotten until the corruption reaches the gums, and the tooth becomes bad-smelling. It is necessary that you hold the patient's jaws in your hands, and his teeth in your sanctum, and pull out the visible teeth until nothing remains; and so do for the blackness and green, jaundice, and other types, as long as they are clean; and if what is at the root of the problem is removed first, it is good; if not, repeat again on the second and third day, until you have everything pulled. And know that teeth require various tools to pull, according to what the work demonstrates, because the instruments used to pull out teeth from between others have different shapes than those used to pull single teeth. Keep these shapes and others with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	You should cure the tooth of its pain as soon as possible, for you must not delay in treating it at all, because it is a very delicate matter so there is no excuse for postponing it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	If the patient is in great pain, then it is important that you are certain about which tooth is causing it.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain continues, and the patient thinks it is a healthy tooth, so you extract the good tooth; however, the pain does not leave until the bad tooth is removed, as we have already seen with these patients; and once you are certain about which tooth is causing pain, it is important that you scrape around the tooth with a strong spatula to protect the gums from all sides; then move the pliers gently back and forth at the first touch, as long as they are well-aligned, and tighten the pliers; keep the patient's jaw in your hand between your knees, and hold it firmly so it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, if it does not come out, take none of these tools and push it gently from every side, moving it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	If the tooth is broken and missing, it is necessary to fill the gap with cloth or thread, either through the opening or the perforation; and if it is tightly stuck with pliers, be careful not to break it while pulling; and it is very important to work gently around the gum line to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	Be very careful not to break it, and if a part breaks off, return it to the patient; due to the evil of its root, it will cause greater pain than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful not to act like the ignorant healers who, by their haste and courage, break the bones at every turn, and do not heed what has been said; but they bring on great illness through their speech, or because of the bones they break, as we often see; and when the swelling is drained, wash the wound with wine or honey and lint; and the pus that comes from it occurs often, so use vitriol powder; and if this does not help, then cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, with which to mute the bones first, should be long and sharp with thick handles, so that they do not bend when you pull out the tooth; and these are their shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let there be strong members such that they do not bend when pulled, and made of iron well-forged, and toothed for firm hold.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root holds fast when pulled, it is necessary to place over it moist cotton or butter overnight or for two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the eyes are relaxed, then apply pliers called 'algefri', which makes the joints look well-cared for; and they are made inside like a file and this is their form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out of these claws, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and put the instrument called 'alethal' (i.e., a plier), which has this shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is hard and dense so that it does not break, and the root jumps out through this, that is good. If not, use all the instruments, and the shapes will come as follows:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument with two prongs, the shape is as follows:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are used in the reasoning of teeth, and this tool that resembles large pliers, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	This tool should be strong so it does not break, and you should know that many tools for teeth exist; there are also other tools, which are not mentioned. The most skilled surgeons create their own tools, according to the specific needs shown by their work and the disease, because there are many different conditions, and if a part breaks or becomes unstable, and he seeks the appropriate tools I have told you about, using gestures to indicate what is needed, then its form is as follows:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be large and well-fastened to hold the bone, so that it does not escape but can be held and removed; and then return the limb to suitable medicine, and if there is decay in the bone, even if it is small, use all these instruments.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural shape of the body, and its form is ugly, especially in young women, it is necessary that you know if the tooth is grown after the others and not in its proper place, and one cannot saw or file it; then extract it. And if it is mobile with the tooth, take this instrument whose form resembles a small beak, and let it be of sharp steel.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And take a small knife in your hands each day for the pain in your teeth, and because you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that it can be filed, file it from one side as this form shows:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	It is also like filing the metal used to make needles; file the tooth gently with your fingers every day until it stops moving, then in the end, it should be completely smooth without any roughness, and if the dens (teeth) is too sharp, it can hurt the tongue, so you must file the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not hurt or impair speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth aches
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth aches greatly, either by impact or pulling, and the patient cannot bear pressure on it, he suffers immense pain, and medicines to restrain it are useless. They should be restrained with a golden thread; for silver threads turn green and rot, but gold never changes. The thread must be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the space between the teeth. If you need to adjust the teeth, take the thread and wrap it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the aching tooth(es) between the other teeth, as many as there are, until you reach the healthy tooth on the opposite side; then continue the wrapping and gently but firmly pull until it no longer moves. Your finger should be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the bones with file clippers and assemble them, and insert them between the healthy teeth, and arrange them so that the tongue does not move; and leave it as tight as possible while it can stay, and if it loosens, the thread will pull again; if it remains tight and serves thus for all its time, this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the arrangement of the two healthy teeth and the two muscles, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is dislodged, it must be replaced in its place, fresh by fresh, as we have said; and let no one intervene unless they are skilled and patient, and never form a tooth from the bone of a sheep, but place it in the empty socket and tighten it as we have said, and keep it tight for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	cut the bandage of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Never cut the ties that originate beneath the tongue, whether from natural causes or an accident during a deep wound; and the work involves opening the mouth of the patient with care, placing his head in yours, and lifting the tongue. Then cut the nervous ligament widely, as much as possible, until the tongue is freed from its attachment, and if there is any hardness or newness (from the injury), immediately insert a hook and cut widely that ligamen; be sure not to sever the artery below. After finishing, raise the limb with rosewater or oil, then apply a thin layer of linen beneath the tongue; and do this for each patient every night so that the ties cannot heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the bleeding comes from an abscess that has been broken open, and if it does not stop, cauterize it with a slow-acting cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with another remedy until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see it is red or black or hard, so the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it turns pale, and there is moisture, soak it with vinegar, and cut out the lump with a delicate spatula from both sides; and if it does not stop at your work, place vitriole on it until it is stained, then return to your work until all is healed. Then lift the limb gently and steadily, and treat it with other remedies until it is well.
des apostemes de la gorge	from the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there appear in the throat small cavities called "godath", which are properly known as the two amandres (amandrs), and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, if they are not cleaned properly, be careful: these abscesses are hard to the touch, of small size and faint color, so do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they are red and the root is thick, do not touch them with iron, also for the discharge of pus; but leave them until they are dry, and then you will remove them, or they might break on their own. And if they are of white color, and the root is thin, have a tool prepared to cover them, but first ensure that the abscesses are calm and at ease.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient stand before the sun, and his feet in a healthy position, open the mouth and grasp the tongue with the fingers between his hands, pressing it down onto the entire instrument, from which comes the shape; and let it be of silver or fine gold as if a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	You cannot press the tongue down onto all of this instrument and see the abscess, so take the chisel and the file and insert them into it, pulling upwards as much as possible; do not touch any part of the threads with them, then cut with the instrument, from which comes the shape that resembles a hook; nevertheless, the head is curved, one side to the other, and they are very sharp, made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, if it is like pliers, then take it to shape thus:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And it should be cut on one side and not the other; and when you have extracted one of the mandibles, extract the other in the same manner, and after the incision, rinse the patient's wound with hot and fresh water, or with broth of pomegranates cooked, or bags of myrtle, or similar things, until the blood is stopped; then treat it while it is still clean; and no other abscesses will form in the throat besides the two mandibles if they are extracted in this way.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was located inside her throat, namely a small abscess; and the entire throat was tightly closed, so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passageway, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if left thus for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that it had pushed aside two ribs through the two openings where it entered.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then quickly inserted a blade into one of the openings where the abscess entered, and pulled it through, extracting a large amount of pus; then I did the same in the other opening, opening the mouth and pressing the tongue; after inserting the blade into the abscesses and scooping out some of the pus, only a little blood came out, and thus the passageway from the throat was opened for the woman. She began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to drain the abscess for a long time; but the abscess reappeared, filling the space I had cleared, growing very large. Then I bandaged it and cauterized it inside the throat: in this way it healed without further growth. And from these actions, God be praised, I was able to save her.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the eye descends and is swollen and distant, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is removed, thick and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the previous section, but the treatment does not help, and you see that the abscess is calm, and it is small, then it is necessary to drain it; and the round one that is not far away, and it is bloody or of a dark color, then it is advisable to avoid incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	So it is necessary, when you see this, according to the manner I have said, that you lay the patient before the sun and press his tongue with the instrument of which we spoke earlier; then insert the point into the eye and pull it out, and cut it with one of the two instruments I mentioned in incising the two joints.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut off more than the excess beyond the natural limit; for if you cut too much, it hurts the voice and speech. After the incision, use what we said about incising the two joints, and treat it as long as it is clean.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient feels great pain, it is necessary that you use instruments for the cauterization of the sensitive parts.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of cauterization is very sharp and hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should place his head on a healthy surface, and then press his tongue against the instrument described in the chapter on cauterization (or mentioned previously), using a sharp, hot tool. The application should not be too thick or too thin; and this is the shape of said instrument:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the patient hold a hair, as if it were the handle of a spoon, and place the tool with all the medicine on the eye; have the patient lie on their side, so that saliva and mucus from their mouth can absorb the medicine without going down to the throat or causing discomfort. Then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour until you see it stop bubbling and the stinging of the medicine is soothed; and if you notice, take cotton and wrap it around some tool, dampen the cotton in the medicine, and keep pressing the cotton into the socket until it sticks to the eye; do this often until the cauterization is complete, then leave it to dry, and after three or four days, or five, if you need to repeat the cauterization of the medicine, repeat it, and after the cauterization, clean around the eye with cotton soaked in buttered water, and purify everything that surrounds the medicine; rise with cold water, and perform gargling until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than cautery or incision; if it is carried out by fumigation in this manner, take plenty of calament, hyssop, oregano, rue, chamomile and avernus (or similar herbs), and mix them all together in a pot, then place the pot on the fire and bring to a boil; ensure the pot is well sealed with a tight lid, as described below:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	It should be either of silver or gold, and one of the joints should be compressed in the mouth of the patient until the vapour rises to the eye through the canal, until the eye becomes numb; afterwards, it often recurs as the eye dries out, and take care not to perform this at the beginning of the onset of a hot abscess, as many complications may arise; do not attempt this except during the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and insert within the mouth a thin piece of wool, so that it does not burn too hot; for the woolen thread does not allow the steam to heat up the mouth, and it is a good remedy for healing together and salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a burning sensation occurs in the throat from bone or fish spines, or some other thing. Therefore, it is necessary that you treat what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with all the instrument so that you can observe the thing; and if it does not open and is stuck in the throat, you must make the patient vomit so that the food cooks in the stomach. Perhaps this will dislodge the thing through vomiting. Or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a dry crust of bread, and then ties a thread to it and pulls it out; and when it reaches its place, it will open up and then you can pull it out forcefully. And if it does not come out as we have said, take an instrument made of salt according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved towards the throat so it can enter more easily, and hold the head elevated; beware not to touch the epiglottis, so that everything does not get stuck, and do not push the bone inside; and move the patient to insert the instrument, because it needs to be moved where the thing is reversed; if it goes down, pull it out slowly throughout the entire instrument until it comes out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never is the throat treated with medicine, as I have said in the previous section, except through medicinal treatment; and if that does not help, then examine the throat of the patient in sunlight, and press the tongue with the instrument I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the vein, draw it back to every tiny needle or use subtle pliers that are suited for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if the above does not work, take a horsehair rope and tie it around the throat of the patient, then tighten or loosen the rope until the vein heats up and does its job. Do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient has a fever with water every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	then take full glasses of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it in slowly, allowing him to swallow it, and do this often; and as soon as the vein feels the water, it will close.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not break as we have said, and fills the patient with bad odor from the instrument used in the fumigation of the eye, do this many times, for it will eventually break without warning.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	The method of fumigation is as follows: you fill a pot with hot coals and place a perforated cover over it, through which the instrument for fumigation is inserted. The patient then puts the tip of the cane in their mouth, seals their mouth, and inhales the smoke until they feel the sensation, without allowing any smoke to escape; if the sensation does not occur, repeat the fumigation several times. The patient should endure thirst, eat salty and spicy foods, and avoid drinking water; then it will be necessary for them to expel the foreign body using this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats the wound, if it is possible to see, resembles a curved pair of pliers for entering the throat; and it looks like a hawk's beak, and has the hardness of lime, so that whatever it grasps, it cannot let go; and here you can see its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many appearances of abscesses are, according to what the memory brings to mind in this book, and they differ in terms of perforation and size; and there are two manners, one being in its own likeness, and those that hold moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is for the joints where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscess of the head is different from that of the base, and the abscess of the muscular limb is different from that which comes in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if, for an abscess, one must not pierce while the bowel is still alive according to its completion; and if for such cases it is necessary to pierce when they are fully grown, and do not die according to their completion, like abscesses that are in the joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	Because when an abscess comes from the destruction of the joints, and it is left until it becomes putrid around, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	If the abscess is in the main member, and you delay piercing it until it becomes gangrenous, it will harm the principal member; or if it is from the foundation, pierce it likewise while it is still alive, otherwise it will putrefy completely, become swollen inside, and develop a fistula, and cannot heal fully.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time of perforation of the abscess which is killed according to completion, and this is when the pain is soothed, and the fever departs, and the pain and redness decrease, and the swelling of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you should make the perforation depend on the level of the abscess, and where it opens; and it should be a long perforation in the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in the joints and muscles and arteries, and everywhere equally, where there is no swelling.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fatty part of the body, it is better to leave the incision until it has healed completely, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before the abscess has formed, the body's defense mechanism will release much blood, and it will fill with pus; and by chance, the lips may harden and get infected from the wound.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if an abscess is pierced according to its size from the flesh and the part of the body that needs it.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must treat them with small incisions, small openings; and in large incisions, large openings, and many fissures according to the size of the abscess; and if it is necessary to insert a heart, or cover it; when it has healed as much as cloth, and becomes numb, one must do the same as for buboes: and if they are cut in three angles, and such that one covers them like the fur of a myrtle, like the abscesses of enemies; and if there is such where a large incision is made, and other sizes and similar cuts.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	For those who have no head, like a superficial sore abscess, you must pierce it thoroughly; and if the abscess is large and has a great bowel, and you pierce it, do not drain all the bowels at once, but a part of them; then stop the abscess for another day, and then drain nothing from there; repeat this many times little by little until all the bowels are drained; especially if the patient is of weak strength, or a pregnant woman, or small children, or old, decrepit men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For sometimes the patient jumps due to the release of gas from the bowels, which might cause the illness to worsen and you should not be alarmed.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Beware therefore of this chapter with great caution, and when you have felt your abscess, if the wound is clean, and if it is a small one, apply a bandage of lint or cotton; but if it is a large abscess with many openings, you should insert a tent into each opening so that they touch each other. If you find a hard part in the abscess and have sewn it up, fill it with dry cotton or linen raspings without moisture and bind it for three days; then remove it and treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, apply ice and cold water, and moisten the cloth, and place it on the bleeding wound repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the bleeding persists, apply pressure and treatment, and use the powders mentioned in this book, and if it's a deep wound or an abscess, cover it with moistened cloth with wine and hot oil; and if it's fresh and the abscess is fleshy, place moistened cloth with cold water and vinegar or hot oil, for up to three days, as we have said; then remove the abscess and clean and treat it, as appropriate, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: for I have already told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and now see this chapter.
des soros	from sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or there are small abscesses that come from the head, which are similar to threads, as in the eye of a needle, and there are many like them.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are large and fleshy, with moisture like pulsations; and if there are such that are hard and difficult to cut, then the arteries do not contradict.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the shoulder is such that you should test every instrument called "entromissory," from which the form comes as follows, containing something.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they make a hole from above down through it.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is emptied, if it does not tear the skin that contains the moisture, it returns immediately once you leave nothing there; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present; if not, use water and string, and apply to the wound, leaving it until the next day; this will heal those who are delayed by night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then resume the bandaging, as before, on the second and third day, as long as you know it does not stay in place at night; then treat the wound with suitable medicine until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess persists firmly, as this form indicates, cut it long; and drain its pus, and scrape from all sides, and apply all your care to draw out the poison from where it lies; and if the artery is against you, do as I have told you.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do the same for an abscess that is hard, and cut and cure it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut the abscess and its moisture gently, for it contains little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if none of these abscesses or pimples have any moisture, and these are the type of abscesses I found on an old woman's head—they felt like hard, sharp, white stones that could not be crushed—and if anyone were to try to break them, it would cause just as much harm as a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses that appear on the head or neck—especially those affecting children and the roots of the ears—it is important to keep the opening as clean and open as possible to allow the pus to drain; and treat them accordingly.
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times this abscess appears in the neck, and discharge pus, and cause pain, and never comes anywhere else on the body, and it is sore, and intertwined with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each goiter is properly inside its rib cage, as we have said of the neck abscess; and there are many types of goiters.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	Some of them contain moisture, and some are evil and do not obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In the one that you see has a good appearance when touched, and is similar to the color of the body, and is quiet from every side and is not closed in the neck or the artery or the duct, and is not too deep; then it is necessary that you cut it from above, and peel it from every part, and the two lips of the heart be open as we have said in the abscesses of the neck; and take care little by little, and be sure not to cut the nerve or the vein, and do not allow the fingers to slip, and do not look too far ahead so that you do not cut anything you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you open the vein or artery and it does not allow you to work, apply vitriole (poison) ground into a powder that stops blood flow, and constrict the wound; leave it until the abscess is calmed, and the wound softened, and begin to heal.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is stained with blood, return to your task until you complete it; then be careful with your work if there remain any small scars, scrape and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the scar, it is not enough that you remove just the scar at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and leave it to fall without harm; then apply old Egyptian poultice to the wound for healing.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you remove the entire swelling, it is necessary that you close both lips of the wound and sew them now, since there is no delay due to excess because of the size of the swelling.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you understand how to close the root of it, and pull firmly, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those swellings that have excess fluid, cut them where they open up to die; and the cutting should be as previously mentioned, depending on it, then apply these treatments with dressing and similar things, so that it does not corrupt what is delayed from corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, continue treatment with ointment until it is healed.
de squinance	from squintiness
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	They spoke and wrote about the incision of the throat, but I have never seen it done in our land, and these are the writings of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those with squintiness, it is necessary to avoid the incision in the throat known as "epiglote"; no aid should be provided for this, because all the veins and the source of the patient's pain are located in those who have an abscess near the mouth, or in the throat or in the stomach.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the throat from a cold, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent the loss caused by strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, we should make it three or four small cuts across, between the two circles, or according to the depth of the cut, not penetrating into the cartilage; and these cuts are most suitable for cutting through the epiglottis so that there is no charring, and the edges remain long and clean.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the surgeon is cautious, he should extend the skin of the throat to the entire circle, then cut through the heart as it reaches the channel, and avoid blood vessels, if you see any, and then remove the tissue, as we have said; and by examining the section of the stream of the channel that has burst out from the broken place, and by the loss of voice, it is demonstrated that the wound should remain open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed and there is doubt about the strangulation, bring together the two edges of the wound close to the heart, and cut through them entirely down to the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote healing, as long as it is healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis states that this should not be done until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be near death, for it lacks breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then, they should cut the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he will breathe through the wound, thus preventing death; and for this reason, the ancients ordered that the wound be kept open until the evil of the disease has passed, which can take three or four days. And then they commanded that the wound be sewed up and dressed, as long as it was healing; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a damsel took a knife, and stabbed it into her throat, cutting part of the tongue from the gum; and I was called to cure her, but found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had come from it; I realized that there was no strength or passage for it to go anywhere but the throat, and the veins burst out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I acted swiftly, sewed up the wound, and cured it until it was healthy; and after she had been weak from voice, she recovered to her former state; that is why I say that in the construction of the epiglottis, one should not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	from the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Cystic abscesses are called "neck hernias," and they are large abscesses in the color of a jaundice, and they occur mostly in women; and they are according to two manners: natural and accidental; or naturally without any cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental is according to two manners: one seems like fat, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear, and it does not suit to make sharp cuts except in the small ones, and test and seek all the entry points: if you find them just like the fat ones, and cannot be moved in any way, then cut them as one would cut the nose, and remove them entirely if possible, and bandage well, and treat as appropriate until they are perfectly healed.
des nous	From us.
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways concerning us, of which I will speak of all their similarities; and now it is necessary that I explain the entire difference between our origins and end.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that the end is characterized by heat and fever, as long as the boiling has not occurred and the putrefaction is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the new birth, there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it possesses satisfaction, which is its own sack and according to the state of the body, and begins like a seed, and becomes large; and they are according to two similarities, either fat or moist, and have much color as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	You should, when you approach the treatment of a new illness, that you try and inquire first about all the instruments called "instrumental" according to their form, as is explained in the following chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	The method of investigating abscesses is to press more or less gently the place you find the abscess, and turn your fingers in and out repeatedly, until you know that the instrument has reached the center, then, according to the size of the abscess, extract the instrument, and be careful not to damage it.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture runs through the cut, what color it has, do as I said for other abscesses; and if the instrument does not come out moist after that, know that it is stuck, so make a cross with your fingers, take hold of it with pincers, and carefully peel it from each side, taking care to extract all the pus, or cut it away if you cannot remove it whole.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.
