For if it does not stay, it returns to the mind repeatedly; and if it lingers a little, without greatly troubling you, it employs the wound with some corrosive powder or hot water, constricts the wound, and applies soothing things on top, and treats other treatments until it is healed; and if it becomes great, it costs both lips of the wound, and treats those who cause harm.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the veins break against you or anything else prompts haste, use the vitriol powder and leave it for two or three days until the wound pus forms and the blood flow stops; then return to covering what has receded again.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Look here at the shapes of the instruments that enter the body, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three quadrants called 'albaret', and one called 'breb', and they are also like needles used to cut through sores, and they are made of gold, bronze, or iron, and the yellow ones are more effective in encircling fistular abscesses; and these are also of three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the wound.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the hooks are very similar, as you can see: large, medium, and small; and there are also hooks with two curves in three ways; and some have three curves, also in three ways; and others have two curves, or even just one curve, and these too are necessary for their respective uses.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these instruments is sharp, and some do not cut well from one side, causing the skin to be scraped, so that neither vein nor nerve are severed; and these inserments are screws returned in several pieces, so that the patient does not lose blood when opening abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and they should only be used on fleshy parts, such as legs, arms, breasts, wounds, and similar places; and never make another small instrument resembling the edges of pincers, according to this form, to stop blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it should never be placed in a place that heals quickly after cutting veins, arteries, and never according to this great form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never inflame the breasts of any man when they begin to be corrupted, as long as they seem like women's breasts; they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them must do so according to this form from this line b until g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then peel off the fat and apply medicinal herbs with charred ash, then close the two lips of the wound with stitches and treat it until it is healthy; if the breast sinks downwards and becomes soft due to its size, as it does in women, making them appear in two ribs, through two similar openings; so that one rib holds the other at the end of each, making the larger line contain the smaller according to this form from this line b to line g. Then peel off the skin between the two lips, remove the fat, and apply what we have mentioned regarding stitches and powders, as well as anything necessary for treatment, until it is healed; if it is not healed, or the incision has not been properly made because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the flow of blood, it is necessary to fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive dressing; leave it until it absorbs the fat and moisture, then treat it until it is completely healthy.
des apostemes des asselles	from abscesses under the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses that come from under the armpits and are hard scrofulas or have lumps, and if they contain moisture.

Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez. de la routure de l’artere	from the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When an artery bursts and the skin above it is sealed, it often leads to abscesses, and also occurs in the veins, causing them to become swollen and abscessed; and if one recognizes this as being due to an artery, then the abscess should be left to heal on its own; and when you feel it at your extremities, it feels strange; and in the case of veins, they appear red and inflamed; and it is foolish to drain such an abscess, especially when it is deep within joints and surrounded by bones and other parts, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary to watch over the iron cure, and he who is in charge must also be vigilant, and on him who has an arterial wound made above the skin, then carefully open the artery from the threads, as much as it is exposed; then insert a needle from below into the other side of the wound, and pierce it through to the other cost, and tightly hold the artery with a double thread in two parts, according to what I have taught you about extracting the two arteries located in the temples; then mark the space between the two threads with an instrument until there is nothing left that can be cut out, and carefully remove the abscess; then administer the cure as soon as the wound begins to heal; then treat any subsequent treatments appropriate for that wound, as long as it is healthy; and if the abscess is located along a vein, it is necessary for you to keep your hand over the abscess from its beginning to the entire skin, then insert the needle below the space you are holding in your hand, and pierce it through, and hold it with a double thread, so that you can pull it from the other side; then secure the abscess as I have told you, or tie one end of the thread to each part; and if you doubt that the threads have disappeared, insert another needle into all the parts below the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and hold the threads in three parts; then remove the excess from the abscess until everything superfluous is cut off, then cut away the excess skin and leave what is tied; then cover it with a moist cloth dipped in wine and oil, and administer treatments with bandages and ointments as long as it is healthy.
des apostemes des ners	from the abscess of nails
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly to abscesses in arteries and veins, nails can also develop abscesses when they are injured or subjected to excessive work, among other things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this occurs more frequently in joints and fingers, causing abscesses that appear as if from the flesh of the body, and are in various shapes with great pain, not completely in line with the rest of the body, but deviating towards the heart; and they move little or not at all forward or backward, or upwards or downwards, and the joint affected should not be bound with iron, for it may cause contraction; and those located on the head or forehead cause the skin to pucker.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, and it can be gripped with tweezers, dig it out at its base; and if it's large, suspend it on a hook, and scrape off the skin, then cut out the flesh and sew up the wound, and treat it until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	Des grosses boces pendans" translates from Old French to "hanging jaws
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	It occurs in the belly alone, and nowhere else, and is a disease known as "fungus" due to its appearance, it has subtle roots, and causes large and small stools; I have seen men with two or more fungus-like growths in their bellies, there was no distinction between them, they were white, had thin roots, and continued to exude moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I gathered them and found in one eighteen ounces weighing, and in the other six ounces, and the work of the incision is such that you consider if the patient is moist, and the color of the artel is white and moist and of a subtle root; if it adheres to the spatula, perform fire cautery in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For cutting often brings too much blood loss, and if it goes without control, then be quick to cauterize; and if you see the patient afraid and anxious about the incision, take a well-made thread and tie the artel as we have said, and leave it for two days; then restrain it and do not cease to pull the thread until it extracts the artel without effort; and if the roots are large, be afraid most especially when cutting near the belly, but you can still cut half of it, then cauterize so that it does not recur; then dress the wound, and be careful not to cut the thin part which is of a bad color and poor texture and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess enhanced, and I will come to the treatment of the cancer hereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the wound is closed due to crusting.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the crust is due to cauterization of the wound or fissure of the flesh, and it is on the belly and not in any of the bowels, as happens with other openings, or from bloodletting or cutting of veins or arteries as is usually done, or from flatulence; and if it is through an opening in the flesh and through the emission of the bowels, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the flesh, and it is a slight thing without pain, and has various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to an intestinal issue, then it is more complex; when pressed with the hand at its points, it repairs itself and returns, and sometimes becomes sealed off, widening greatly at the bath entrance or through hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a minor issue and opens well when pressed with the hand, without constraint; and if it is due to blood, it appears through these signs: large and hard abscesses, and is fixed in quantity; and if it is due to wind, it feels soft to the touch, and the severity is such that you must observe its appearance, whether it is the blood of an artery, a vein, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is necessary, you must leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter about abscesses, both for the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if it appears to be an intestinal or bowel problem, you must instruct the patient to keep their leg still and extend it straight, then mark around the bowel; next, command them to move it gently between your hands, then wrap the marked area with a strong thread or a firm silk string, making sure the bowels are completely immobile; then open the other half of the abscess that is above all the pain, and insert your finger, exploring the intestines. dou chancre	A cancer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have spoken in the previous section about the appearance of cancer, and how it should be treated with medicine, and how to avoid iron therapy; we say that cancer is insidious and requires great caution in its cure, and they advise the ancients that when a cancer is located where it can be cut out, as is the case with cancers of the flesh, or in the foot, or similar places, then it must all be removed when it is in the beginning; however, for large and old cancers, you should not approach them, because I have never been able to heal any, nor has anyone ever healed one before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And for the work when a cancer is located where it can be removed, as we have said, do not at any time purge the patient of black blood; then make them healthier if there is evident bloating, and cut out the cancer from a good place to perform the operation; then pour on your poultices or cancers, and remove all parts, leaving nothing behind; let the blood flow completely, and check the place with your hand or anything else, and if the occurrence of blood makes you hesitate regarding the incision of an artery or vein, cauterize it until the wound is healed; then apply another cure until it is healed.
de ydropisie	Of hydropisia
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already discussed the signs of hydrops and in what way the collection of water occurs, and the symptoms of each condition, and the treatment using medicines, and that which is treated with iron; in these two cases only; for touching iron on these two conditions is dangerous, namely tympanitis and yposcare, as it is a deadly matter. Therefore, when treating this hydrops-like condition, called "eclites" by medicine, and the cure does not help, consider if the patient is weak or has another illness besides hydrops, such as intestinal troubles or similar conditions; in these cases, do not use iron, for there is doubt; and if you see a patient with strong vitality, and they only have hydrops without any other illness, and are neither too young nor too old, then proceed thus: lay the patient gently on your hands, and the assistant presses the abdomen towards the lower part, draining the water to its lowest point, then take the sharp spatula according to this form.
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And make incisions from the second part.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Stab it with a point, but do not push it in so deep that it reaches the intestines when inserted, and do not let it pierce; then observe if there is any droplet formation towards the intestines. It is necessary to make an incision from three fingers' width directly beneath the armpit; and if the hydrops is due to a disease of the liver, make your incision on the left side of the armpit; and if it is due to mucus, it should be on the right, and do not let the patient lie on the incision site so that the excess fluid does not flow towards the weak joint. Then cut through all the skin with a tool, and sever, and gently pull your hand across all the tissue between the skin and the sinew as if scraping with a fingernail or slightly further; then cut the sinew until the tissue comes to rest in its natural position, and this is the shape of the instrument:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it resembles a small silver chain, delicate and made of fine gold or silver, with one opening at the base and three on one side, and two on the other, and one on the opposite; and the part is cut as if with a quill, which is the form of the incision that scribes make when they cut quills.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top of it is the opening, so that when the instrument comes into contact with water, it sinks directly onto the instrument; then empty half or a third of it, for if you remove more than is necessary at that moment, perhaps the patient dies due to the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he falls unconscious, or approaches death; but empty according to its quantity and according to what the nature of the virtue in the patient indicates, and his pulsations. Then take the instrument and hold back the water, which is now retained by the plug that stops the opening I mentioned above, which you pierce in this way; then repeat the process on the other side the next day, if you see the patient suffering, and remove a small amount of water; do this for several days, and be careful not to let it dry up completely.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and leave much water, either by burial or hot sand, or through sweating or a bath, or in the sun, and he turns color; then cure him with drying medicines as soon as he is healed, and cauterize his stomach and liver and spleen after draining the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	from the obstruction of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born without an opening in the penis, or if the opening is small, or it is not in its correct position.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary for him to pierce all the very subtle spatules according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then open the very subtle cleft of the bladder, and hold it closed for three or four days, and when he wants to urinate, remove the closure, let him urinate, and then replace it; however, sometimes it is not necessary, because the hot urine that comes out will not allow it to be closed again.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the opening is small, it requires a gentle closure of the bladder as we have said, so it will enlarge.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have a gap in their joint are blighted, for no one is born with a gap at the top of the bone, so they cannot urinate until they raise their bone up; and they cannot engage in sexual activity because the matter cannot reach the marrow, and this is a terrible disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient lies on their back, then the gap in the bone and its head, as well as the top part, are opened up to the size of a feather, so that the gap is wide enough; and be careful not to let blood flow, which often happens, and if it does, stop it with what stops blood, and treat the wound until it heals.
des pustules de la verge	from the pustules of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often, this inflammation appears on the penis, and it can be either benign or malignant; it is necessary to prick them gently with a needle, scrape and clean them thoroughly, then apply a moist cotton ball in an Egyptian ointment; then continue treatment with the ointment of diaphoretic until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the inflammation is malignant, with putrid color and discharge, it is necessary to treat it with cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have achieved it, and if the splint is comfortable, let it rest on the body with a portion inside the wound and another outside; then it is necessary to remove the splint inside first, and when it is removed, treat the wound.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it together, unless you are certain that the splint is not damaged, blackness and decay will appear in the splint and the wound; then it is necessary to remove all of what is black and corrupt, then apply a poultice of honey and flour made from the bark of red apples and leaves, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a blood clot occurs, then administer the lunar cauterization according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauterization is carried out as follows: that is to say, in case of blood clot or corruption; and if the part of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary to insert a plug made of soft cloth into the urethra and let the patient urinate; and when the hair on the head of the penis is dry, which occurs in those who have not been circumcised, or there is a wound or abscess, then you should scrape it with a sharp instrument until the ties are loosened and the part of the penis is freed from all sides; and if this is a difficult matter to decide, it is necessary to scrape it gently with a spatula at the base of the penis and the stone, then separate them slightly and put a fine linen cloth moistened with cold water over it so that it does not dry out.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a dislocation like other wounds; however, when we perform this operation of our own will, especially on children, it is necessary that we make the best and most gentle incision for healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcision for their children, because they did not practice it in their laws, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen most of the masters and elders who practiced circumcision around that time, and they did it with strength and skill; if it had been according to custom, since there were two layers, someone might cut through this one and delay that one.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or she returns to the wound, and the pain doubles, and with the cleaning that is done from time to time, the tip of the member is not assured; and in the cleaning of the nail, by chance, the iron escapes and corrupts the work, and often they heal in such a way that they do not need cleaning, and I wish it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the cleaning that is done with force on every link of thread, I have found the goodness of experiment, for the forces cut precisely as well from above as from below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because when you press your hand, if you cut evenly in all directions, then the thread should be well twisted around the skin; and make sure the manner of the first operation so that the child, if it listens, understands that you are not making him suffer more than necessary by twisting the thread around the stick, and then make him feel at ease in every way possible. Then twist it between your fingers straight, and press the forces between your fingers or under your feet so that the infant does not see or notice any of the tools; then bring your hand back to the stick and blow on it, drawing it up as high as the end of the stick is; then clean it well of all the dirt gathered on it, then tie it with a double thread, and connect it to another thread; and hold it by the second link at the index finger and the little finger, and cut between the two threads, then gently remove the heart from above violently and pull the chief of the stick; then let the blood flow slowly, for that is how it heals; and apply powder on top and cover it with a cloth dipped in a mixture of rosewater, finely chopped fresh herbs, and good oil, and leave it until the next day, and treat it with care every day until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of purification is this: both shoulders should be held tightly and cut, and the shoulder blades should also be large and equally measured.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in purification is when the veins are not cut properly; then you must stretch your finger so that the shoulder joint becomes abscessed; and do the same for the other, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, use pliers, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it persists for three days, and the area under the arrow is swollen, leave it until the abscess is calmed, gently scraping off the crust; cut it as much as you can, and be careful to avoid the arrow's shaft, which will not harm it in any way.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat therefore the injured part suddenly affected by powder (that we have spoken of in treating powders), and if it is cut too deeply, and it goes above, then it will cause no harm; treat it, therefore, as we have said, while it is whole.
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is caused by the obstruction of a stone, or frozen blood, or bowels, or a baby, or similar conditions, as we have described in the previous division; and if the urine cannot be released, and you observe that the retention is due to a stone in the bladder or at the neck of the bladder, it is necessary for the patient to be bent over his knees; pressure should be applied to his back, and he should extend his belly upwards from the lower part of his back, and restrain him as much as possible. Then the neck of the bladder is forced to expel the stone above, allowing the urine to flow; if it does not pass, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must provide an extraction for all instruments called "syringes", which have this shape: they should be made of fine, lightweight silver, like a bird's feather, with a length of about 1.5 palms, and be thin at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the method of urination is as follows: Take a double thread and tie one end with wool or cotton at the top of the syringe; draw out the thread inside the syringe, cut off the excess wool, and insert it up to the top of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and position the patient on a seat. Let them urinate while the syringe is gently inserted into the penis until it reaches the root, then double over the penis towards the tip. Then, insert the syringe before the bladder, and have the patient feel the urge to urinate until the bladder is empty, but not too much that it becomes painful because of its twisted position; tie off the thread tightly, following the wool as it goes, and extract the urine, then drain the bladder, and repeat with the syringe until the bladder is completely empty and the patient relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	From the illnesses of the bladder.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When ulcerations or abscesses come to the bladder, and putrefaction is gathered there, you should draw out water and medicines with a device called a 'clepsydra', and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has three openings: two on one side and one on the other, as you see; and the furrows by which the medicine flows are made so that they stop the flow well without addition, if one can draw out the moisture and push when necessary. And when you pour your medicines into the bladder, place the head of the container in the moisture and draw out the liquid slowly. Then, push firmly on the container; it will draw out the moisture from within and enter the bladder immediately, so that the patient feels it. This is the shape of a delicate enema bag used to enema the bladder: thus is it.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or gold, and the matter is more valuable; then remove it from the breast where it is lodged; take a sheep's bladder and fill it with the moisture you wish to use for cleansing, then tie it between the two breasts with a strong double thread, and warm the moisture over the fire. Then insert the end of the cleanse into the urethra, and press your hand on the bladder until all the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, make a circle of it, and pierce it around the circumference; then thread a strong thread through these holes, assemble the circle as one would an earl, and put inside what you wish to use: oil, moisture, and water. Tie it with the instrument, and do as you did with the bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	from the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already spoken of the methods for treating stones and their extraction, along with various medicines; and I have explained the difference between stones that cause rain and all the signs, and what kind of stone requires surgical intervention; and in the bladder, and in the penis; I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone that is lodged in the bladder occurs more frequently in children, and this is a sign of acute urine retention, resembling water in its subtlety; it opens up the urinary tract, greatly disturbing the patient, often recurring, and then becoming chronic; and most of these blockages originate from the kidneys. The cure for children up to the age of four is relatively light, but it is much more difficult for older individuals, especially those between youth and old age; the treatment is lighter for those with large stones, than for those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to treatment, it is necessary first to purify the patient with a cleanse, to draw out all impurities from the bowels.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often gets stuck when trying to pass stones.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet and upright them, moving them away from each other so that the stone descends completely into the bladder, never sticking up high; then place him between your hands with his hands resting on his thighs, causing the bladder to tilt downward; then tie him down and feel inside. If you feel the stone in the space, now hurry to cut through the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not come away with the touch, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, and if the patient is an adult, press gently on both sides; hold it in place at its base, and when you feel it give way, press firmly on your right side, and the stone will come out from the opening where you cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the assistant to press the bladder with their hand, and command them to extend their right hand upward and stretch it, while removing the skin from their left hand beneath the stones in the area where the cut is made; then they should apply the scoop-shaped tool, which forms the shape as follows:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And they make an incision between what is between the cheeks and the fundament, not in the middle but on the side of the left navel; and it should be straight on the stone, and your fingers should always be near the fundament, and the cut should be wide on one side and narrow inside, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; so that the pressure from the finger at the fundament causes it to come out easily without effort; and know that there is part with angles and margins where it comes out; if it is stuck, it is gripped as if it were a spearhead, round, and smooth, whose exit is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	If there are angles and margins where it comes out, make the cut larger; and if it does not come out, you need to use pliers that are also like a file at the tip to pull the stone so that it does not escape; or you can insert a small, curved instrument at the top; and if you cannot do this, you should enlarge the opening slightly and then extract the stone with vitriole; and if there is more than one stone, first pull out the largest one from the neck of the bladder, then cut around it, and finally pull it out, and then the smaller ones after that if there are any others.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, they want to cut it out, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things can happen to the patient: he dies, or his urine flows again through a wound that the limbs cannot heal; but nevertheless, strive hard to extract it with pincers, as you dislocate it piece by piece; and when you have completed your work, apply incense and aloe and dragon's blood to the wound, and bind it, and place on top a damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or oil and rosewater and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then dress the patient's neck, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you dislocate it, if a lot of good oil and water arises from it, then apply the curative ointment and basilic ointment, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses and corrosions occur in the wound and congestions of blood in the bladder, and urine retention, known in this manner as difficult with urination: then press your finger into the wound and extract the blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and rot; then cleanse the wound with water and oil and heat, and aid it in every way that you know, until it is healed; and it is necessary that at all times that you treat it, you bind both thighs together and apply medicine to the joint.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is caught in the urethra, and stuck inside, and urine cannot pass; then this cure that I say, to cut it many times, is excusable due to this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have tested this thusly.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take the iron at the forefront according to this form, and insert it into three pieces of wood.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the urethra beyond the stone, so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then gently push the iron into the urethra until it reaches the stone; and turn the iron in your hand slowly into the stone, as much as you can pierce the stone from the other side; soon urine will come out, then press your hand on what remains of the stone inside the urethra.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is broken and jumps with urine, and it pains the patient; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then insert a thread into the stone from below and another from above, then pull the thread, loosen the knot, and clean the frozen blood in the wound; and treat it until it heals.
de la piere des femmes	of women's stones
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It is rare for stones to affect women, and when they do, the treatment is difficult, hindered by three things: one is that the woman may be a virgin; the second is that it is hard to find a woman skilled in this matter, especially one who is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that, by chance, one may not find a woman well-versed in this art of midwifery; and the fourth way is that the stone of the woman's womb is more acute than that of a man, for which reason it must be cut deeper, and great fear exists. And if need arises, it is right that you should engage a midwife well-versed in it, and if she cannot be found, then look for one who is somewhat skilled; and present her with a prudent counsel regarding the life of women, or a woman who knows part of this art, and command her to do what you command regarding the inquiry about the stone; and take great care that this woman is chaste. Then she must push down her finger into the base and seek the stone; and if she finds it, she should constrain it from below her finger, and recommend that she pushes her left hand on the distended bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, she must move it little by little from the entrance of the bladder down to the root of the thigh; until it reaches the middle of the thigh where it is mobile, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move the stone above or below the thigh, or make a small cut first. Then press the stone out from the wound as much as possible, and know that there are many types of stones: small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and those with edges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know these similarities to understand the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the wound does not heal, put crushed vitriol on it and keep it there for an hour until the pain is gone; then return to your work, as long as the stone remains firm, and have the tools I told you for extracting stones from men to assist you in your task; and if the wound does not heal, and it's an artery that's cut, put powder on the spot and press with tenes and bends, and do not repeat this, leave the stone and do not pull it, unless by chance the patient dies; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat from the blood is calmed and the veins are opened, return to your work as long as the stone remains firm.
de hernie carnouse	Of herniated flesh
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Moisture is nothing other than a gathering of water or white wax, which is removed from the heart of things, that which contains the life; and it is called 'syphac', and never properly part of the life's web, if one thinks it another thing; and this is the skin of the coion between the white syphac we have spoken of; and this does not happen by chance.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this syphac is due to weakness that comes to the joints, and this material expands.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And it never comes from striking against the joints, and this moisture has many colors: it may be yellowish, without red, black, or white liquid, and so on; and these are signs to know this gathering, for if it is the white syphac we spoke of, then the abscess is bright red, long, shaped like a vein, and does not open the joints, as it is surrounded by moisture.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the wound bed, if it is accompanied by redness in a part of the flesh, then one thinks it is another wound; and if the moisture is between the skin of the tissue and the white part, then feel it well; then when you want to know the color of the moisture, try all the intrusions carefully, from which the form is determined.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, after examining the intrusions, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When treating it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healed according to their strength and the replenishment of their body; then place them on their back, on something slightly elevated, and cover them with many sheets; then have them sit on their left side, and command the attendant to sit on their right, and extend the probe to one of the two ribs near the heart of the tissue; then take the scalpel, and cut the skin of the tissue from above down to the elbow, and make the incision entirely straight by examining the skin of the tissue until it reaches the white part beneath, and carefully remove the flesh without damaging the heart of the rib; then make a large opening in the flesh with water at a suitable distance, and extract all the blood, and then apply your ligatures, and draw the flesh upwards; and do not touch the heart of the rib, but only the flesh; cut it as finely as possible, for if you do not cut it carefully, the blood will return; and if the operation is successful, put it back in its place when you have finished the work on the flesh; then sew together the two parts of the ribs near the heart with a stitch, and treat it like other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the heart corrupted by another illness, it is necessary that you hold the vessels that are suspended, in doubt about the flow of blood; then cut off the vein from everything that is suspended, and extract the heart, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the vein is assembled in two parts, knowing that these are two branches; cut off the other part as you did the first, then dry the blood and apply it to the wound with clean moistened wool; and place another layer of moistened wool in wine and oil, and lay the two veins on top of each other, and cover them with doubled cloth, and tie it securely according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two strips of cloth, and use coarse woolen material according to this form, and sew them together at the throat of the pants, one strip covering the hip joint up to the back, and the other on the palm side; also wrap the second piece tightly around the two angles, and assemble all the constraints in the loop of the pants. Never apply this cauterization with a hot iron, but use a delicate surgical knife, cut through the skin of the coions, and heat it as we have said, until the white substance that holds water is exposed; take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that substance at various places, and scrape off with this delicate hot cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the surgeon in all ways that you can, as long as you drain everything; and be sure that fire does not touch the wound; and know that this work is safer; and move cautiously to avoid infection, and treat the wounds of cutting carefully; and if anything contradicts you, whether it's an abscess or a complication from blood or any other thing, cure what contradicts you, as has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	If the patient is afraid and does not want to undergo this operation because of its horror, then perform a perforation as I have told you, and make sure that when you are certain through the signs that we have mentioned that the pus is present, place the patient in a sitting position; then incise the abscess from below towards the entire spatule (area) widely, and insert the perforation through the flesh lengthwise; make the opening wide enough for all the pus to flow out; then place cotton on it and bind it, allowing the remaining pus to drain, then dress the wound until the wound is healed. If the clean bandage does not allow the pus to come out into the wound's mouth, then it is necessary that you insert a needle or an instrument used to drain water from dropsy, as mentioned before; widen the wound and know that the pus will flow out and collect after six months or so, and when it has collected as before, the patient's condition will improve.
de l’aposteme des coions	from the abscess of the hairs
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	You know that in this chapter there are many different arrangements that cause great pain, which is why I think it is better to leave it alone; and I will tell you about the work and the similar conditions of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I therefore say that many abscesses come with hair, and most often in the hairs; and this is in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is due to the excessive acid and ague that spread through the hairs, or from percussion; and the color of the abscess matches the color of the skin; and it does not cause pain, and it is a severe abscess; and sometimes there are many grayish, piercing, and dark-colored abscesses, and sometimes they come from a new artery or the swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is through lack of an artery, if it is constricted by the hot disposition of an abscess when you press it with your hands; and it is not appropriate that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made from vein inflation is constricted by the disposition of being touched by the fingers, and he can be cut to fit this appearance, and other parts; and it is to open the heart of the matter, then heat will go up, and the pain becomes mild, white, soothing, and releases all parts of the heat.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the heat is already sore with these cuts, it is then appropriate that you release the heat and open it; and if it is in the veins or inside the vessels, it is then necessary to free all of this tension, and open it properly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the base of the hair is behind, it is necessary that you pull it out entirely, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, immediately apply the wound with moist wool in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the bowels
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess surrounded by a similar wrapping like a borion, with the swelling of the bowels, and it makes the patient suffer greatly when it appears; and the cure for this disease is just as important, if not more so, than the one mentioned before, and nevertheless, we will tell you about its work according to what the ancients did.
