Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You should make the sick person sit on a comfortable bed, then hang the suspenders of the testicles below your hands, to all the vessels near the penis, and stretch them gently; next, use a sharp spatula to cut through the vessels, as long as they are exposed, and scrape from each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries in temples. Then insert a needle where there is a double thread, and tie it to the first joint where the vein appeared, and tie it again to the other end; then cut them evenly according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupt moisture; then treat the wound as you would any other, so that no vessel seeps and nourishes one of the testicles. For by this there is no harm, and all vessels will be healed, it is necessary to pull the testicles through all vessels, so that the ovary does not lose its nourishment due to incision of the vessels, and dries up and cannot help itself.
de la routure dou syfac	From the rupture of the sinew.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The symptoms of this condition occur either through the rupture itself or from its extension in the abdominal area, causing the intestines to descend from that rupture into one of the hernias; and this rupture is either due to the sinew or to its extension, and these two conditions can arise from various causes: a blow, a jump, straining, or lifting a heavy weight, and similar things; and the signs when it is due to the sinew's extension include gradual occurrence over a long period and not appearing suddenly; and the hernia remains even until the entire area is affected, as the herniated material pushes against the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is from the incision that a sudden pain arises, and there appear various abscesses under the skin near, and this is due to the discharge of the intestine and flesh from the syphilitic fire.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never drain the abscess with the intestine, as it becomes stuck and causes great pain to the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these poor treatments of iron, for which one must be wary.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of the operation is that you command the patient to move his intestines back into the wound in his hand, if he can; then gently place your fingers on his collarbone between your hands, and press on his buttocks; then stretch the heart above, and cut all the skin from the cojons along. Then insert the blades of a scalpel inside the abdomen as needed to open the wound, so that they can pass through; then be sure that the sharp edge of the blade is exposed; then bring your index finger over the cojon, between the white flesh that lies under the skin of the testicle and the second piece of flesh, and between the second flesh; remove what is behind the testicle, and between the second flesh. And then move to the right hand inside the heart of the cojons, and place the white flesh on top with your left hand, and press on the testicle towards the tailbone. Command the surgeon to stretch the testicle upwards, and loosen what is attached behind the ligament; and be careful if there is no intestine or hard white flesh wrapped around it, and if you find anything, then put it inside the abdomen under the skin. Then take a needle with a thick thread made of 10 threads, and insert it into the back part of the flesh after the skin of the cojons; then cut off what appears of the threads, as long as there are 4 threads remaining; then arrange them one on top of the other in the form of a cross, and bind the flesh, which we have said lies under the skin of the cojons, with a strong ligature from both sides. Then wrap the threads around the testicles, and tie them in two parts so that no vasel can enter inside, and no fistula occurs; then place the first ligature 2 lengths long on each side of this one, and after these two ligatures leave some flesh under the heart of the cojons as wide as a finger; and afterwards do the same with all the rest according to the shape that the testicle takes. Then cut off the skin under the cojons as far as it is loose, and press on it, as we have said before; then apply moist wool to the wound, and put on the ligature we have mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never should the white part of the wound be cauterized as we have said, after incising, out of fear of bloodletting.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens, leaving the wound open until it heals itself; and if it takes time to heal, one should apply hot water and do as we have said, until it is completely healed; then treat the wound with another remedy, until it is perfectly cured.
de hernie carnouse	herniated cartilage
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this condition, one has never seen anyone who dares to treat it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients say that it is made like a root that holds together a joint, in such a way as you bind vessels after cutting them lightly on the inside; then cut through it and treat the abscess of him who opens, until the vessels stop bleeding; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	No rupture should occur unexpectedly, as we have said, and open the vessels; and let no intestines drop out; if they do, it is bad, and repair them every hour; nevertheless, if it persists too long at this point, one believes it to be a wound or an abscess, until the intestines drop out; and this happens due to the extension of the abscess at the angles, as we have said, for it becomes stretched, then softens and swells the vessels, and opens them; and its cure is by cautery, as we have previously stated; and never should it be cured in this way with iron. And it is that the patient lies often on his back between your hands, then cut the vessel of the rupture deeply according to the quantity of three fingers; and then extract the abscess that is beneath the skin from the usual habit; then take the knife and place it over the visible part of the abscess; and press it completely into the belly, then cut both the visible parts of the abscess on top of the handle, and pull them; then remove the handle, and do not cover or extend the abscess or anything else, as I have told you in the cure for the vessel of intestines; and then cure it with wound dressing.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you treat the wounds, if they are dirty and you clean the wound, as long as it is healthy.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The treatment is difficult, and it has no appearance in the fracture, but the cauterization is moved on this side, and it is closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the thick skin of the wounds
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the wounds becomes softened in no one's case, because the humors that are inside are mollified, and it is easy to see; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, to lay the patient on his back and cut the skin that is mollified on the natural skin; then bring together the two edges with a single stitch, or at most three stitches firmly; then cut between the stitches and cure it like other wounds, as long as it is healed, and pull out the thread.
dou chastrement	Medical treatment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	You know that castration is banned in our law, and for that reason I would not like to speak of it in this book; nevertheless, it is necessary to discuss it in two ways: first, by explaining its response when someone asks about it and how to perform it; second, because we often need to castrate some animals to help us, such as goats, sheep, cats, and other creatures.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I therefore say that castration is performed in two ways: either by attraction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method where we perform castration by attraction, we should keep the animal in hot water until the testicles become soft and relaxed; then you grasp them with your hand until they are returned to their normal state and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	From castration of the horse: You must tie up the animal and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tighten the suspensory, and cut each one, as you have properly scorched them; and leave no trace of any pain or subtle pain that is on the vessels; and this method of castration is more effective than the one done by attraction, because at attraction, by chance, something from the testicles may remain, causing the horse to desire lust; then treat the wound until it is healthy.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	A hermaphrodite is according to two manners in men: one is when between the two testicles, the shape of a woman's nature is open, with hair and never shortens the urethra.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And another way is in women, and it occurs on the wrist as well as a stick and two joints.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for hunger and thirst is to remove all the blocked passages, and treat it like other wounds; in the second way, for men whose urine leaks through the skin of the penis, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the goiter
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Goiter is a blocked passage on the natural part, as it is too ugly to see; no woman can move it as much as a hand, and this is its cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you hold the excess of the tendon in your hand or with pincers, and cut it lightly; do not sever too deeply, so as to avoid complications from blood loss, then apply other remedies until it is healed; and for another matter that appears at the mouth of the wound, and spreads, and perhaps jumps, and resembles a cow, and for this reason the ancients called it "cow disease.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	It is necessary that you cut it, as we said about the tendon, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic is the nature of a woman if she is not properly perceived, or the wound is small; it is either by birth or accident due to illness that comes upon her; or it is due to an ill-fitting garment, or a subtle or serious disease, and it occurs in the marriage bed, or on the side, or beneath, or wherever; and it affects conception, childbirth, and perhaps even the flowers (of youth). Knowledge of this comes from observing the signs.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the signs of inflammation are close at hand, either due to your own actions or through natural rights.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle disease and the signs are close to the liver, act quickly: place your two index fingers together, have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread apart; then form the two fingers into a shape as the subtle symptoms subside and the inflammation disappears. Then take wool and moisten it in oil and place it on the affected area, having the woman lie on her side each day so she cannot move.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if it feels hard and sensitive, you must then grip it with a spatula resembling a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is from a burn, suspend it at the joint and apply a compress; have remedies to stop blood flow, such as mint, dragon's blood, incense, together with plenty of egg whites; then apply a wide plaster so that the wound cannot close; and thus continue, applying a dry linen poultice; and perform other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when a blister appears from a burn, it must be covered according to this manner; if it is an abscess, it should be drained.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess that has enlarged in the wound, one must not attempt to treat it with fire.
des emorroides	from hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that, without proper treatment, can become severe. In the previous section, we discussed the signs and symptoms, and here I will outline the treatments for these conditions.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and their complications, when they are fully developed in the rectum and do not cause pain, can only be cured with heat.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	He who is at the mouth of the wound, one can feel, is he whom one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore advisable that you place the woman in a cold house, then apply pliers to grasp her teeth and cut them at the roots; next, sprinkle medicinal powders that stop blood flow, such as licorice and dragon's blood, and similar substances; then bind her feet to the wall for an hour, and immerse her in cold water. As the blood flows, prepare a mixture of sumac, scorch from pomegranates, gall, and similar substances, and then take oats flour, mix it with honey and ash, and make an ointment to apply on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it becomes wet, that's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If that does not help, apply cups on the back and around the breasts without causing harm; then take lint and soak it in plantain juice or mulberry juice mixed with old wine, and place them over the dislocation.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has subsided, apply the treatment to the wound as long as it remains clean; and that which is called "albathir" is red and resembles a rough head, so it should be covered as I have said in the previous text; then treat the wound until it heals.
des apostemes de la marris	from the abscess of the mare
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses occur in the mare, such as chancres, old abscesses, herpes, boils, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot abscesses, among others, as mentioned in the previous division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I discuss in this treatment the hot abscess that occurs in the mare, which is not truly an abscess but a swelling; and if you wish to know the effect of fire, consider whether the abscesses are aglow at the beginning of their appearance, full of heat and fever, and turn red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hasten to pierce, but let the patient suffer until the pain is eased; then place the ill person in a sitting position and give them two small pillows on which to rest, bending their legs away from the body, and supporting themselves on their back, bringing their feet together as much as possible. Then spread their thighs apart, placing their arms beneath their knees, binding them tightly with a good bandage; then open the patient's mouth towards the right side, and insert the instrument used to open the womb, from which this form arises; and it is important that when you insert this instrument, you first push the tip inside to determine the depth of the womb, so that whatever enters through the instrument does not go further than necessary, causing harm to the patient. If the instrument is too large, cover the depth of the womb with cloth, so that the instrument does not cause discomfort; and it should be placed on top, and the instrument itself tied off.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens and it is made with a gentle hand, if necessary, cover the base of the wound with a spatumile; and when the bowel is empty, put moist tents in rose oil or dry green oil into the wound to the full extent of the ulcer, and place a tent outside the wound over the ulcer and on the surrounding tissue, wet with clean water or cooked mullein and long aristology; then treat it after two days of treatment coming to this, as long as it is healed; and never raise the ulcer and the wound by a cleansing of water and honey, and then of water or cooked lily roots and aristology; then return to treatment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is healed in the ulcer, it is necessary to be careful not to use fire, but treat it as we have said in the previous section.
de l’enfantement	from birth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Skill is primary in the dance that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see a woman in labor and she desires to smell the air: then hasten for the child to be born; then know that these children are according to the natural figure, and are issued from their heads, and follow them; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press her belly so that the child is born immediately; for when he descends onto her head, she follows him with him, and the mother gives birth to her superfluities through good purification; and this one who comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it never comes upon its feet, but strikes the body or the joint, and the hands, or comes up to the stomach, or suddenly turns about on its neck, and assumes other evil shapes; so it is necessary for the doctor to be wise and clever in these matters, and to guard against error and deception, and I will show you all the shapes how aid should be given.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the fever comes upon his head by natural cause, and a woman is giving birth painfully, and her strength is weak, then she should sit on a saddle, or women should hold her; and prepare from oil or fennel seeds cooked, and then bring the bath between her two hands, the small spatula whose shape is as follows:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and split the second bone, and cut into its nail until the moisture that is inside comes out; and press the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to cleanse the woman with fennel seed musk with sesame oil; then make her sneeze and blow her nose for a condition, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child comes.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	If both hands are too weak, it is necessary to reset them gently, little by little; and if they still cannot enter, place the woman on a chair and raise her feet up high; then remove the chair from the ground and have the woman lie down, so she does not try to stand up; and if her hands cannot enter, and the child dies within, cut into the womb with a knife that has been previously placed there, and extract the child, and reset them both equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the birth of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child is born on its feet, it needs to be pushed up; then it is turned little by little until it is even; then press on the feet and extend them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it can jump up to the knees, with the command to press, and make it sneeze from the condition; if it jumps high, God wills it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not happen as we have said, turn it little by little according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it becomes slightly easier.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not work as we have said, take some musk, and oil of roses, and liquid gum, and grind them all in a mortar; then apply this remedy to the woman both inside and outside, leaving it on in warm water down to the ribs; when it has softened, put a collar of myrrh around it and leave it for an hour; then place her on a seat, make her sneeze, press her mouth and nose tightly, and gently press her stomach, as the baby is now ready to be born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	From the emergence of the child on its knees.
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child presents in this manner, he should gently move his hands little by little; then he should rest on his collarbone, and let his feet hang downwards, lying on his side; and gradually move his hands, first pressing them against his stomach, removing the cushions from below, until it is completely open; if the child does not come out, take his feet and mold them, then move his stomach upwards, and finally press your hands; and gently deliver the child little by little; and instruct the woman to strain as long as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the birth of the child who comes with a large hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I know how to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, then make the woman get up and walk; if she cannot walk, lay her down on her bed with her legs bent; then apply the muscle relaxant I mentioned; and if she still does not give birth, have her sit on a chair, and study how to bring back the hand; deliver the child according to its natural position, and make her sneeze, and command her to press as hard as possible.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the birth of the child on its chest, with its hands spread and its face turned away from its mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I want the patient to hold his hand, then tighten it little by little and gently; and when it is even, he should apply a light, muscly compress of herbs and oil, as we have said, then command that it moves little by little; and once you've done this, make him rest it on a hard place, and tell him to press it; and make the patient sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner, for all the rest.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to this manner for all the rest, if the seconding (presumably a type of bandage or treatment) sticks to your finger while evacuating moisture; and if it catches on his face and neck, cut it from the edge so that it is not held, and let the child breathe; then bring the baby back inside, as you have placed him properly, and command the woman to press herself at regular intervals. Then gently pull.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	You know that twins are born many times, and never three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and it often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Twins are considered strange, and do not live long, they have no name; I know that they are multiplied, and their deaths are caused by the joy of those who divide them, who are tied to the womb; and they never emerge as naturally as a single child, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are born badly, if the cure is as we have said, and they are delicate and quickly and gently do what she does, and thus it is moved to safety.
de plusors enfans	from many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	They are never formed in the womb I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more than XV, and they are all formed in the shape of a child according to the measure of his noble wisdom, and it is necessary that the skilled midwife knows all this, for by chance similar things may happen; so do as is proper.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you cure a woman who has lost her child in the womb, as I have said in the previous division, and there is no movement, and you are compelled to use manual force; it is necessary that you know if the woman's health is sound and free from any fear of death; she should be placed on her back, with her legs raised, and her intestines turned inward. The attendant should apply two parts of oil, or she should remain in bed so as not to hinder the descent of the child; then rub the mother's mouth with moist olive oil mixed with althae and fennel seeds and flaxseed, and apply this mixture and the oils to the midwife's hands. Then gently press the uterus, then tie it at a place where the contractions are comfortable for her, and pay attention if the child descends onto her head; if so, fasten or hold it in place with your fingers and place the middle finger between the two thumbs of the left hand, and gently press the whole hand to the desired part until it reaches the empty space. This is the shape of the uterine contraction:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then find another joint, where you need it most, so that the extraction is even; and then stretch it equally in both directions to pull it out, and make sure the joint is sharp for moving, just as this form shows.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains stuck, apply no oil to any of its sides and push it in that direction, then pull the other side; and if nothing comes out, place this joint higher up and do what it takes until it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes forward over the other and it cannot return due to tightness, you should wrap it up in a cloth until it comes out completely; then cut at the joint of the finger or at the knuckle, and do the same for the other hand, and have two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the baby's head is large and stuck in the birth canal, and has a sharp, painful crowning, you should insert the spiny spatula between your fingers, and push the head down and extract the water; or use the instrument called 'almidach', with which the form comes out along with the instruments of this chapter, and thus do the same for a baby with a large natural head; then pull the bones out with pincers, and if the head gets stuck, break it in pieces as much as you can; and if it cannot come out, cut it off in chunks until the moisture in the worst canal is removed; and if it swells up in the abdomen or under the ribs, pierce it through until the moisture runs out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the infection is on the feet, it has a light attraction, and the direction towards the opening of the wound is gentle.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is in the belly or the breast, it is necessary to pull it out with the hand wrapped in a cloth; and make an incision on the belly or the breast, as much as the moisture within it allows; and if another member is dislocated and remains stuck, then turn the patient's hand towards the wound, and pull until it reaches the opening of the wound; then use a knife or something similar, and remove it forcefully; and if the opening of the wound has narrowed due to heat from an abscess, one should not work on it, but rather apply moist and greasy things; and apply poultices, using soft water that softens and moistens.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the dislocated joint is on his side, you can set it even, as we have said for a living child; and if it cannot be reset whole, then pull it piece by piece, leaving nothing of the second one.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, apply what we have said about abscesses that occur in the married state; and if bleeding occurs, it should be treated with immediate restraint, and other remedies should be applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose stomach had been cut open, and another was made on that place, and the other wound was healed.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, there comes a swelling in the cheek, it grows until it opens, and begins to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called upon for treatment, and I thought for a long time, but could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong poultice, and a bone came out, after which every few days another one appeared.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very amazed, because this belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought this was a bone from a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I examined the wound and found a bone in my hand, until the woman was in much better condition; she lay for a long time thus, and then a little bit of warmth left her. I have never heard this chapter mentioned except because, when the masters encounter something strange, they know how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the woman back to her place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	After this comes the form of a press, with which books are bound; and at the turn to the other side, the two halves of the binding.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be more subtle in their tightening, and made of ebony or box; and the opening of the fust (a term for a type of horn) should be wide, with a margin of a palm length and a half; and between these two parts, there should be an appropriate adjustment of the same fust, which should fit tightly in both directions, about halfway through a palm's length or slightly more; and this adjustment is inserted into the opening of the mare (possibly referring to a female animal from which horns are taken) when the two horns are turned.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, resembling pliers; and it should have two adjustments at each end, as you can see, a palm's length long and two fingers wide; and when you open the mare (possibly referring to a female animal again) with all the instrument, place the woman on her back, legs spread, and open the two adjustments together into the mare, holding the base of the instrument between her thighs; then open your hand over the entire instrument, just as you did with the pliers, according to how much you need to open the mare's mouth, until it reaches its desired position.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	The surgical instruments are all well-equipped and varied in appearance; and when the mirror has made them appear even more distinct, the work is done more swiftly, and with greater skill by the craftsmen due to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not disregard the instrument even if you have not yet prepared it, for the need for it is not an excuse for negligence.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine (a tool used during childbirth) is applied, it is important that you instruct the patient to retain her breath, then make her sneeze gently, and hold her hands to her mouth and nose; and if she does so, all is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If it is not possible, take I a pot and make I an opening or cover, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the wound, such as calament, rue, anis, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or any of them, should be cooked or steeped in water on the fire; then place one end of the pot or opening over the mouth of the wound, and hold it there until the vapours enter the wound; then make the patient sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the patient experiences a second complication.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if, after this treatment, the patient still feels pain but not severe, instruct them to moisten their left hand with sesame oil or aloe and then apply it to the affected area. They should hold it there until they feel the pain subside; however, they must gently move their hand slightly to the right and left, and then remove it. This will come and go.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the opening of the wound is narrow, we have said the cure of sneezing and fumigation with herbs; but if it does not respond to these, be careful not to extract it, but he who has a narrow opening in the wound, should tie it to the woman's thigh, then wash it with a four-ingredient ointment; it will heal and come out, but nevertheless, when it opens, a bad smell reaches the stomach and head, and the patient becomes pale.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, it is advisable to use suitable fumigations: none of the ancients have tested fumigation with parsley and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which the woman is cauterized to prevent the flow of blood and swelling, this is it:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is like a glass tube, similar to a candle, and one places the narrow end in nature, and the wide end over the fire; and there are fumes from the coals, and the smoke until it is consumed, and then another is lit.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born whose foundations have not been pierced, but they have a subtle opening: therefore it is necessary for the midwife to pierce this opening with her finger, and not with an acute instrument, and protect the wound so that she does not touch it; then she should cover it with moist cloth in wine and oil, and apply treatment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it does not return, either insert or remove a plug of cloth, and leave it for several days, and when the child wants to go to sleep, it will be dislocated.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And this sudden stopping of bleeding or an abscess should never be left untreated; if the bleeding stops, it is necessary to apply pressure as we have said for a plug of cloth.
de la fistule dou fondement	from the fistula at its base
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that originate from beneath the fundament are called nodations, and they are larger than those that emerge from above the fundament, or in the space between the two parts, if there is a fistula or more; and when this nodation is old, it opens up, and still emits white or subtle discharge, and these fistulas do not heal; and they are known by the presence of drainage or flatulence when the patient evacuates, and sometimes they cause pain.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if they puncture fistulas that reach the bladder, and half of the penis; and they reach the joint of the thigh, and the root of the cow.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus, you recognize the fistula present in the fundament, and it is not present: and it is that you insert your index finger or fundament, and insert a fine needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has curvature, if you insert a thin plunger or a horsehair, as long as you feel the resistance or the hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and it does not come out with perfusion or vomiting, as we have said: know that it does not pierce; be hasty in curing.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is persistent up to the bladder or up to a ureter, if it leaks urine, and cannot be healed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced up to the joint of the thigh, then the veins nearby become swollen; if there is no curvature or pain around, and it remains in that state, then nothing helps, neither medicine nor dressing; and these persistent fistulas have no cure except through hard work and the futile efforts of those who interfere with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the case where it is not persistent and not ancient, there is hope for healing by cauterization, as I have experienced, and the patient lies on their back between your hands; they extend their legs up to their thighs, and their thighs are bent towards their belly. Then apply a thin strip of iron or, if there is curvature, a round one, as long as you know where the fistula is located.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain in the foundation, it is necessary that you press your index finger onto it, and he will feel that the aching has been pierced; whether it reveals itself as satisfaction or pain between your thumb and forefinger, then know that it is persistent; if you do not work with it, it cannot be cured.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One can in any case not be completely cured of these things, but it happens rarely; the aid that is provided consists of applying hot cautery according to the extent of the fistula, as mentioned above, and filling it with hot oil until it reaches the foundation; do this two or three times, until you know that these charred marks have healed, which resemble a bird's feather; then apply moist ointment, and after that, bandage and treat with healing herbs.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is in such a state, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If he cannot be healed in any other way; and if a thread enters and does not pierce all the way to the bone where it is rooted, and there is a thick covering of cloth or something similar between your finger and the thread, and you see a fistula forming after the covering is removed from the heart, then cut through the beginning of the fistula and pull out the thread before the covering, and then cauterize it as it comes to the tip of the thread; and the covering will be freed and healed. Then beware of those false threads that look like a bird's feather, and do not hesitate.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the pain goes away, and the wound is closed between you and the injury, cauterize it with fire or a strong medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For fire cautery brings together two good things: that is to say, the burning of these tissues adjusted, and the drawing out of blood and the drying of moisture; then treat the wound with moist ointments or crushed things, until the bones are bent downward, and make the burnt tissues in the bowels go away; then cure the wound with sudden hot compresses and hard bandages, and they are dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healthy and will not come back.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula appears down to the very foundation, and it is distant from the body, if you press on its root or foundation, and ask it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the pulsation, and between it is the thread or the silk or the char, or it is about to pierce through, if there is no other way of hope and rescue, through one of the three methods: cauterize it as we have said, cut it down to the bone, or if you can gently insert something and cure it as before; but be careful not to cut too deep that you don't remove the covering which holds the foundation, and pain will come from the other side unwillingly; then cure it as we have said. Perhaps it will heal, or you shall remove that covered wound and clean it after it has been cut away from the foundation, either with a needle or another instrument pointed; then sterilize the evil-doing thread in the wound as best you can; and try to restore the wound, and hold back the fistula from the part beyond the foundation. This is a lighter matter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And never are fistulas made in this way: and it is when you press the tent into the fistula, and it is on the side near the foundation of the skin above, then take a tent that is pierced at the top according to this shape.
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And press the thread twisted in two, and push the tent along the entire thread into the fistula as far as the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is persistent at the edge of the foundation within, then extract the thread from that perforation, so you press your other or second foundation; and hold the top of the thread, and assemble both parts together, and tighten them onto each other, and leave it for one or two days; and do not loosen it, until the threads have healed that are between them, and stopped itching; then treat the wound until it is sealed and clean.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If you cannot pierce the fistula, no matter what method you use, it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not appropriate to attempt to treat the patient if the fistula is too deep, and then cure it as we have said, until it is healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form is a sharp, spiky mass from which the fistula is formed, it is very hard and one-sided, and cuts; on the other side, it is not, so that one cannot pierce or attempt to pierce it, as you can see.
des emorroydes	Of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids exist in two ways: either they are inside the anus, resembling grains of resin, with small or large sizes, and oozing blood, or they protrude from the anus and are surrounded by a little or moderate amount of moisture, sometimes containing clear water or blood; they have the color of skin. The treatment for those situated inside the anus is to order the patient to stay in bed until the anus heals completely and the hemorrhoids disappear; if you hurry, using pliers or your fingernail, grasp them at their base, then cut them off. If they cannot be held by the moisture, use a piece of cloth, cotton, or a chamois to extract them, then cut them off and apply some hot powder from cautery; or cauterize them as described in the chapter on cautery, treating other ailments until they heal. If the anus cannot be opened, enema with bitter and sharp solutions should be given to wash out what is inside the anus, so it can be expelled easily. When the patient feels pain and when the thread (of hemorrhoid) protrudes from the anus, the cure is simple; you cut them off using your fingernail or pliers, then treat them as described earlier until they heal, avoiding incisions with a knife.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary, you must administer the stitching in this manner: take twisted thread, and wrap it around a needle, then pull the thread from above and pierce the needle from the other side, and pass both ends of the thread under the needle, and if it is too wide, tighten the forming thread, then tie the thread, and extract the needle, and do thus with all the others, leaving one for draining the excess blood; then place a moist cloth or wax on the base, and put it in place, and instruct the patient to rest; and then leave it until they heal, and when they fall, apply treatments and other remedies until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	The phrase "dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement" translates to "carefully of the parts or
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is a drying up of feces in the intestine, due to constraints of nature, and when the illness is old and no remedy avails.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you scrape the skin with a spatula or your fingernail, so it does not become moistened; then treat it as soon as it becomes dry, in the manner appropriate; and if it cannot dry, repeat the scraping more forcefully than before, until it becomes healthy, and is scratched; then treat it as long as it remains healthy.
dou fremit	Douloureusement" is the correct translation
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ants are a small, hairy creature that moves very quickly; and they never cause pain, and you would think them dead from their trembling, and they spread throughout the body, especially in the hands.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a feather from a goose's wing, or a strong feather from a hawk, and place that feather on the trembling until it covers the entire trembling; then turn your hand over the entire feather until you cover all around the trembling, and set it in place, and remove the trembling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see that it is a feather of steel or iron according to this form, and be subtle from below and draw from above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	I do not feel any pain, so that I can hold still, and must press myself. And if you see, cauterize the tremor, as it is in the chapter of cautery or treatment before it.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of a douche
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never should one use a enema of silver or lead, or molten iron or brass; nor should these small and large instruments be used according to those who employ them.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those, therefore, who are employed in the treatment of children and those who are weak and full of pain, should be small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	He makes a small and wide incision if it is above, binding the abdomen in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and if there is an inflammation or the abdomen is bound, as you see, and the feces are trapped inside, he should have two openings on one side and one on the other. The abdomen can be filled with medicines from a bladder of animal or parchment, with small openings all around, each opening spaced by one finger's width, then thread through these openings a strong thread twisted in an 'X' or along their edges, and gather the abdomen as if it were a goat. When the medicine is inside, tie the bag tightly ahead with a strong thread, then enemaize; this is the shape of a circle.
