Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and apply a warm cloth with oil or goose fat or similar, then bind it gently; then the attendants should massage it with both hands together until it is entirely absorbed, then remove the compress, and raise the patient's legs to the wall, and allow the medicine to take effect as best as possible; if they sleep soundly through the night, it is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you use the clister for a belly cramp, and the medicine quickly takes effect, it returns as soon as it is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoid is at the anus or abscess, it should be treated with as delicate a clamp as for a newborn; and this is the shape of the delicate clamp on which the skin is tightened.
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken of the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments of hands and medicine, according to accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the place where the wound is made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are through the use of stone, and sword or knife, or lance or spear or arrow, or similar things; or they are made according to the laws of the body, such as a wound that breaks through the neck, or head, or side, or belly, or liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and begin with simple head wounds, for the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, be careful if it is due to stone or similar things, and the skin is nevertheless torn and the wound is deep, and you doubt an abscess forming: do this quickly to make the wound healthier from the head itself, especially if there is little blood loss from the wound, and treat it conversely for the affected part; and let the patient avoid wine and rich meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to heal, let his flesh be reduced, and let him not drink wine, nor eat cheese; and apply a poultice of rose oil only, or aromatic wine; and if there is a hot abscess, apply it to the wound while it is still fresh with all its blood, and do not let the air, powder - which I will speak of later - touch it, as long as it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a sword's length or similar in size, and the edges cannot be brought together, then sew them together, as I will describe for wounds of the abdomen, by stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed and deep, but only temporarily affects the skin, then treat it with medicine, replace the bandage with hard leather, and instruct the patient to eat substantial meats, such as tests (liver), cooked wheat, and also poultry, and similar foods.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find putrefaction in the wound or leather that has not reached the bone and destroys everything, then drain it thoroughly; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein from which blood will not stop flowing, and medicines cannot stem the flow, then tie it with a thread, and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is light: it is that you put this powder which sticks so that the fire moves it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The method for the powder is as follows: take one part incense, two parts dragon's blood, and three parts of the living coal, mix the powder finely, apply it to the wound, and tighten it until it spreads well and joins with all its blood; then bind it tightly, and do not loosen it unless it swells, for the medicine is not removed as long as it remains healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never should one use only the coal alone, unless one has incense and neither dragon's blood, but that the fire does not move the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fire has moved the wound, especially if there is no such powder applied; but place some prepared herbs or flour of barley made with water and honey onto it until it boils; then apply other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a bone fracture occurs with the wound and it is small, then extract it with delicate pincers; and I will tell you below about fractures of the skull.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the collar (or neck).
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound appears on the neck and it is simple, with no distinction between it and another from the top, but if there is damage to the nerves of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, then there is no other remedy but to let them heal and put nothing restrictive on them, as that would harm the nerves and cause them to retract; do not apply anything sharp to the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation extends to the brain, which is the highest member. But use medicine according to this method: wash with warm water and mix with rose oil, also wash with warm water other compresses made from various herbs, and moist compresses.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is great, cutting it open wide and binding it, then apply treatment until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and infected, full of pus, pierce them to the bottom or even deeper; and if an artery is cut, and blood flows, leaving it untreated can lead to further complications such as gangrene, so cauterize it properly; and if there's a pinched nerve in the throat or heart, do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural position; then tightly bind it and leave it for no more than a day, applying treatments without delay until it heals; and if the wound has pressed against the bone, break any bones that are stuck together, those that cannot be broken leave as they are, allowing the wound to fester and become lighter and easier to heal; and for fresh wounds, apply the powder I mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones and a fistula in the wound, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a spear or knife, and deep, then consider the disposition of the wound as the patient alone can: knowing thus that the wound is mortal; but if it is not too deep, and still full of blood, do not apply powder in the first hour, nor bind the wound tightly so that the blood does not coagulate and return to the body, and aggravate the patient; but apply a drawing ointment, and change the bandage twice a day; and if you have no ointment, place old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture, and make the patient lie on the wound for three or four days, or even longer; if there is no spasming, nor trembling of the body, no extreme pain, then know that the wound is healing.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	 Cure the wounds with various remedies and others, as long as they are healthy; and if they cannot heal, know that there is a fistula; then treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is shallow or deep on the front, back, or side, treat it accordingly; if it's large, sew it up; and if it's small, use powder; and if it has penetrated into the bone, and there are pieces of bone protruding, dig out the foreign bodies if they are visible; and if they are not visible, let the wound heal on its own, and make the extraction easier. And for other wounds in other parts of the body, judge them as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	disruption of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The disruption of the belly is great and medium and small; from a large wound there will never be any leaking of the intestines or the nerve of the intestines, which causes external insertion; and stitching is more difficult, and never worth less than a small wound than a large one, because we do not apply as much skill to the intestines when they are smaller, so they do not stay in place as well, and for this reason it is better to move a small wound, because we must first bring the intestines back into their proper position. And know that the rupture of the belly occurs in four ways: common stitches occur in the stitching of the belly, and the stitching of other wounds on the body, and other specific stitches are common to other wounds; however, they are more suitable for the stitching of the belly, and I will explain each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and nothing internal is affected, and it is a difficult thing to heal, then it is through one of two methods: either because of the small size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to the injury.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a thin cloth with hot water only slightly, or cook in water with squinant (a type of herb), cipre (another herb), and spique (possibly a spice), and straighten the intestines as soon as the swelling is gone; and never use wine to constrict it, but rather let it be until it is completely unswollen.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if the intestine is filled with water or any other liquid, and the veins are closed, for this lightens the entry of a little thing; and if it cannot enter, then make a small wound with the instrument used to treat hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to move that which cuts, so we do not cut without great need; and this is the instrument to split: it cuts into the vein and does not divert, and see how it looks.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound has enlarged and the intestine is protruding, if you can return it to its natural position in its proper place, do so if you have the ability, for it is beneficial.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it's in the lower part of the belly, you should make the patient lie on his back, and raise his legs higher than his head; and if it's in the lower part of the belly, place the head and buttocks higher than the lower parts, and also ensure that the tear in the belly is in one of the two halves so that the injured part is higher than the other; thus, it is necessary to apply what I say to both large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, you should prepare what is necessary, then take in your hands a clean and soft material to cover the entire wound, and gather the edges together; this is the common method of stitching. You insert one or more needles according to the width of the wound, leaving two spaces at the beginning of the wound, and sew with a strong thread; then pierce both layers of skin with the needle from inside, gathering the edges together, and assemble the two ends of the needle three times. Then take another thread and double it around the needle from both sides, then gather the edges of the wound properly, leaving two spaces, and insert another needle; fasten the thread like you did with the first needle, and continue to do so until the entire wound is secured. The needles should be medium in thickness, neither too fine nor too thick, as fine needles can pierce through the flesh, and very thick ones cannot enter deeply enough. Therefore, they should be medium. Do not pull the needles too far from the flesh and skin, or they will open up the wound before it heals; then cut off the ends of the needles so that they do not disturb the patient during sleep, and place bandages or cloth over the wounds to hold them in place until the wound is healed. This stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because a single needle or two is enough for the second stitch, and you gather together both layers of skin and the two edges of the cut with a needle that has a strong but medium thread; and when you have pierced these all four times together, return the needle to where you began, in the manner one sews clothes. Leave spaces between each stitch about as wide as a finger; this stitching is useful for men, and I once sewed up a wound on a man's belly that had been cut with a knife, and it was over an inch wide, and went deep into his intestines, and the wound was in the middle of his belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine to its proper place after it had been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound healed completely within fifteen days, and he was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And they marveled that he did not die, and this was a miracle; I did not cure him with any treatment, for I was in a place where nothing was found, neither any medicine; and I put clean cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey-water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle, and thread it from the outer part to the inner part; when it has pierced through both entirely, bring the end out at the top where you began stitching, and make it pierce from the inside to the outside again; and the listening to this stitch is that you sew as a tanner does leather, leaving the thread on one side and taking it up on the other until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second way of stitching, which Galen properly calls, is like nothing so much as when two parts are joined together in a natural manner, and one of the ends is applied to the other with great care: insert a needle or a point near by, and pierce only through the outer layer, leaving the inner parts intact; then turn the needle and pierce from the opposite side towards the inside, passing between the two parts; then pierce each one from the opposite side towards the inside, in another pair of parts where the points are on either side; and this is the most effective way of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen refers to this method, and no one testifies to it more effectively than the fact that the stomach must be sewn with two needles, each having thread; one needle should be passed from one side, and the other from the opposite, in a manner similar to those who sew up wounds; and know that when the rupture is within the stomach, the stitching will be more difficult than for other internal wounds.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is the same as for other wounds: and it is that when you pierce the fresh wound to all its blood, and the flesh moves, then reapply the bandage and the dressing; then sprinkle the healing powder over it; and if the flesh moves again, apply any present remedy until the wound bows; and let the thread tighten, and seal with balm and mirra; then treat the wound as for other wounds, until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, apply at once, as soon as it begins to bow, old cotton, and move it twice a day until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you need no other medicine in addition for simple wounds; and if you doubt that the wound does not affect any principal members, it is enough to moisten light linen with warm seasonal oil, or rose oil, and place it around the wound, and under the armpits; and if it feels pain or putridity in waves, and this often happens, then give it enemas of red wine, especially if the putridity reaches the intestines. Puncture inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestinal organ called "young" cannot heal when it is irritated, and this is due to the condition of the veins, and the subtlety of the entire body, and the nearness of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	If the fat (or tissue) jumps out of the wound, reset it back as with the intestine, while it is still fresh; and if it has become old and turned white or black, you must hold the black part still, as there are veins and arteries within; then cut away the tissue between the ligaments, and hang the two parts from the opposite side of the wound until the fat (or tissue) falls out, thereby facilitating its removal.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the rupture of the bowels
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is ruptured and the wound is small, it cannot be restored in any man, as I have seen one nobleman's navel or abdomen pierced by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, it became inflamed and fistulated, and there issued forth excretion and flatulence; I applied remedies according to my ability, and did not cease to try different things until he was healed and his strength returned.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him heal, I doubted that the patient would not suffer pain in his belly; but he felt no pain, only improving in condition and appetite; and none of the experienced physicians said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be treated in this manner: take a large reed, then bring together the edges of the wound, and when the reed has opened the mouth, place it between the two lips so that it draws them together; then cut off the head of the reed, and this will hold so that he cannot open his mouth; then put another reed in the same way as before, until the wound is entirely closed; and then dress the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	This chief is sharp within the intestine, and causes no harm to the patient, and it is possible to sew up the intestine with a thin thread cut from the intestine of an animal, in this way: take the tip of this intestinal thread that is very stripped, and then tie it to the tip of this thin linen thread twisted, then wind the thread into the needle, and sew up the intestine, and rearrange it at the rupture; and this method of stitching is not stronger than according to reason and hope; and if the wound is large and deep, especially when it is in one of the major intestines, no one can heal it except with great subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	whether it is a fistula or wherever it is located.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Every wound or abscess, when it opens, is generally called a "fistula", especially when it is filled with pus and has an opening.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	A fistula, according to the true nature, is hard and white, without pain, just like the quill of a bird; it does not clear easily, sometimes being thin and other times thick; sometimes soft, and other times firm; and it can be due to one of the nine causes: the thickness or hardness of pus or scabs; its malignancy; the presence of hard matter inside and on the lips that prevents the formation of moisture; excessive bowing; corrupted or bad-quality flesh; improper medication; the corruptive nature of pestilence; tardy digestion due to regional properties, leading to delayed healing and flatulence; or the presence of veins or bones. I have already discussed all these causes, their symptoms, and the appropriate medications in the previous division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I make you know the treatment of the fistula which is performed by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	You know that fistulas can occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that affect major veins, arteries, nerves, or organs such as the bladder, intestines, or kidneys, or any of the ribs, or the spine in the back, or any joint in the hands or feet, and if they affect the vital organ of a limb or similar structures.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	All types of fistulas in this manner are difficult to heal and require hard work and knowledge; therefore, if there is a fistula that does not come to the surface as I have described, and you believe in the cure, and you understand it, take a thin blade of iron or steel, if the fistula is straight cut it as desired; but if it is curved, seek a very delicate plucking tool because the pressure from the plucking should follow the curvature; and if the fistula has an opening for the fingers and you cannot reach it properly with plasters, wash it out through one of the openings; for moisture travels quickly from one opening to another and cleanses it. Then cure it as I have told you, and dig out all foreign matter and corrupt flesh, cutting it as deep as desired. When you are certain of the depth and location—whether it is near a joint, nerve, artery, or vein, or any of the places I mentioned—cut it completely through, and wash it with hot medicated water, placing moist bandages over it until the medicine corrodes away all excess matter at the bottom. Then cover it with fresh, healthy bandages, and if it still does not heal, cauterize it as we have said; if the bone is damaged by the fistula, cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not affect the principal members, as we have said, and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, treat it with the king's power until the corruption is completely removed; then take care of the ensuing conditions as well as possible while it is still sound. And if it remains unsound and bows back as before, know that you are not yet safe: expose it and leave it until you reach the bottom, remove all the corruption, then restore it to its place; and if it becomes healthy in this way, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If the corruption is too deep and you cannot do anything about it; if there is no other remedy but to let nature take its course; and if there is a small bone corrupted, which can be extracted with tweezers suitable for this purpose, extract all of them without leaving even one; and if moisture makes things worse and there is no doubt or fear, dry and warm it, and relieve the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in one hour, apply something putrid to the wound, and let it fester until the pus has formed around the bones; then they will become easier for the bones. And if it is a large bone, like that of the leg or thigh, scrape away the pus until the blackness is completely gone, then treat the wound; and if there is a great deal of corruption extending almost to the bone, you must cover and protect it all up to the point of corruption, and then heal it as quickly as possible. And I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take an example from it and use it in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man around thirty years old who had a pain in his leg due to something that came from inside the body, causing matter to accumulate in the leg, and he had a large abscess that would not open; but because of their foolishness, they worked so much on the abscess that it opened, and many corrupt materials came out, becoming a fistula, and there were many ruptures through which all bowels and moisture from the body leaked out. And for two years, many doctors treated him, but none had knowledge in this art, until I was called to see him, and I examined his leg and the medicines used to cure it, and what was corrupt through the ruptures causing great damage to the body; and the young man's skin became red, with a citrine-like color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these openings, and then I searched all the openings, and found that some came against each other from every part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	Then I quickly acted, and cut into one of the openings until I discovered a part of the bone, which was rotten and pierced, and the corruption went as deep as the bone; I knew what appeared to be the rotten bone, and thought there could be no other corruption except that which I had left; and I began to treat the wound with medicines for a long time, but they could not heal it. Then I re-examined it and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, so I treated it and then set it, and bent it back into place; but I could not do this until I had removed a palm-width of the bone, and straightened it to its original state, after which I applied more medicines. It became healthy and healed steadily, and did not want to relapse again except for the weakness due to the patient's condition, who could not bear it, and for the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Because often there is the evacuation of blood, but it was completely healed, and a hard scar was left in its place on the bone, and it had a good disposition and caused no harm or damage at all, neither to flight nor to movement.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this manner: take a rope, and stretch it across the opening of the bone, and command anyone not to move it upwards; and tie another stronger linen rope over the first one, and fasten it to the scar that is now away from the bone, pulling the scar until it is completely detached, exposing the bone where you saw it was broken. And place a piece of charcoal or a table under the bone to protect the exposed part; and it should be treated as much as can be seen and felt to be corrupt, and in this way again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if a bone is corrupted and will not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then expose the entire limb; then apply heat from beneath, and then move the corruption from one part to another until it comes out, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, cut off the corrupt joint and take hold of the bone on either side; and if the corruption is in the connection of two joints, there is no other instrument than to cut off. And if the corruption is in the wrist or ankle, this is a very difficult matter, but you must inquire into that corruption how it opens; and cleanse it in every way you can, as long as the vein or nerve do not resist; and know that there are many instruments for cutting bones, according to their position and appearance, and their size and thinness, and their length and shortness, and their hardness; and therefore, each task requires a tool suitable to its appearance; and know that the work will show you the instrument you need, according to your knowledge of this art and the signs of the illness. Choose the instrument you need according to what is appropriate.
dou feu	Of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The joint dislocates internally or externally; and when you have treated the inflammation with medicine but it does not benefit, it is necessary to cover that limb until the inflammation goes away, so that the patient escapes from death or from the evil, which is greater, of the defect in the limb; and the sign of this is that the limb turns black, as if burned by fire, and then the inflammation spreads throughout the body; therefore hurry to cover it, and if it is caused by the bite of some venomous beasts, such as scorpions, snakes, and similar ones, if the inflammation is at the top of both limbs, treat it immediately and do not give it time to come to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it reaches the hand, cut off the bone at the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, cut through the bone; and if it passes through the bone, it is death, and there is no cure outside of its quantity of virtue; and thus do the same when the corrosion comes to the foot: if it affects the first joint, cut after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, cut through the entire foot; and if it rises in the leg, cut at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to leave the patient to die; and the manner of cutting or binding the member is that you tie it above and below, and stretch one assistant with each cord, and you sever the tissue between the two cords with a wide spatula, until the bone is exposed; then cut or bind it, and place a linen drape on each side so that the linen does not touch the healthy part, and bring about further injury and abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if the flow of blood occurs when you open it, cauterize the wound carefully or apply certain powders to restrain it; then return to your medicine until it is completed, bind the injured member with a suitable ligature, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to this man in all respect: he had a blackening that seemed like a burn from fire, and that ulceration came first on his right big toe, until it discolored the entire toe; and when he saw the ulceration, he covered his foot, and it was healed. And a long time later, the ulceration returned on his left hand, and he came to me, and I placed him on repulsive things after purification of the body, and the ulcerations would not stop; and he begged me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to do that, for I had hope of overcoming the material. And I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, because the strength of the man was weak; and he became completely desperate, returned to his land, covered his hand, and it was healed; and I have heard no other report but this one, if one does otherwise, when necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	No abscess forms in a fatty tissue, and it lingers so long that it causes great bowing of the limb; then it rots and pierces through, causing the bone to move as if a vessel, and the flesh around it becomes weak, just like a delicate cloth, and does not extend to the bone or nerve, and this disease is called "sain" (ulcer), and not "fistule" (abscess); but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone completely, it is called a "fistule". The flesh around it should be cut away entirely, especially when it is delicate, like a cloth. And its corruption should not be left unnoticed.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you believe the skin is infected and the corruption is not completely healed, and the skin is dry and brittle, then cure it with a cleanse: check if the breast is swollen and emits a foul odor, then cleanse it with Egyptian medicine made as follows: take equal parts of salt, oil, lithargyrum (alkali), and place them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and thickens like honey. Then, according to need, mix it with water and honey, and apply it to the breast, constricting the opening; leave it for two hours, then drain it while squeezing; repeat this several times until the breast is cleansed and the infection healed; do not cleanse with water from ashes if this medicine is not available, but instead crush ashes of vine bark and pour water over them, then strain it and use it to cleanse, as long as you know the breast is clean. And if the patient cannot tolerate either the Egyptian medicine or the water from ashes, cleanse him with a mixture of water and honey containing a little lithargyrum; or use honey and mead, allowing the honey to purify and wash, and the wine to aerate the flesh; when you have done this and believe the breast is clean, cleanse it with a substance that produces heat in the body, and make an application of rosin mixed with wine; or use certain other medicines and ointments whose properties have been discussed in the section on ointments. If the opening in the breast is very small, and the catheter cannot enter, widen it slightly with a hot iron, and apply a thin layer of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is widened. And if the wound is too large for the catheter to enter, and the pus is discharging from below, then make the opening higher or lower than where the catheter enters.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bowel is in perfect condition, it does not allow itself to be dilated; and if you cannot cover the opening of the anus as you see fit, arrange it in such a way that the bowel moves to the lowest level possible, for when the bowel is perfectly aligned, it does not allow itself to be dilated, and if you cannot cover the opening of the anus as you see fit, arrange it so that the bowel gently flows downward, leaving no residue from the bowels; and take consolidative medicines to place over the wound, and wrap it with a linen cloth that covers the entire area; then press as hard as possible in the direction of the aperture of the anus, making it wider than before; apply a soothing dressing over another piece of cloth according to the size of the aperture, and place it over the aperture of the anus to lighten the load from the bowels, and do not remove the large cloth outside until after many days. And whoever is over the aperture of the anus often removes it to release the bowel, and you must know what flows from the bowel, whether it be poison or a little or enough or digested or undigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or no, and when your medicine has taken effect in such a way and you see the nature of what grows on the aperture of the anus, then know that the bowels have opened, and bring back health; and then unbind it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you unbind the wound, change to another cloth and renew the dressing.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast becomes bowed and distended after many days, knowing that it will not open.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons appear after a long time, do not despair of health, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are people to whom tardy purifications of wounds are beneficial, and others for whom the opposite is true; and if the breast becomes bowed and distended after many days, knowing that it will not open; and if the breast refuses to open, and remains distant, then apply medicines that are moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as a final ointment, because there is much vitriol, which is the last medicine; take the final ointment and mix it with rose oil, and add equal parts of old wine; then conserve it and use it; and do the same with honey thickened with cooked grain, when final ointments are not available; you can also use myrrh, aloe, and incense, crush them and make a powder over the honey once it has been removed from the fire; then spread it on a cloth and place it over the breast; do not administer any alogues or roots of celestial lily, which is like flour of times and centaurium; use simples or composites; grind them, make a powder, and mix with the honey I have mentioned, and apply. And if the cure prolongs, and this cure does not help, then know that corruption has reached its peak, creating pressure in the bones, or in hard members, or in the ligaments; just as we said before about the treatment of fistulas.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	A nail abscess is a infection that forms under the nail of the hand, or foot, or occasionally in other digits; and when it becomes old and care is not taken, it can lead to a deep abscess, causing pain and discharge until the root of the nail is destroyed, or even the entire nail. It leads to corrosion reaching the bone, producing a putrid odor, and the skin around the digit becomes swollen and red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	If, as we have mentioned in the previous section, you treat it and the treatment is ineffective, then you should remove all debris stuck under the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is sound; and if the nail catches fire among other things, and begins to burn, then you must place the right tool under the burning nail, turn it upwards, and gently cut off the charred part, and apply hot and corrosive medicines to remove all of it; then treat the wound with ointments until it heals.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	If the corruption is in the bone, cut it away and pull it out, for as much as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see both bones corrupted, remove them as mentioned above, then treat it until it heals; and if it is burnt and blistered, and causes great pain, first treat the wound; then cut the nail with a sharp spatumile at an angle across from the charred part below the nail, and be careful that the cutting does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, as the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, apply something soothing.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain from the deep wound causes the hand to ache.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The adjustment that is born in the hands of no one by chance is entirely fleshy, and by chance it has a joint or bone, and never does a fingernail grow, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, where birth is not in any way desired.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	The one that is born in no way in the joint does not move, and the one that is born at the joint of the joint, by chance it moves; the size of the one that is fleshy is very light, in this way: cut it from its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the jointure is difficult to cure: if you keep it covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	As for those who are born or have an injury elsewhere, it is necessary that you first cover the wound thoroughly up to the bone, then cover the bone with a suitable cloth, and then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The deformities that come at any age come either from birth, or from the healing of a wound, or from burns by fire, or similar causes.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If you need to secure this joint, so that it must be repaired according to their natural forms; then place between two damp or oiled cloths, so that they do not stick together; or between two pieces of fine cloth, as long as the limbs are joined, as appropriate.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If dislocation occurs on any of its fingers with the palm, then secure this joint as appropriate.
des vils	Des vils" translates to "of the
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Their veins are thickly wrapped, full of melancholic excess, which comes to many members of the body; and more so in the legs of those who walk, work, and carry, than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary for you to administer purgative neither at once nor immediately after food, but afterward.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure of fire is according to two manners: one is with the use of cups and drawing out the black blood; and the other manner is that you open the vein and draw it completely out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The incision is made according to this manner: first, raise the affected leg with hot water, until the flesh becomes tender, then stretch the leg of the patient downwards from the knee to the ankle; next, cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a broad knife, then squeeze and draw out the black blood in your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the sick person can endure; and then bind it, and command him to keep himself warm with flesh that turns black; and repeat the evacuation and cleansing when the veins are full, and harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Lift the affected leg and if there are many hairs, immerse it in a bath, then raise the leg with hot water until it turns red and the veins swell; and if you have no bath, heat it over a fire, then press the long part of the vein from the top of the knee to the ankle; then open the skin at the point where it touches the vein, until you can feel it; and it appears red and black, and when it enters under the skin, it looks like a white cord. Then turn the leg outward until it is raised from the skin, then press it gently at the next hook, then continue to press in this way every two hooks, then open the skin over the vein as before, then raise the leg, just as you did previously, and press it at another hook; then repeat this process if needed, then raise it and apply a soft cloth dipped in wine and rose oil to the wound until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if you see that it is contracted and twisted and rolled up together, and it is not straight at all, as we have said, then you must cut it crookedly, but do not cover it; treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The way to do it is to bend the eye gently so that it does not cut, only when it reaches the vein; it must be done with great care, because if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but since it is thick, as we have said, this is the form:
de la voinne civile	of the main vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is located in the legs, in warm regions where no herbs or trees grow, and on land where there is no moisture; and sometimes it appears elsewhere than in the legs, which happens due to putrefaction that arises from beneath the skin, just as it comes from within the body winding and twisting.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein appear, it is characterized by a severe inflammation in the leg, then the color changes, and the vein begins to emerge forcefully, just like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.
