When the vein opens, it is necessary to wrap around a piece of cloth from one and a half to two fingers thick, leaving the cloth on the leg, and whenever there is no exit at the surface, you must re-wrap it around the cloth, and do not cover its root until it is completely emerged; for if you cut it, it will return to the flesh, causing an abscess, putrefaction, or other illness. For this reason, it should be treated little by little, and nothing should remain in the body; and sometimes this vein appears when it has been cut from five to ten fingers in length, and after cutting it, a plug or hole remains, and you pierce it all the way through, so that everything comes out; and the substance inside is drained, and medicines are immediately administered to the vein to prevent putrefaction for as long as needed, then treat the abscess as usual.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And never again touch this vein, especially when it opens in the joint of the foot or leg, and there is much bleeding; treat it then as we have said above.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	vers that are born between leather and bone
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "bull disease" in our land because it often affects bulls, and it is a small worm that is born between leather and bone. It spreads throughout the body, moving from one member to another, causing great pain as it eats through the skin until it reaches muscle or other tissues, and then it moves deeper into the body. It is caused by putrefaction of certain humors, just like worms, snakes, lice, and roundworms in the stomach; and its malice is uncertain, for when it spreads throughout the body, it ascends to the head, and sometimes reaches the eye, where it may enter and destroy it. This happens frequently.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it healing and draining, it cannot be done except when the pus is gone: therefore, it is necessary that you lie the limb above and below with a strong, tight bandage, then cut and drain it thoroughly; if the pus is still present in the wound, cauterize it with fire until it heals; and the greater damage it causes, the more oil it will leak, as we have said; and if you see the swelling coming near the oil, tighten the bandage below the sore eye, then cut and drain it; and it is important for the patient to use purification of the body with solvent medicines to remove harmful humors, and bathe in warm water to prevent putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	From the pain that comes from flatulence.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in no particular member, but can move from one member to another; and I have seen this as I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the breast; and after that, I noticed it rising up towards her shoulder, as alive as a piece of silver when it is cut from one place to another; the pain left that area and went to the shoulder, and then, shortly afterwards, spread throughout her body, reaching the other breast; then she told me that she felt it moving around inside her body, as I had seen.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marvelled much at how it moved from one limb to another, for I had never seen this disease in such a way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had noticed that many people experience great pain when moving from one limb to another, but I hadn't understood why, as I observed in women; and I thought it was because women have dry skin, exposed veins, and this constraint appears; and I didn't see the same reason for those who are healthy, with moist skin and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see this disease heal, and the patient feels that pain as we have said, if it appears again from above and below, press firmly until that constrained windiness in the limb is gone; then cauterize the limb; and if you cannot do so yourself, cure it with those who know how to remove windiness, like foul pills, serpentary pills, and others similar.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows vary, according to their appearance and the parts of the body from which they originate.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	Their diversity lies in that they have varying tips—some are large, some small, some serrated, and others smooth; and there are those with curved angles, elongated ones, and those with barbs. They can pierce different parts of the body in two ways: into vital members like the head, body, liver, kidney, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it comes out in any part of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, appears: it is necessary that you fight for the extraction of this arrow, because death comes later with various dispositions; and when this bad sign does not appear, and the arrow is not fully extracted, pull it out, and heal the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the signs of the brain when the arrow comes out and pierces the bone, and if there is swelling on top of the brain, it appears dark and sore and twisted and red alone, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of speech, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps there is no discharge from the nose or ears; and possibly he loses his ability to speak and sing; and there is also a white moist discharge from the wound resembling pus, and it smells bad like rotting meat; and if these signs appear, since you are in charge of treatment, remove the arrow even if it is not completely embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of a shot when it leaves the body or heart is that it is near the left breast and feels as if it were stuck in hard matter, not empty; and sometimes the arrow remains silent like the pulse, there appears black blood, coldness, cold sweat, fainting; therefore, know without doubt that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that never affects the liver is that no foam appears from the wound, the throat swells, the patient's skin changes color, he breathes heavily and loses strength.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow breaks in the deepest layer of flesh, it damages the small bones; it causes great pain and makes the patient gasp for breath, and all the muscles around the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow pierces through the stomach, perhaps something from the undigested meat might fall out.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow pierces through the belly, and there is no healthy passage through the intestines, then there is little hope for treatment or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow pierces the bladder, the urine flows out with force and the patient feels severe pain; know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, as they feel and their pain and pressure in the throat, shoulder, joints, back, knees, feet, and legs, and appear similarly, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you, because you do so.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	There was once a man at my home with an arrow that had pierced his cheek or ear lobe: I attempted to remove it, and pulled from the other side beneath the ear's fat, and he was healed without pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And once, in play, an arrow pierced the fat beneath the skin, but the shaft remained below the paper-like skin, and the arrow was completely extracted, leaving only its tip towards the bone, and it was a large arrow with a turquoise bow, without causing any harm to the ear; the wound healed, and no ill accidents came of it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And take an arrow from the throat of a Christian, which was an arrow with ears [a peculiar description for an arrowhead]; I cut off the barbs, and drew it out as much as I could, and healed the Christian.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I pulled out an arrow that was stuck in a man's body, which had pierced his gut, and thought he would die; but after thirty days, he showed no change in condition; so I cut the arrow at its base, wrapped it, and drew it out, without any bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man with an arrow stuck in his back or chest, and the wound is deep; and the arrow remains inside him, and he shows no change in his natural condition, and finds no harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And look at another man, to whom an arrow fell into his face and the wound became deep; he remained thus without suffering great pain; and many others similar.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I extracted an arrow from the body of a prince, the king, which had become lodged in his neck and was slightly inclined to the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded, and I was called for treatment after three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I gently probed it, and I felt nothing; however, there was a sensation of pressure and pain behind his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow I placed a soothing plaster on the shoulder because the muscles were not tense; and I noticed the arrowhead.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the plaster firmly and then dressed the wound, allowing the patient to rest for a long time, until they no longer felt the arrow inside their body; and it came out on its own.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a strong corrosive medicine to the wound for a long time until it opened up, and I tested it, feeling the tip of the arrow still embedded in the flesh; then I adjusted the opening of the wound with that same medicine until the head of the arrow became visible; and after four months, the wound had healed so much that I used pliers to pull out the remaining parts, moving them from side to side, but I couldn't remove it; then I continued to try subtle and clever devices until, in the final section of this chapter, I describe how I finally removed it by pulling and cleaning the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And they believe most highly that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I nevertheless restored it, and the wound healed, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have also told you about the quality of extracting certain arrows, so that you pay attention to what I say, as books cannot contain everything; but wise masters compare well very small and present things, true new works, and new instruments, for the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come out of members except in two ways: either through the vein where they enter, or from another part; and when they exit from one side, it is because they have entered into their flesh, and they will never come out again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out now, let it stay until the swelling around it subsides, and make the opening larger; and if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it for several days, and move it each day, and then it will come out, piercing through all the tissue inside as the swelling around the joint is enlarged.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in a bone at its base and reaches up to one of the cavities in the brain, and none of the remedies I mentioned help the patient: do not pull it out, but let it stay until the swelling subsides each day, for if the arrow reaches too far, death will follow.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not embedded in the bone alone, and does not heal sufficiently, and does not leave the patient without a bad outcome for several days with skill to draw it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot come out, then administer heat around it, as I have told you; then heal the joint while it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is returned into the flesh of the body so that it cannot be seen, even after trying everything; and if you feel it, then use any suitable instrument; and if you cannot due to the tightness of the wound or the depth of the arrow, or there are no bones, muscles, or nerves nearby, then leave it until the wound is severe; and pull the arrow if you can, and if it has roots by which it holds onto something, then cut out the portion that is embedded in the body from both sides as much as you can, and then break or bend the arrowheads until you are able to pull it out.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, leave it until the swelling around it subsides, then treat it, for extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	If the signs of blood poisoning appear to you, apply what we have said in that chapter about treatment; and be careful with incision near nerves and veins, and use every device you can to extract the arrow safely, either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the position it was in when the arrow entered, for this is the greatest aid, and if you cannot, put him in a position that the symptoms indicate.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another direction, where it opens something within, causing the skin to swell in that place as one can see or feel: then cut there, until the pincers can grasp it, and then pull it out: if it jumps out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	If it is stuck in the bone, turn your hand round, until it enters the bone, widening it, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it for now and then try to extract it again until it comes out; and if there is still an arrowhead in the wound, let it stay, and then use a tool with a sharp point, so that the arrowhead enters the opening of the tool; then pull it out, and if the arrow is removed from the wound, use the tool to push the opening inward, easing the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if an arrow is embedded, it is necessary that you remove all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, and then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow has pierced the body, whether in the belly, bladder, or side, and it is accessible, and you can remove it, then do so; beware of damaging the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and subsequently dress the wound, as required, and treat it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The instrument used to extract arrows resembles a bird's beak, and here is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways to do this: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape pointing downward is like the quill of a bird, to drive the tip of the arrow, as follows:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of pincers for driving and gripping, as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are 31 veins from which one can draw blood, of which there are 16 main ones: two that run behind the ears, called "dubbed herbs"; and the two arteries visible in the temples; and the two veins in each arm, called "aspirations"; and the vein running across the forehead; and the vein at the crown of the head, near the eyes; and the two glands on the collarbone; and the two veins located above the lips, which are called "augerich"; and two veins below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The common veins from which one draws blood are five in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, located on the inner side of the left arm, and the common people call it "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "fast", composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and the common people call it "vein of the body"; and the basilic is on the right side, and the common people call it "vein of the belly", located above the fascia, and it is the one from which they draw blood that clearly opens up on the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the cure is the vein that lies between the little finger and the ring finger, and if it rains; and in the leg there are three veins: one below the ribcage on the left side, and the second is at the ankle on the right side; and the third vein, called 'nasse', is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg, there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The cleansing of the veins behind the ears aids in the treatment of old catarrh and migraine; and the quality of the healer, as I have said, is that you raise the patient's head and rub the affected area with a rough cloth; then tie the patient's collar tightly around their neck until the two veins behind the ears are visibly dilated depending from the head. Hold them thus, and where you feel pulsation below your right hand, take care; then take the lance, and insert it beneath the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand along the entire vein upstream, and cut and the skin and flesh and vein well in two, straight through, and draw out the blood until you see; then tie and dress it, while it is still healthy; and I have already spoken of incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	He heals the two arteries that are in the temples, as if they were an old and severe migraine, and a sore, accustomed to weeping, and at the source of the hot tears; and the quality of the healer is such as I say: and it is that the patient pulls his neck, until the two vessels open wide; and he feels the pulse beneath the index of his right hand, and then signs with the needle below; then gently presses the heart on top of the artery on his right side, and draws the needle below, and gently opens the vein at the top, and the clot, as you did for the other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need; then release the patient, and place your right hand on the vein for an hour, then put cotton; and then form a bandage and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of their healing and extraction, as mentioned at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The surgeon of the vein on the forehead is as valuable as the surgeon of the skull for facial diseases old and new, and for migraine and redness; and its quality is such that the patient pulls his neck by twisting, until the vein appears. Then take the instrument called "denter," which has this form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the tip on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, allowing the blood to flow out according to the amount you see; then loosen the patient's neck, and tie the vein as long as it remains healthy, never opening a wide wound.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, one must not let the flames be too intense; and do not burn from across, for the bone is close, and by chance may break the flame when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The health of the two veins located in the arms is beneficial for many things: it helps with itching, redness, swelling, and facial diseases; and its quality is such that the patient's skin remains taut without any distortion, as before. Then, the treatment should be such that the flame is neither too thin nor too thick, for there is no middle ground.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, they may break; then draw out the blood, as much as needed, and then bind it with cloth, and tie it securely.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The health of the vein near the nose is valuable for colds, sudden fever, and facial ailments such as migraines and redness that appear on the face, especially when it is old. The quality of the health is such that the patient tightens their jaw, strains their nostril with their left hand, and inserts the subtle flame longwise between the two nostrils, since the vein does not open well enough, and the blood will begin to flow. Do not dig too deep, and draw out blood as needed, then bind it for a night, for it is quickly restored; this is the form of the flame.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The holy water of the two eyes is helpful for narrowing the eyelid, and at the beginning of inflammation, and for many diseases, and ulceration, and corrosion, and herpes, and swellings; and the quality of the water is such that the patient pulls his eyelid from both sides, as we have said; and the master should be on top of the head of the ill person, and the sick person sits in a certain place, then clean the vein with long-drawn blood slightly, then treat with warm blood as necessary; then repeat the same thing in the other vein, then loosen the bandage, and tighten the veins moderately so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, until the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the cleansing of the veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The cleansing of the veins above the lips helps to heal the mouth, and the corruption of gums, and cracks in the lips, and pain and swelling around it.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the cleansing involves having the patient sit before you, restricting their collar as I have said; then turn the lip and examine the veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, which can be recognized by their black color and small surrounding veins: therefore cut both, and if you do not know them or are in doubt, cut the thicker ones from each side, and do the same with the two veins above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	From the health of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The health of the veins beneath the tongue is of great importance after treating the health of the head, and it applies to the constriction of the throat, and diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the healing is such that the patient should bite between their fingers in the light of the sun, soften the tongue, and examine beneath each side for a dark vein: then both are healthy, but do not press too hard, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the body, commonly healed in two ways: either by pressing with a hot flame, or with an olive-sized, thin tool called an "anesil", and they are wide or thin depending on the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame burns intensely if it is very renowned, and it is wide as you can see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it requires skill to open veins with thick blood that is clearly visible, and which contain great blood and pus; and this is the form of the olive-colored flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtly pointed, and is for healing the fine veins, where there is subtle citrus-colored blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The healing of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, is very helpful for illnesses that are below the throat, and the collarbone, and the chest, and the belly; and it is important for the healer to heal gently and wash the artery below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it affects the artery, and blood loss occurs, if it is necessary to stop it, as I have said; and the flame should not be gripping but cutting like a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the vein does not open clearly, it is necessary that you extract it and choose another one; or if you wish to take any part of it, do so in the vein between the arm and the shoulder: it opens clearly; and cut it with a knife, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you come to know the place of the vein, it is necessary that you extract the arm, touching the vein until you feel the pulse; then mark the place with a sign and bind the arm, and cut the vein with a knife, cutting gently; and be careful not to injure the artery when you see it dilated, for it is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it gushing out from above like the urine of a child, and the wound is red and tender, know that this is an artery: then hurry, place your finger over it for a long time, then remove your finger when the bleeding has stopped, which often happens; let the arm be still and do not move the patient; be afraid, and do not move it until it heals.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the wound does not stop bleeding and it becomes necessary to open an artery, since the pressure is great, and the wound remains open, then press the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a piece of fig bark, and cut it, and take one half of it and bind it tightly to the other side; if it stays unstained, that is good. If not, cure it as we have said, with powders that stain blood; the staining is not too grievous in many dispositions due to the small size of the wound, and the power of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The wound healing is more effective if it stains blood from the top and from inside, because it is composed of both basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and the healer should wash himself for the nerve that is inside, and if he does not do it properly, and touches the nerve, it swells and the healing is affected, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any person due to its subtlety, then you must use an antiseptic instrument first, and avoid touching the nerve.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if the vein is between the two bones, cut it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The treatment for headaches that originate from the head is to draw blood from the neck, which helps the limbs; and it is better to use olive or myrtle fire because it is the safest of all veins, as it does not affect any nerves or arteries.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is better to choose the lightest vein, and do not be concerned if it hurts the first time, just try again; and sometimes, the veins may swell up in some people when they are cut for the first time, but this should not cause any harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that it should only be done to preserve health and prevent future illnesses; and blood should be let in one of the three veins: these are the cervical, femoral, and basilic veins. One should bloodlet at the beginning of a meal, and in autumn and winter after meals when the signs of saturation appear; and one should bloodlet on the first day or third day, after two or three hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	Bloodletting to treat illnesses has no set time, but should be done as needed each day or according to diet, at any hour and in all seasons; and it is not appropriate to bloodlet children under 12 years old, nor pregnant women after the first three months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	One should not treat the old who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone wishes to be cured, in any way whatsoever, it is necessary for him to cleanse the bowels with a light enema, if he has a great deal of feces retained, so that the veins do not draw out from the intestines superfluous and harmful toxins to the principal limbs; nor should one cure oneself who is too salt with meats, or drunk, as long as it persists, or a hydroptic; and wash after colic, vomiting, intestinal cramp, frequent urination, much sexual activity, hard labor, staying up late and fasting, and everything that weakens or harms the body, whether by weapon or illness; then subtilely remove humors, if they are too abundant, through foods and drinks and medicines, if you have them at hand; then enter the bath, if nothing prevents it, to sublimate the blood, and cure the vein from below in the third hour, as we have said; and guard yourself that day against work, exertion, luxury, and similar things; and be calm and cheerful, and let the cure be better than that of others, and rub the arm twice or three times, then gently press the ligament above, because when it is too tight, he cannot correct it without hurting himself; and then rub it with his hands until the veins become swollen and warm. Then moisten the wound with a little old oil, and place his left-hand finger under the vein opposite where he wishes to be cured, so that the vein does not go away and injure itself.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flow as if they were strings in the body of a sick person, and if they are of such kind that they are filled with windiness, when one applies heat, the blood retreats from the flame, and the vein cannot be opened, thus becoming one of these cases; and if the vein is opened, the wound is too narrow, so it is necessary for the healers to be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; but if not, it begins again from the previous place or with greater difficulty, as the limbs are not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the joint is swollen and the patient fears, he should let it be for one or two days, and do not bind the arm: perhaps an abscess will form. Do not enter the bath, then recommence the wound care if it pleases him; and if the puncture is small, pierce it gently and you will doubt that it does not exude as much blood as you see, so proud of that very puncture to all the flame straight; and work a little slowly, otherwise the joint will swell, for this happens often when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros. Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess occurs, which happens often, especially when the opening of the vein is small and you are not healthy to do it, then act quickly, and place a moistened sponge in water and a little hot salt on it, and hold it for an hour; after the blood drains from the vein, you should do this, and if it stays on the wound for several days without turning black or green, it will not harm him; and if you see, apply aloe or myrrh mixed with calament juice, a plaster, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often an abscess and swelling appears at the wound of the basil (a type of surgical incision): so place your hand on it, and if you feel the flesh is soft under the pressure of your hand, then this is a bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid putting anything on it that we have said, for perhaps it could cut without an artery; but make a dry plaster to harden the joint, then apply another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each case of pain according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the pain.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the pain is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it swollen, leave it until it becomes smaller; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for one who is patient and strong, and has the skill to extract blood, to make a wider wound, and have broader flames; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and treat him more gently and often, and one should heal him by cutting across, not by pricking; and this way of healing is safe from blood loss and nerve damage, and it moves faster than long-term healing.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body requires healing, it is necessary to apply moist heat from the juice of pomegranates; if he is overheated, he should be treated with bloodletting three or four times. Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints at the sight of blood, after a great flow of blood, it is necessary that he drink a brew of char and subtle-scented syrup, and use other things as we have mentioned in the division or chapter on syncope for the evacuation of veins.

And if he wishes to raise his arm and heal it better at another time, when he is weakened by much blood, he should clean it gently and gradually, according to the amount of its strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to raise his arm after the first cleaning, and there is a strong crust, he should clean it seven hours after the first cleaning, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if he wishes to get better from another angle, then he must heal himself on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood in the body that has been heated, causing fever; if it is necessary to extract a large quantity, and widen the wound until it takes the shape of a palm, then after you have done all things according to health, and placed your hand on his pulse when he is healthy, so that death does not come in place of healing, and this happens often when healing is neglected; and it is not right when you see the arm loosen, and cause blood to flow again, and the wound close, pressing strongly; nor if he is curved, should he stretch the arm forcefully, for that would be harmful; but leave it until it heals a second time. Or you can apply a pointed flame to the tip of the flame, until the blood that has congealed at the vein opening leaves, and put a little string soaked in water on it, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and do not squeeze it until the abscess is healed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it becomes necessary to drain blood again from the abscess a second time, either in the same place or in another vein or arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is healthier than the one in the neck because it is composed differently.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method for vein extraction is as follows: The patient should hold his hand in hot water until the veins are red, then tie it moderately so that the vein appears well, and now extract through it, not too wide or too long; the punctures should be large, and the sainie (vein) should be extracted close to the joint of the hand, and if it cannot come out, return the hand to hot water and let the blood flow in the water until you have enough; and if this is done, do not pull the hand back into hot water again, because more heat is applied than necessary. The vein extraction from this vein is safer than from any other, as there are no arteries or nerves nearby.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The salve for the salvation of the hand, if applied with due skill, is effective against all diseases of the flesh: stretch the hand and immerse it in hot water until the vein is filled; then twist the wound and press from all sides, without causing any pain; do not apply too forcefully, as the nerve ends are entirely exposed, and then reimmerse the hand in hot water so that if any part of the salve remains in the wound, it can come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as well as your skill allows, apply oil and silk to seal the wound tightly, and do this for each person.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The healthy person on the left hand side is beneficial for the illness of the mouse, and does everything just as I have told you towards the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The health of the soul is beneficial for all diseases that affect the body, such as diseases of the marriage (reproductive organs), retention of flowers (perhaps referring to a type of inflammation or infection), diseases of the kidneys, and old legs and similar ailments.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of his soul is such that the patient finds rest in hot water, rubbing the vein until it bursts, and binding it above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and extends much towards the toes; healthy then, or a wider wound, or at the ankle, whatever moves him most.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you apply it to the foot, be careful not to harm the tendons that are beneath, and clean it as if you were stitching; and the flame should be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	If the bone cannot come out, place the foot in water and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if you clean it the first time, repeat the process a little above, because the tendons are stiff; do not doubt the nerve, as we said, and do the same thing for the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein's lion is at the ankle's heat, and its health corresponds to the pain of the back, when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its health is such that the patient feels pain in the bath and needs to stretch it three times around the ankle, otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, the health is in all ways as you wish, and flowing; and it should be moved slowly, because the lion (vein) is intact, and it is greatly relieved by manual manipulation.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you cannot open it, let no blood flow from the vein that is opened on the back of the foot towards the little toe, and be careful not to tighten the bandages; and make sure the blood flows as well as you can, then loosen the ligature, place cotton on it, and tighten it; now the health (vein) is cured.
des sainies de ventouse	From the suction of the ventose.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses are made of horns, or iron, or glass; and suction is performed in two manners: either by pricking and attracting blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction, performed without pricking, is done in two ways: either it is completely hot, or without heat; and the suction performed by pricking and extracting blood is done in twelve parts of the body, with some on the top of the head; others between the collarbone; others on both sides of the collarbone; another one under the chin; another on each shoulder; another on the knees; and others on both legs; and others on both ankles; and the suction of the veins should not involve blood, except from small veins scattered throughout the flesh, and for this reason it does not weaken anyone, as is done with vein punctures; and it should not be performed gently, nor completely hot or without heat, in any disease caused by overfullness, until all parts of the body are emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of disease or habit it seems to be necessary to vomit, we should allow it each hour at the beginning and end of the month, and in every season; for there are such as, when they have need to vomit, have a heavy head; and some who suffer from fullness and redness in their face, head, neck, and arms; and such as find a drop of blood in their mouth, have their tongue swollen, and bleed; and those who dream, see blood, feel pain, and suffer similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we observe these signs, and especially in the middle of the month, we order vomiting after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The healer of the muscle should aid in the separation of the joints with a gentle touch...  it is not advisable to do so after evacuating all bodily humours; and this procedure is done by the doctor of the head, and it is not appropriate for those with a cold complexion or scrofula, as it causes them great harm; and for that reason, the elderly or those with cold headaches should avoid it.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who heals it often becomes obstructed, and for that reason, a cup should be placed slightly lower down out of doubt about the obstruction.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The windward position over the collarbone is contrary to the healing of the head and basil (possibly referring to the base of the skull); for that reason, it causes tightness in the chest, division of the duct of the penis, constipation, and other ailments; and it should be applied gently, as if it presses too hard, it can cause obstruction or pain in the stomach and body.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The puffiness of the chest with a pain in the head, eyes and temples, strangulation, and pain in the roots of the teeth, is in the location of the blood flow from the basilic vein; and it is necessary that you command the patient to extend his hand when placing it, not to cut the artery, and let no bleeding occur.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The puffiness under the chin indicates a mouth disease, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases in the mouth; it is related to the blood flow from the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The puffiness of the shoulders indicates a disease that arises from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventilation of cuts is as valuable as three veins in the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the healthy one not to press too hard, for the tissue is devoid of fat, and knows how to sever and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The ventose (suction cup) on the rump is as valuable as a hemorrhoid from the anus, and helps with internal ailments. It should be large and made of iron, so that it can effectively extract; but if it is too delicate, it may break and cause great injury.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The ventoses on the legs grip tightly as they draw blood from throughout the body, and are as valuable as chronic pains in the joints, and in the bladder, and unblock them; and they are located on the two knees and two ankles, but they weaken the body after prolonged use and cause numbness in various places.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying a cupping glass is as follows: you apply it at first while it is empty and suck gently, then press it firmly and move it equally, without ceasing until you see the red and inflamed skin appear, opening the veins' redness; then release it, and reapply the cups, taking care in the placement of the glasses, for there are those with thick skin and others with thin skin: it is enough to make one single pass, and it is necessary to make wide incisions and quite deep; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the veins are thick, it is necessary to pierce twice: first to open the thick vein path of the blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the pain is very sharp, it is necessary to strike the third time; and when we want to draw out blood little by little, we are content with only one strike.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, let us strike often; and if the pain is sharp, make each blow count, so that the veins burst immediately; this is suitable for those with thick skin and hard flesh, and who have scaly pores. In such cases, apply oil to the suction cups: either stimulating oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil from pumpkin seeds; and if it is in winter, use oil of watercress, or daisies, or chamomile, or any similar herb.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take amber oil, or balsam, or donkey oil, and similar substances.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if anyone has a tendency towards a hot and swollen joint, it is not appropriate to apply oil, but instead, after purging with rosewater, cold water, water of morelle, water of cucumber, or porcelain water, or similar, one should wash it.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those with much moisture should raise themselves up with myrrh water, sumac water, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have great excesses should rise from old wine, or holy water, or decoction of nettle or chamomile, or other similar things; and it is not advisable to use a vacuum pump before the bath or after the bath, but an hour or two later; and one should not sleep after vacuuming, and it is necessary that he bathe, as required for vacuuming and when vacuumed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And be wary of those who have a temper (coleric), and those who are too hot and inflamed; it is necessary that they apply cold things, such as pomegranates, endives, lettuce, and similar things; and eat little, and chestnut food, and moist meats.
