Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion should take syrup of honey and fragrant wine, between old and new, and eat little, and eat acorns and small birds and pigeons; and on the day that he opens his pores, he must drink more than he eats; and it is fitting to give any man at times triacle or mace before or after opening the pores, to strengthen the principal members; but it is a subtlety without which those who are hot should not drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are applied without causing harm are those placed on the liver, and the spleen, and gout, and the belly and bowels and joints and the spine, for these members do not endure injury easily, and they are only done so to draw blood from one member to another, as we place them on the mammary glands when nursing; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we apply suction cups to the belly and bowels to reduce the member; and it removes pain, when there is congestion or a stone, as it may by its attractive virtue draw away the congestion, or abandon the stone from its place; and thus it does when placed on the liver and spleen when there is retained windiness, and these suction cups are left empty to suck only; and they are never at once hot and cold, nor filled with warm water or water in which suitable herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cup (ventose) applied with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it should have two-and-a-half palm widths in diameter, and on one side there is a small hole, as if to push an needle, and it should be made of metal, soft enough not to hurt the patient when placed on the body; and at its center, there is a crossbar of metal, either iron or steel, to hold a cloth for better grip, and their sizes vary according to the illness and age of those who use them; for the cups for children are different from those for adults, and smaller for the thin than for the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus one should place this suction cup over the member: take the wax or linen cloth and put it through the hole in the suction cup, so that the clarity is at the bottom of the suction cup that it does not burn the patient; and then place it over the member, and your fingers should be on the opening we mentioned, so that when you want, the vapor goes out, and remove the suction cup; and take up the linen cloth as before, and repeat often, if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the case of the suction cup used to treat pleurisy, a condition characterized by sharp pain, it has no opening or hole, and it is only effective when it is filled with water. It should be placed over the affected member only when it is empty; and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without wounds that are amenable to poultices except in members where it is impossible to apply them due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar areas; and when they are bare of hair, like the skin of a dog or cat, or other parts; and the condition of the wound, if you find wounds that are in clear, sweet water without putrefaction, take them; and place them in clean water for as long as they remain firm, and have nothing within their bellies; then clean with vein and poultice, and rub the member until it turns red, and apply the poultices; and when they become sore and chafed, if it is a part where a poultice can be applied, apply one, for this is much better.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If the lion is not calm, raise it from its resting place and then water it well, and hope; if the joints are still sore after the body has healed, moisten a linen cloth in cold water and place it upon them until they are relaxed; if the sores multiply, apply vitriol or gall, or similar substances, until they are healed; or you can put half-peel fava beans on the lion, leaving them until they adhere to the wound, which will now heal. If you need more, take other lions.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the lions refuse to be caught, rub the wound with fresh blood, or insert an needle into the sore until it bleeds, and then apply them; and soon as they smell the blood, they will stick; and when you see that they are chewing, sprinkle a little aloes and cut silk or ash powder on top, and they will stop.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	We begin the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it restores fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear reader, that the fools' gaze deviates from this chapter, for they have never seen or read it in any ancient books. For this reason, the science is strange in our land, because I never found a good one; and I know nothing of it except through the knowledge of ancient books, on which I have studied so much that I have mastered the science, and through experience and the custom of my life. And I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and I have abridged it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments used, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we explain in this prologue of this book the principles of speech and the chapters where the wise men apply their understanding, stopping on truth, so that those who are tested know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	When a fracture, dislocation, twist or sprain occurs, it is necessary to hurry and treat the patient on both sides, if nothing helps, such as weakness of the body, sickness, or old age; or if he has a high fever, or it is too cold, and he consumes cold things like ice, and avoids wine, does not eat any greasy food, and does not fill himself too much with meat that fills the veins with blood, until you have no doubt about the heat of an abscess or the swelling of tissue in the member; then the patient returns to his former state as if he had never been ill.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that we ease the patient of the flesh that causes great swelling, or has a thick consistency, like cooked flour in water, and laughter, and tears, and pressure, and bloating, and weakness, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For great swelling returns repeatedly, and the fracture does not heal as quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the bones of the very old and frail cannot be well healed or fused according to their nature due to the stiffness of the members, nor those that are too tender, like the bones of young children; but do not worry, hold fast to the broken bone with strong grips that join the member together as it was before, as long as it still has strength; and feed it with substantial foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, and in this chapter, I will tell you all manners of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to the bone, and another when sharpening, like the edge of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, then the fracture is at every small fissure.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each condition has its own mechanism and specific means of restoration, according to the memory that arises in the place where it is; and the fracture of a bone is recognized because the limb is twisted, and it opens well from pressure, and sounds when pressed with the hand; and when there is no distortion or pain upon touch by the patient, there is no fracture; but it can have distortions, or splits, or small fractures.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You should not move it with the hand, but apply remedies that will be mentioned later, and then gently tighten it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture that goes up in the air, where the two parts are separated, it is necessary to bring them together equally, so that the abscesses follow one after another; and if hot abscesses come, you should leave it for a day or two until the abscesses subside; then place it equally as gently and carefully as possible, and know that the restoration of such a fracture is lighter than the restoration of those where pieces are missing; then tighten it, as will be mentioned later.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if a bone is broken into pieces, if it is fractured from two parts, whether it's the hand or foot, or one of the smaller members, or two tendons, or a tendon and your hand; place the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are aligned, rearrange by all means the additions to their original positions until you can, and be careful not to cause the patient any injury or pain through your work; adjust both joints of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And if you feel well in your hand and it seems to be correctly aligned, but not tightly enough: treat it neatly, without excessive strain, do not press as those who, through their work, cause heat and contraction in the member, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is completely numb, be very careful not to move it, neither awake nor asleep, nor in any other way; and be sure that the limb is so secured that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels no pain, it is only completely numb, and you must be sure to put it in a position where it feels no pain; and be careful that it is placed correctly, so as not to develop any deformity as it heals; and the quality of the damaged member will depend on what I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	You should know that the damaged member can be different in size and shape, and in its form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Because it has small members, as bras and legs and such: it is necessary to envelop them in soft and fine linen; and those that are large, like the thigh or leg: it is necessary to wrap them with a wide and firm ligature, for the wide ligatures embrace the entire large member and tighten it equally from all sides so that there is no movement; then apply light tourniquets, three times or four according to the member, and tighten your hand slightly on the entire ligature, then go above the break and tighten less, so that the break moves away a little; and soften the ligature little by little, as much as you press into the healthy part of the limb, then take another ligature and tie around the broken part again; then return to the under-part of the break and tighten moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first chapter above; then place between the firm linen ligatures soft cloth or bandages, until they are all even, then bind everything with a broad bandage, and then place your well-made staples on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is an inflammation or abscess, apply a hot compress to it, which reduces the swelling, and leave it for several days; then strain your eyes, and make them half the width of a wide cane sharp, or of wood used to make chisels, or of palm leaves, according to this figure.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the thread placed on the break be slightly thicker and wider than the others; and just as long as appropriate for the size or length of the limb; then tighten the thread on the eyes just as you did in the first layer, and tie a thin thread on top, as in the first layer on the fracture; it should be tighter at the end, but less so afterwards; and the thread should be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft flax; because if the thread is thick, just like people who make their bindings from twisted flax strings do, it's a great error, because the binding cannot be even if it's too delicate, and it is not appropriate for there to be less space between each eye.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is angry because of the pressure from the stars after dislocating their joints, he should place soft cloth or other padding over them so that they are not hurt.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture and the vessels are broken, I will describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to straighten all the broken stars on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not appropriate to apply stars too soon, but after 5 or 7 days, or according to your judgment regarding the healing of the hot apotheme; and here you see the ancient method of applying plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists: take flour that clings to the walls of the mill, mix it with enough egg, and make this paste, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it. This is the common method for applying a plaster that restores fractures in many positions, especially for women and small children, as it is neither too hard nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way to make a plaster that restores fracture and dislocation and torsion: take wolfsbane and ladanum and frankincense and myrrh and gum arabic and mugwort, each in equal parts; add mirra and aloe, each in five parts; and ales (a type of resin), nine parts. Mix them into a powder and blend with egg albumen. If the patient's body heat is high, use this plaster, as it is of good composition and restores broken bones effectively and benefits many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another plaster for torsion: take mugwort and wormwood, each in ten parts; mirra and aloe, each in seven parts; acacia in six parts; and Armenian bole, ten parts. Grind them well and mix with vinegar or egg albumen, then apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of setting joints and realigning bones in their sockets, soothing the pain that arises, and using the saw to cut the bone, and the fracture: take a fresh new cloth, and soak it in hot ash and oil, and place it on the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Cysts cannot be restored, but they are good for soothing hot abscesses, and for carefully removing pains from the bones.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of setting broken bones: take dried fig leaves and terrestrial pavot (opium poppy) leaves, crush them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of bandaging to restore broken bone, and to lessen the pain of healing.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of chamomile, violet flowers, each in equal parts; grind them and mix with wine, and apply to the affected members, which should be heated first. Also mix with fresh coriander water or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another stronger method of bandaging when a hard abscess forms to restore the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take the roots of chamomile, flaxseed, balm, melilot, and fennel, each in equal parts; grind them and mix with salty water, or sweet water, or wine according to the heat of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates writes in his book that to restore a broken limb, one should use a plaster made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and it should be between two extremities, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen suggests that one should apply dry and slightly heated substances to the broken limb to restore it, such as mirror, aloe, incense, and similar things, as we have mentioned.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of plastering that is effective for injury and pain: take mugath (mistletoe) and chevolz (hair from a human's head), or feathers from an owl, and wool, and cut them to equal lengths, then grind them into a paste and use it as a plaster.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then dislocate it a little later, and be careful that the patient does not feel any pain, and that the bone has not moved from its place; if it dislocates by itself, and there is no pain, or the bone has not shifted, then quickly dislocate it and remove the splint immediately; take a light bandage, and a moist sponge, and dip it in water, and elevate the limb until the itching stops, and the pain is soothed; then rest the member for an hour, and place a dry cloth, moistened with water or rose oil, and bind it with a nut, as long as you are certain of the hot abscess; and relieve the inflammation of the affected member, and let the pain go away, then continue with the delicate process, and use a little splint, and not so tightly as before; gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is red, swollen, painful, and full of pus, and you need to apply plaster and bindings, then repeat it as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if the limb shows no improvement after what we have said, do not dislocate it until after three, four, five, or seven days; and never leave a fracture untreated for more than twenty days, as long as the healing process continues, and the joint approaches its normal position; then tighten it more than before, and thicken the flesh as I have said previously; and if you notice that the limb is drying out more than necessary, know that treatment cannot be effective. Then apply warm water each time you dislocate it, every third day, and gently massage the area; by this means you will cure the limb, and prevent the harm caused by the foolish practices of those who twist the limb incorrectly: it is harmful and involves great risk, and I see no other solution than to leave it alone or do it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various methods of breaking (or dislocation)
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many ways of breaking bones, with various shapes and causes; for some breaks occur from the impact of a sword, and the chisel cuts through all the bone down to the soft tissue, like a hatchet or axe; and for this reason, this type of break is called "haichure" (axe-like).
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or, the sword may cut through the bone without striking it, and this is called "absolute" break; and this type of fracture has a large or small wound from these two breaks.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded impact, or a crack, or a stone chisel, or a blow on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a recent fracture, which approaches the skin just beneath the bone, or it is on top of the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound has healed around the bone so subtly like a hair, and it is a small fracture, then this dislocation is called "capillary"; and if the wound is caused by striking with stone, or falling, or something similar, and the bone fragment enters inward, and the limbs are bent as the blacksmith does when he works on the cauldrons; if it gets stuck between the stones.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often with those who have moist bones in the head, as in an infant's head; and it occurs in all these ways of fracture that small fragments are dislocated as if they were broken; and I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all the ways of fractures from traction on them, and inquiry at close range, and by the corrupt flesh that is above them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the fracture is recognized because, when the bone is discovered and rubbed with the finger, it opens up the broken fragment.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, be cautious of accidents with the sick person, and if you notice any ill omen, such as vomiting blood, loss of consciousness, extension or bending of the limbs, paleness, ague fever, sudden heat, or other similar symptoms in various dispositions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming accident and hope for healing, then begin treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fracture comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the month that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if this happens, if you hurry to remove the bone on the seventh day, so that the tissue around the bone is corrupted, then come the complications that we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone breaks down to the tissue covering the brain, it is necessary that you split the affected part in this way: and it is important that you press the patient's head with pain, and expose the bone in every way possible, and gently uncover the wound, if a pus pocket appears upon exposing the bone, or an abscess, use what is appropriate help, and fill the cavity with moist, rosin-infused cloth; then rest the wound until the abscesses subside and be sure of no further pus discharge. Then begin to remove the bone, and this should be done in two ways: one way is to cut very tightly in front, and this is its shape...
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I use another treatment even greater than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	The second method is that you have many different shapes, some narrow and others wide, and they are sharp and made of iron indelible; and perform the operation gently, so as not to damage the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and dense, you need to drill around it, so as to administer cuts with intervals, without going through the bone too deeply, and there should be a margin or curve on the tip to prevent it from passing through the bone; and you need many of these, so that each one goes in its place according to the density of the bone, so as to have intervals for all bones; and this is the form of the three types of intervals:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality to perceive around the broken bone is that you apply pressure on the bone and return to your fingers until you know the bone is perceived; then place the pressure elsewhere a little later, and do this all around, then cut with incisions the space between the cracks in the bone, and do it as subtley and lightly as possible, while handling the bone with your hand or any tool like pliers or pincers, and be careful not to touch the brain or the sinew.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have perceived and treated the bone, it is necessary that you observe the delay of tightness remaining on the bone compared to any other tool resembling an incision, but it should be more tender and subtler than the other incisor; and if it does not leave any small bones or scales, gently remove them with a suitable instrument; then treat the wound with bandages and remedies as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of treatment is that which Galen says, which is safer; it is very powerful, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you expose a part of the bone, either by opening the fracture wide enough, so that when you have exposed this part, you will place the blade of this crescent-shaped knife underneath, which has this shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, but expose the acute part on the second side, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike gently with a small hammer over it, so that you gently press the bone all around, and be very careful of the membrane that lies underneath; if it is detached from the bone, lift it gently, for it can be lifted without pain or harm.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not reach the skin, and the bone is cut only from above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to smoothen these rough edges, and remove the scales with a delicate rasp, having various quantities of it, in order to make each part as suitable as possible, according to the severity and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you encounter great rasps (or tools) and then even more subtle ones, do not stop until it is done well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair cuts and subtle fractures, it is necessary to make the correction according to its location; and this is a matter that is not easily answered for one who has dedicated their study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if it pleases him to reveal himself, you should then press the linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it with rose oil, and place it over the wound; then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and moisten it with wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth; do this as lightly as possible so as not to burden the flesh, then apply another bandage, and do not tighten it too much until it only covers the wound; leave it thus for one or two days, until the abscess is calmed down, then remove it, and administer medications such as fennel roots, meal flour, incense powder, aristology, and similar things; make a powder from these things and place it over the wound, and continue to apply medications from around the world without scarification; ensure that the wound is always clean, do not leave any treatment, nor let pus accumulate, for when pus accumulates on the skin of the head, it corrupts and rots, and causes great harm to the patient, because when a sharp object is placed over the flesh, it can pierce through.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed therefore, if no ill accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is questionable without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if darkness comes only because of the medicine placed upon it, to see if it has any virtue, then you should apply a part of honey and three parts of rose oil mixed with a cloth over the sore; then cure it in the manner of cures that are appropriate until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	You should know that the two parts of the bone above are never broken, either together or separately, because they are two bones; and the inner one is cartilage, which does not break, but only bends or twists, then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you should fit your little finger or a thin tool into the gap, and place the break back in its natural position on your index finger, and hold it there until the joint returns to its normal form; do this gently, and ensure the patient feels no pain from your actions.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the joint and the fingers cannot be moved to their normal position, you should place a thin stick across the top, slightly thicker than the finger itself.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in both parts, repeat the above process and hurry to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day (when the swelling has subsided), then place thin linen strips over the joint, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or turn to another part, if it is broken, and make the splints so thick that they fill the gaps in the bones.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say that no restoration is required to make the splints moist with butter, and each day they must be changed.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think that this is good, but it is necessary that they be moistened with egg albumen and flour powder; then remove the splints, as soon as the bones are hard and the cartilage firm.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never apply the fat of duck or goose to a wound greater than smaller, and if it becomes inflamed around it, hold the break still, and blow air into it; or do what you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess appears near a new wound while you are treating it, apply a poultice or moist cotton in rose oil, or in a small bag of hyssop.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If an abscess does not form, apply a paste made of flour and frankincense powder mixed with egg albumen, then place light bandages on it and do not tie the wound; if the fracture is small and the bone is broken into fine pieces, use suitable instruments to remove them, then clean the wound with hot things, and cure it with poultices and dressings as necessary; and if there is no injury inside the wound, treat it externally with plasters until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	from the dislocation of the mandible
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is dislocated and there is no external wound, the fracture is only slightly disrupted, not in two pieces, but it has a support from within, if you know how to recognize it gently.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is in the right side, you should insert your index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is on the left mandible, insert your index finger from your right hand, gently disrupting the fracture, and with the other hand, pull it outward, making it equal.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is severe in two places, then you must administer an extension to the lower part, as long as it remains even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the teeth occurs, or rupture, by applying tension with a golden or silver thread or silk, then place cerate on the broken jaw and put a double cloth; and place the cloth on the tooth a large star well made, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the jaw, and tie it to the muscles that you can, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you notice that the figure changes on the third day, then remove it and reset what was changed; and apply plaster above, with fine powder ground with enough egg or sesame flour after removing the cerate; and put on a thin layer of plaster, and if the plaster hardens, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it is healed; often it heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess appears, it is necessary to do as we have said many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is both a fracture and a wound together, do not attempt to remove any part of the bone that is still intact; use gentle and suitable instruments instead.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, stretch it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and it does not delay, clean the wound if it is wide, and place suitable patches on it to draw out pus, as long as it remains healthy.
de la forcele	from the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps break many times near the shoulder, and the fracture is in three manners: it may be broken and separated into two parts, with pieces, and is easiest to restore; or there is a fracture with an accompanying wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And for the work when the fracture is without a wound, you need two assistants: one should hold the aid, which is the broken forceps; and the other extends the collar towards the affected part. Then place the fracture evenly with both hands, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is no bulge or depression.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it further, place a round spike of cloth or wool beneath the shoulder of the patient, as thick as required; then stretch and gently apply force, holding the spike with your hand so that you align the break correctly.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the spike from the depth because it is stuck completely, then it is necessary for the patient to lie on his side with his shoulder beneath the spike, and have assistants raise the spike's other end until the bone of the fracture is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then address the fracture with your hands, and if you feel any debris, it is necessary to cut through; remove the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join together despite your best efforts, place a second spike beneath the first as a support.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it looks like a spoon, and is not crooked, and is as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and it has two prongs, as you see, one wide, and the other narrow, just as the cut of the wound that you made when you split the bones; and when you are sure of the hot abscess, if you cut the wound deeply, or if the incision is small, then you doubt a hot abscess, applying drapes and tenting the wound according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses occur, then moisten the drape with rose oil and linseed and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The binding of the bone, when it is sensitive to wounds and cuts, is to place on the bone the plaster of very fine powder and egg white, and lay light bandages on top, and insert a spear under the joint, if necessary; then take a very wide strip of cloth, about a palm length, and place the bandage with the plaster on it, and wrap it around the injury; take a thin, long, three-dois wide steel and wrap it around the cloth so that the edge of the cloth is hanging down; place the steel on the fracture, and turn the bandage back over the collarbone, and under the healthy joint and the affected joint; rearrange each part, and when you see that the string holds the fracture well, and clearly see that the steel does not move on the broken bone, reward it with this each day, and as the ligatures loosen, tighten them; put the patient on his back and place a small pillow under the collarbone to raise the affected area; lighten the fracture by aligning the shoulder, or tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it for twenty days unless a bad accident happens; then recommence the plastering, if necessary, tighten it, and leave it so until it is healed; it is healed in no more than 28 days, and less for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	from the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	If the shoulder is broken or dislocated, it does not respond to external touch; if you realign it according to the shape of the dislocation and restore it to its natural position in every way possible, then apply a fine powder mixed with egg yolk and a little wine, and cover it with light bandages. Place a broad and thin plate above, slightly wider than the shoulder, and secure it so that it does not move from its place; examine it daily. Whenever it tries to dislocate, tighten the bandage and realign the plate if it has moved. The patient should lie on his side, and after ten or fifteen days (or twenty-five at most), carefully release it, being sure, because it is not a bone that can be easily put back in place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone sticks out and is not pulled away from the heart, it causes inflammation, and the bone, and does what we have said in the weakening of the heat of an abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	from the weakening of the heat
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The flesh is never broken open, but it happens little; but it often breaks at the heat.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken open, it declines away from the heart, and the patient feels great pain, and weakness, and sometimes bleeds, and opens up the cheeks in the broken bone, and feels all better.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on their back, and places a cushion between their shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and aligns the ribs with both hands, subtly making them even in all ways as they should be; then apply plasters and bandages over the delicate skin of salt or another light material, and wrap it in a cloth, binding it to the broken bone so that it does not move; and turn the ligature around the back, tightening it properly, and checking the wound every hour, if it becomes softer, tighten it; if it needs to be released due to decay or itching that occurs at the site, or pain or abscess, act quickly, release it, remove the plaster, and address the cause of the condition; then apply the plaster again, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	from the fracture of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	You know that the fracture of ribs only occurs in the upper back and at the top, and they do not bend unless they are broken; and this causes great pain to anyone who suffers from it.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you put it back in place as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, tightening it with a stick if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is declining inward, it causes the patient to feel great pain and stabbing, as if from crying, because the bone pierces the skin; and he loses his breath, coughs, and vomits much blood, which is a sign of grave illness, and old physicians have devised great remedies.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And for those who say it is appropriate to administer foods that cause bloating in the stomach to push the fracture out.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not claim that hot applications will not come if they have not already arrived.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it comes back, as healthy.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say none of you should use cupping glasses on the skin, as it forms sucking marks, and this seems reasonable; nevertheless, there is doubt that the cupping glass might draw away excess fluid from the body due to its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say none of you should cover the skin with moistened wool in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to even out the heat around it, then treat the cure for pleurisy, flesh, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure by the bone that holds the skin, then doubt is in the patient, and it is necessary to cut into the broken ribcage, and put a tool to stop the bleeding; and then one must break the bone, and draw gently, and then sew together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with bandages, until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses form, one should place moist, oil-soaked rags on the affected area and put the patient on their side; and treat while the abscess is present, resting the side where it is located, until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	from the break of the collarbone
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No break occurs in the collarbone bone, and rarely does it happen if it rains; also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to a person, and you want to know if they will recover, take care to see if their hands are softening, swelling, and turning pale, and if they cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Knowing that it is deadly in many ways, if they are silent and feel well when you hold them and touch them, know that the joint of the bone is safe, and that the patient will be cured if proper treatment is given.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing occurs in the lower back, you should know if it is healthy or not, taking care if the feet are softened, and if there is an accident involving the hands, and on the back, excessive sweating and ejection without will; and when it is remembered on the belly, it has excessive ejection without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is remembered on the back and wants to press, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Knowing it is deadly: therefore, do not labor in its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen, then it is a lighter matter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is as follows: if there is an abscess that is hot, apply rose oil or egg yolk oil to it until it is soothed; then place a comforting and drying plaster on it and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where they feel pain, until they are healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is separated, it should be covered with a bandage; then remove the bone, and stitch together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, then apply a healing poultice, until it is healed; and if the fragment of the bone is broken off, which is called the "fragment of the fracture," press your palm with your left hand onto it, and place it level with your other hand, then apply the plaster and the splint, if necessary; then tighten it, and if there are any separated bones, reduce them, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	from the fracture of the bone in the shoulder blade
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	If the bone in the shoulder blade is fractured, and there is no significant reduction in size at the site, it causes the patient great pain, swelling, and inflammation at the fracture site.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over the fracture site, ensuring you understand where the fracture is and its shape; if the fracture is only at the top, then make an equal cut, maintaining its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, it declines inward, then place the patient on his stomach until the healing of that fracture becomes apparent.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And once you have made it even, place a splint on it, then put a board or a hard material over it and hold the fracture still so that it does not move; and keep the limb beneath the ribs until the bone is aligned.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess appears and is not touched, it should be calmed down until the abscess is healed, and then apply what we have previously said; and afterwards return to restoration, holding it as appropriate, unless there is some adverse event; this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the joint
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The joint (ajutoire) is that which is between the shoulder blade and the top of the shoulder, and if it is dislocated, it should be restored using one of two methods: one is to take a straight, thick stick, approximately as follows:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And hold the two feet, and bend them up, and look at the patient in a high place; then throw one broken arm over the leg, until it becomes loose, and put a piece of wood between his hands, and hang something heavy on it so that he extends his fingers together, until the fracture returns to its proper position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another method is to place the patient on his side, and tie his hand to his neck, then command the assistants to one hold what is above the fracture in his hands, and the other hold below at every joint, and extend them according to their parts.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too forceful, then hold it tight at the break, and on the break, stretch each of the assistants to their side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the break is close to the shoulder joint, it is necessary to place a moderate link below the acromion and another towards the neck, below the break; and likewise, if the break is on the side of the neck, a light link should be placed without strain, as long as the break is level on the bone, then align the break correctly and tighten it, but without causing discomfort.
