Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess forms after it has been extracted and the wound is not healed for seven days, place a moist cloth with rose oil on it until the abscess subsides; then grip it, and the way to do this is to put the splint over the fracture, then bring the arm back into position, and place your hand on the shoulder or the breast; cover it with a drape, and grip the arm and the joint, so that the arm remains immobile, unless something prevents it, or if the bone has not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt that the bone has not moved and use splints, place a wider and stronger splint on the fracture, ensuring there is a gap of two lengths between each splint, and make each splint so long that it extends three gaps from each side; then grip the splints, as I have said at the beginning of this chapter regarding the fracture, by making them stronger and farther apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the position of the stars and the constriction, as we have said, when you return the broken member, and you doubt the heat of the abscess, leave it attached for up to seven days, as we have said; then every three days examine the wound, that no inflammation arises or comes to the place, so that the healing cannot come to the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it responds, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accident happens, do not release it until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back with his hands on his stomach; place a flat cushion under the dislocated member, equally covered with wool, and observe it every hour during the day and night to ensure that the shape of the dislocated member does not move or become relaxed. If it responds to medication, give him food as we have mentioned, in such a way that the food is the finest; and when he begins to regain strength, it will be significant.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the joint and leg should be re-set after forty days; and then one must loosen and administer baths and medications with oils to correct the position.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the contraction is severe and tight, it may take forty days or two months to loosen it.
de la brisure du bras	of the dislocation of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "fossa", of which one is small, adjacent to the elbow, and the other is large, located below, towards the small bone; so sometimes only the large fossa breaks, or only the small one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, healing is light and quick; but when the large ones are broken, healing is poor and more difficult than when they were broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small bones that are broken, then it is necessary to extend slightly and align them equally.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bones, then it is necessary to pull stronger; place them on a cushion and position the palm higher than the others, with the small bones lower, crossing the patient over itself. Then, extend the healers' hands towards the part below their hand, or to the joint, and another helper above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then set it even with the eyes, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture, each piece is set in its place, and if none of them grasp the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place by making it whole again, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is an open wound, I have spoken of it in detail in the previous chapter; then take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of restoration there appear abscesses, first apply a bandage made of oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; and wrap it gently around, until the abscess is calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the plaster, and mix the pouder from the fine mill with enough egg, then place the needles, making the needle of the break more firm and a little wider than the others; know that there should be six needles or more on each arm in different positions: whether the break is in one bone or two; tighten above the break more than elsewhere, but always less distant as mentioned at the beginning of the chapter; and make the cloth covering the break soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the thread from which it is pulled be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the ligament after no days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if no adverse incident occurs in the limb, such as itching that arises in the limb, then it is necessary to raise the limb with hot water until the itching is relieved; and let the limb not be too tightly rested.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then repeat the process, and if the ligaments loosen and the bones align themselves, and such things, then address it accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if stiffness prevents the limb from moving, because it is too tight, then it is necessary to loosen it slightly and leave it for a few days until the stiffness disappears, and then tighten it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said comes to the patient, then he should be dislocated for up to twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	If uncertain, then tie his hands to his chest, ensuring his collarbones are even, and guard against movement and digitation, and have him sleep on his back. Know that this fracture is healed in thirty days or forty-five, or perhaps in twenty days, depending on the combinations and complexities of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	You know that on the back of the hand and at the joints there are often small fractures, and it brings only pain many times over.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the hand's plant is broken or bent, it is necessary that the patient cuts across the affected area, and holds it straight in front of him equally; then he places his hand on a flat surface, and extends the broken bones with the aid of another person, aligning them properly; and applies a poultice and bandages if an abscess does not form, and wraps it up in a linen drape according to the size.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is near the stomach of the hand, make a ball of cloth and instruct the patient to press it onto his broken hand; then take a long strip of cloth, and form it into a ball as large as the hand itself, and apply pressure as necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	If the fracture is at the end, then you must place one stick on top and another underneath in the socket, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind it tightly around the hand, and stop the bleeding between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If the fracture occurs in neither of the joints, and it is dislocated, place it evenly, as appropriate, and tighten it with the socket; if you see that putting a small, straight stick will raise the dislocation without moving it, do so, and bind it tightly. If the fracture is in other joints, like the index or any others, place it evenly and bind it to the healthy joint afterward; either hold all of them together firmly, or put a stick on top, as with a dislocated joint. Take care during restoration and positioning near the abscess, and support what comes, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	from the broken hip
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The hip bone is often broken, and one can clearly see it when it returns to its position in front and behind; its restoration is achieved by binding it tightly over the break and from below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each limb extends equally to its side; this is when the break is between the bones.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the hip, one must bind the limb towards the knee, and the others bind below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is close to the knee, then the ligaments of the knee should be loosened, and the extension adjusted; then place the splint with both hands, so that it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster and tie it, so that there are no further problems.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, leave it to heal, then return to your work and treatment; the bandage is made in this way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary to wrap the broken leg with a hard bandage, cutting off the excess, and then return the leg until the heels reach the root of the toe, and insert a long thread between the thigh and the leg below the knee, and come up with the thread over the top of the leg bone; then place the splint on top. Put a star on the bone of the leg; then take the remaining cloth and make eight folds between the leg and the thigh to ensure equal tension, then start tying three or four turns around the splint; and as you go higher on the splint, loosen it; then take the two threads that you have threaded between the leg and the thigh, and tie three stars on top, then return to the bottom with the thread, until you reach below the foot; and tighten it, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, and if there is no further problem, no abscess or swelling or anything similar.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens that it becomes dislocated, and you address what comes, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that cling, it is necessary to do so whenever possible; and if it cannot be done, it is necessary to break the joint and pull out the foreign body; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never should the foot be broken in this way with staples, as is done in the aid of the arm; nevertheless, in this way of restoration, it does not benefit the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the foot is restored in 7 to 10 days, or a little less or a little more, depending on the diversity of the constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the alley of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	You know that in the alley of the knee there is little breaking, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, even if it is only a crack or a hole, it becomes an open wound, and feels like a wound, but the patient feels no pain.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is when you put back what is broken in its place, as much as it can be adjusted; then apply the poultice, and put a round bandage if necessary, and tighten it appropriately, then follow all the arrangements that we have mentioned for other fractures, like an abscess above or any similar condition; apply whatever is suitable for each case, as long as it heals.
de la brisure de la jambe	from the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	You know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called "the thigh bone" and the other "the shin bone"; and a fracture occurs in the leg just as it does in the arm, and its treatment is similar to that of the arm equally. And if both bones are broken together, the leg recovers from all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, they heal forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, it causes great pain, and its deformity is visible; and it heals slowly.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then apply an extension, and set it even, and tie the stars equally; but nevertheless, it is necessary that the fracture be ugly, and there are several parts, so that the extension is less and lighter; and alight according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your task, take two strips of cloth that are red and cover the leg on both sides, extending from the knee to the ankle; then wrap two bands around it above and below, and tie them in the middle, so the leg cannot bend to the right or left, and thus is well. And no one should apply any bandage along the length of the leg, but if it is made of cloth, place the leg to prevent movement, and properly treat the fracture where there is an abscess or any other accident; move the leg each day to see if there is a relapse or another complication; and cure it as soon as it heals.
de la brisure des os dou piet	from the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but the bones of the foot can be fractured in various places and there is no strong reason for it to occur in any particular disposition.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	If the bones of the foot are fractured and you see them stacked on top of each other, so that the patient feels great pain in their foot on the ground, just as if they wanted to walk, then put your foot on theirs, raising the broken bones, and press it until they return to their proper place; then apply a splint and bandages above, and under the belly of the foot, a small wooden board with two holes, then tighten it around the foot properly, and wrap it with cloth and other things as needed.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And after three days or four have passed, if you loosen the bandage, for you will find the bones even, either broken or discolored.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if none of the bones are broken, and they need to be restored, as we have said regarding the hand's joints, then take a stick according to the length of the bone and make it slightly wider, and place the cloth from beneath, as I have said, tightly around it; and if there are two or three, or more, broken bones, take a stick for each, wrapped in a piece of linen, and bind the cloth beneath the foot; and let the edge of the cloth extend over the top of the table, towards the belly of the foot, so that it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other breaks, when we have discussed them; and treat each accident as it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	On the break of the bone in the hand.
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When a woman's bone in her hand is broken and the swelling subsides, then tilt her body towards the affected part, holding it from behind. Next, fill the space with cotton and also pack it tightly; then raise the woman up slightly, and gently massage her back, little by little, until the cotton reaches the opening of the wound, and the bone returns to its place. If she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and after she has urinated, replace it, and do this for seven or eight days. Then the break will be healed, and if she still has pain, take a bladder of goat's hair, tie a tube to the opening, and completely fill the bladder inside the wound. Blow into the tube until the bladder is inflated within: the nature will heal the break; then pack it with cotton and leave it like this for several days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of a man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said in the hipbone; and these fractures are not hidden from one who puts their study and skill into it, and listens to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture indicates various arrangements for the right way of restoration: understand this therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	When a stick is broken, take a goose throat and insert it into the stick; then wrap cloth around it, and leave it for three or four days until it heals naturally.
de brisure avec plaie	from fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is important for someone with a fracture and a wound, especially if it is large, such as the bones of the leg or shoulder or similar, to seek medical attention immediately, so that the healing process we have described can begin.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, but there is still residue of poison, and you have no other remedy, then begin to restore the fracture in the same hour or day that the abscess appears.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the abscess appears again, leave the healing until it is completely healed, and do not touch it for at least a day or two, lest you bring on a bad outcome.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone appears on the heart's surface when it is exposed, you should gently place your hands over it with slight pressure and a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension does not appear to be equal on both hands, take this instrument made of iron, with seven or eight inches in length, and adjust its width according to the size of the wound; and for this purpose, it should immerse three or four times, depending on what is needed for each fracture treatment; and it should be round and slightly thicker, so that it does not bend under pressure on the limb during your work, but rather is sharp in front and thick in the middle.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", so that the dislocated bone should be placed on the visible head of the joint; and press it once, until it returns, and becomes even one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, it is necessary that you hold the head of the bone, while the instrument has purchase.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back, as we have said, with a suitable instrument, such as a chisel or a saw, within your power, then remove what is remaining in the bone of roughness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reduced, and the patient feels great pain afterward, knowing that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do your best to put it back in its natural place, then moisten the cloth with a drying wine and apply it properly; do not put any bandage or other substance on the wound that has oil, otherwise it will cause putrefaction and corruption. Then administer herbs once you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover it around according to the size of the wound, and be very careful that the wound is not constricted by the break; and many times this has caused great harm to the patient, or even death, or corrosion. And the compresses should be milder and softer than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or great, and you doubt that a bad accident may come of it, as we have said, and feel pain in place, if it is not suitable to lay on bandages; but cover around, instead of bandages, with hard cloth, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days the wound swelling, then remove what you have put on it, and apply healing ointment to the wounds, such as four-ingredient ointments and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the member twice a day, in the morning and evening, as long as it is swollen and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be dislocated in such a way that the bowstring moves slightly downward.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it persists for many days, and it cannot heal but keeps reverting to the bow position, knowing that there are small fragments of bone, then you must want to open the wound with a knife and remove all these unwanted pieces causing the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula appears in its place, or any other form of corruption, it is necessary that you treat it according to what it says in the chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when a bone is broken and opens up on the limb, such as the bone of the calf or the shoulder, or other similar bones of large limbs, do not pull it, for death often results, but let it fester until it heals; perhaps after twenty days or thirty, then treat the wound if you can; if not, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	burns that come from the solder
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the healing of the burn, especially when it is near a joint, and it is a terrible sight to see the disfigurement of the limb; and by chance, it may not be able to perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then, if we must treat it: if we administer astringent medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, so that you press any of these things or all together, and preserve them in stoppers with astringent wine or with abundance of heat or with cold; and place them on the wound firmly, and do not loosen them for many days; and then dislocate it, and begin another, until the swellings are removed; or you press a well-made plug of lead, for the property of lead is to remove all swelling from the limbs; and if the nodulation has already turned into hardness like stone, it must be removed, cutting off the excess above, and making it apparent; or you shave it with a razor, until it is removed, and treat it as long as it is healthy.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The weak member after treatment.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored and the weak and delicate member remains, it happens for many reasons: one is because it was tied too tightly and not tied as it should be; or because there are too many bindings and it cannot assume the normal shape of the member; or due to excessive bleeding; or because of too great movements, not at the right time; or because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body firm, until the blood flow multiplies within him; then administer baths, and give joy and relaxation; then apply pitch to the member, so that the pitch attracts great blood flow, and often moisten it with warm water, until the circulation reaches the member, and it recovers its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	Both members are twisted after health.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the members are twisted after restoration, and the bones are broken open, and the form of the member is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the foolish ones who say one must break the member from the very beginning, and many foolish practices have been done in our land; these practices are blameworthy, and great harm, and perhaps death, come from them. Nevertheless, if the dislocations and tortures are fresh, it is necessary that they be treated with hot water, or gentle herbs cooked, such as fennel leaves, roots, melilot, and similar things; and apply an emollient, like a good-made ointment, and take the mucilaginous part of fennel, and mix it with goose fat or sesame oil, and make an ointment from it. Or you can use fig fats, and grind them with colon powder, and similar medicines that reduce inflammation.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never should the node be broken by continuous and lengthy friction with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And allow the limb to move every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the swelling and hardness is like stone, and needs to be cut with iron, then it should be done carefully just below the bone, with a subtle, light incision; and apply compression and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book on dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocations occur from a joint moving out of place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs unexpectedly, it may be necessary to act immediately to reduce the pain.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Because if treatment is delayed, the limb may swell, and upon resetting it, one might cause additional pain; therefore, it is not advisable to move the limb when it is inflamed. Often, this leads to swelling and other pains. However, once the inflammation subsides, the patient should be made comfortable, then apply hot water and oil, gently reset the dislocation, and treat each member as appropriate for its specific condition.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations of the shoulder joint all the way to the foot.
des mandibules	of the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Sometimes the mandibles are dislocated, and this dislocation occurs in two ways: either they are slightly out of their sockets, somewhat bent; or they are completely dislocated, hanging down towards the chest, and preventing the mouth from closing, so that the person cannot hold saliva in their mouth, cannot close their lips, and their tongue moves around with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns to its proper position through more or less orderly arrangements.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is entirely and fully healed, then you must reset it forcefully, without delay; in such a way that the healers place their hand firmly on the patient's head, and pull the lower jaw gently from the root of the dislocation inside the mouth, where the dislocation is from two parts; and the other two hands should be extended, making them equal. Then command the patient to soften his jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And make the other hand equal, until it returns to its proper place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is brought back, it should be carefully done, especially when both jaws are involved, by using hot water and oil, gently realigning them; do not delay in bringing them back, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are realigned equally, and the patient's mouth closes well without straining, moistened bandages made of rose oil and wax should be applied, then gently tied with soft ropes; and let the patient sleep on their back, with their jaws resting between two pillows, so that they do not move to either side, nor make any efforts to open them wider, but gently chew soft food until the pain is gone and the jaws are healed; and then eat what they wish, without opening the mouth wide for eating or drinking, until the jaw is fully healed and strong.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be properly aligned within an hour and do not return to their original position, then there follow fevers and persistent pains, and perhaps intestinal distress or purulent vomiting.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, know that it is a sign of great danger; and often those who experience it die within seven days.
de la forcelle	(referring to) the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The fork cannot be dislocated from any side within the continuity of it, and it is never dislocated properly outside, and one feels it very much.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back and extends his arms; then he presses the joint firmly in your palm, and it will return; then apply the plaster and bandage and tighten it; and the part that is towards the shoulder cannot dislocate; if it does not, or if it dislocates once, then you must put it back into its place, as we have said; then apply the plaster and bandage and tighten it, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed; and in this way the part of the shoulder is also brought back when it is out of its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	**Shoulder Dislocation**
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	You know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: one is when it dislocates at the acromion process; the second is at the part of the scapula; and sometimes dislocates towards the top, which is rare; and it does not dislocate behind the shoulder, nor inside the nerves; often it dislocates downward toward the acromion, especially in those with little muscle, because to them it goes easily; but for those with sufficient muscle, it barely dislocates, and returns barely.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to no one that a bone is shattered or broken, and causes an abscess in the hot shoulder, and they think it's dislocated because of that.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is necessary for you to test it, until you are certain; and then begin treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And dislocations are known when they turn towards the joint, and distinguish between the affected and healthy shoulder, and you will find their diversity manifest; and you will find in the top of the shoulder a hollow place, and by pressing on it, feel the top of the shoulder as if it were one; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his body, or move in any way; and also, if it is dislocated higher up, unless it is hidden, for you will find it manifestly by touch; and this type of dislocation is not merely to be reduced when it is new, or if the enemy is afflicted.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the healer places his hand on top of the patient's ill limb, then puts his palm beneath the joint, and pulls the joint upward with force towards the bone; and the healer lifts his hand and extends it overhead, then places it underneath; this will bring relief.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	If it does not come as described above, within a few days, then the patient must be bathed in hot water; administer gently a soothing and softening treatment, such as an infusion of fennel and melilot in water, and attend to them. Then, have the patient lie on their back and place a piece of equal thickness of wool beneath the joint, not too soft or too hard, then position their heel on it, and with care, pull up the head of the shoulder; massage the hand of the patient who has the illness, so that it does not move. This will correct the shoulder immediately, as you can see if done correctly: and make sure there is a witness present, someone stronger than the patient, who stands by the side of the bed, straight against the patient's ribcage; pull the patient's shoulder away from the joint beneath it with their hand, pulling it upward so that the patient's arm hangs down. Another assistant should massage the hand of the patient with the illness downward towards their stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, so that any heavy thing causes him trouble, then the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is also remedied in another way: take a long stick and insert it into the ground so that the end of it is as bright as a pistol, neither too thick nor too thin; then place it under the patient, but ensure there are soft rags on top, and the patient's limb is extended along its length; then bend the patient's hand downwards from the other side, forming an arch, and the joint will return to its place naturally; and if it does not want to come back for all the reasons we have said, do this cure: take a stick from both arms, wide enough for four fingers, with a pointed end that can enter completely under the bone, according to this shape.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then he places a heavy cloth over the head, so that it does not hurt the patient, and puts the affected limb on top; then he extends his arm above the head, and attaches the aid to the head, and the arm to the wrist of the hand, then places the arm on the edge of a wide spatula, and extends his hand downwards, and lets the body hang from the other side: the joint is now realigned.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is aligned in any way, it is necessary that you place beneath the limb a spike of equal wool, then apply a poudered plaster device with incense and eagle's egg, over all the shoulder and around, then remove the spike from the limb carefully, and tie the bandage again on the plaster, and embrace the hand to his chest, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he move the dislocated part little by little, as long as the limb is comfortable, because it will heal faster; and then after one or two days he can move it; and if it remains stiff and is not softened, then it heals.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is stiff due to moisture or any other cause, it is necessary that you apply fire cautery in three places, as described in the chapter on cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and after seven days the dislocation releases but the joint does not hold, and the patient cannot raise his arm above his head, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is cut, stretched or damaged; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place again.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the worst side, and affects the joints, often occurs due to a sudden movement or stretch of the hands, and should be treated immediately; and cure as soon as it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after healing, if the member suffers from stiffness and movement is delayed, the patient often uses their hands repeatedly until the stiffness disappears and it returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation, cost
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the dislocated joint is weakened to a degree, and it returns slightly; but if it is dislocated from all sides, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not corrected because one can see and feel it well, then it is treated according to its form.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the diseased part with the healthy one, if you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm, nor reach its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it in such a way that the vein does not close again, for if the vein closes after resetting it, it will be difficult to bring it back, especially when it is at the rear; it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and possibly death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is possible when it can be brought back, that you extend his hand with both of yours; and his arms should be spread out, and the hands turned towards each other according to the cost around, from inside and outside, and bring the joint to his palms together, or to the base of his palm, until he returns to his place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his palm, and turn the base of the palm towards the joint that is out of place.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, apply a strong extension; and have the other minister extend the arm, and press it with his hand so that it does not move at the extension; then turn the arm from each side, after you have wrapped a double long and wide cloth around it; and when you see the joint aligned with the hand, rub it with no oil to soften the joint, then pull the joint firmly, until it returns; and once it is in place, apply dry plaster with egg white, and strain the limb, and bend the arm towards the patient's chest, and leave it for several days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is firm in its place, loosen the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not pull well, repeat the splint and bandage, and leave it for a few days, until it is firmly set; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if the patient feels pain after resetting the joint, and it becomes stiff, bathe and massage it gently, applying pressure until it is relaxed; or place a piece of fat sheep's wool on the joint, leave it for a day and night, then remove it, and give the patient a bath. And when the swelling has gone down, rub the joint temperately, then apply the wool again, and repeat this process twice or three times until it is healed; and if necessary, use fine moist warm wax with butter, and strain it over the joint. Then it will return to its normal position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The hand joint moves slightly and returns to its place, more so than other joints. It is important to bring it back into place gently, especially if the limb is swollen or an abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And when you bring it back, place the patient's hand on a table and extend their fingers, ensuring they are even, so that the palm rests over the joint, holding it in this position until it returns to its place. But it is important to check if it is back in its proper place; then place the patient's hand with the back of their hand on a table for extension and bringing it back.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, have the patient lie down on their hand on a table, and look closely at the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, then this is good; otherwise, if the pain of soothing abscesses persists, and it does not begin to heal,
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place for several days, then the joint remains crooked; and it does not cause any harm to the patient while the hand is swollen, and nothing can be extracted: then know that a nerve or an artery is severed; there is no other mechanism by which cautery can be used to extract it, and perhaps there is nothing else that helps.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, if you put the plaster we have mentioned on it, then pull it and leave it for a day, then loosen it and leave it so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well and there is no fracture, then moisten it with hot water and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	on the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	The fingers of the hand should never be dislocated at each joint, neither at the back of the palm nor on the palm's surface; then pull the finger and straighten the dislocation as it regrows, then hold the top of the finger, and bend it towards the joint where it is separated; leave it for a day, and then repeat this process every day until it heals; and do not bind it, as we have said, but loosen it each day and move it, and then re-bind it; and do so often, while it remains stiff, and also do the same if it is dislocated on the palm surface, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and also do this when it is dislocated elsewhere.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	dislocation of the spine
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine or the neck is dislocated, and there is no cure, the patient's condition worsens quickly, leading to death.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the patient's limbs jump spontaneously without their will, they cannot hold them, and often the muscles of the legs or arms or both become weak, and sometimes the spine becomes rigid in four parts; the part that becomes rigid at the back is called "gycosis". The treatment for this is to reward the patient if the gycosis has been present since childhood; if there is no cure or recovery from it.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And for that which comes from a fall or impacts or similar events, the ancient methods of treatment speak in grand words, offering no great benefit; but I have abbreviated it according to my understanding and formed tools in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the stiffness that comes to the penis facing down, no one has a remedy; and also for that which comes straight to the side, and it cannot be cured from outside except by the one who comes to the back, as I said; and it is that the patient should lie on his face equally in the first position, and have traction underneath him so he does not move; then insert a stick into the ground forming an angle, and another at the pelvis, and tie a band around the patient's limbs, and another at the ankles, and at the knees, and at the wrists; and these practitioners know the bands, one on the head and the others on the feet, among the two sticks; and they should be well secured, the stick as we have said, and let the pain come back.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this treatment, take a table three feet long, cut through the wall from behind, place the patient on their side, and turn the head of the table away from the wall; then place the middle of the table over the spine, and put both feet under the other end of the table, pressing firmly until it returns to its place; and if you see fit, do this in a rotating motion that turns towards your hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And take two sticks, each a foot long, and place them at the head of the patient on one side, and insert two more below the feet on the other side; between each stick, dig a groove deep and wide enough, and make an opening in each stick through which it can rotate, so that they do not move; and between the two rotating sticks, there should be a smaller stick to facilitate rotation. Then tie the stick that connects the handles to the rotating part near the head, and the other handle to the feet at the other end, and let each assistant turn their handle until the entire spine is aligned as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, apply a dry plaster with plenty of heat, then the compresses, and then the end of a tablet three fingers long, which should adhere to the area of the gibbosity and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a bandage, as we have said, and use the patient's gentle rest, until they are healed; and if any thing comes about at the end of health, then it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the help that we have mentioned above; and never should a piece of bone be administered, nor does it ever appear in the rear spine, and one should not think it is dislocation; and it is the opening of the joint, for which one must not have presumption, for perhaps death would come about.
des dislocations de la hainche	Of dislocations of the neck.
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	You know that the joints of the neck and the joints of the shoulder only result in dislocations, unlike other joints; and the joint of the neck is misaligned according to four parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more so inside, and less so at the front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation within is such that when you join the affected leg with the healthy one, it becomes longer, and opens up the affected knee more than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their knee fully; and it is the inflammation around the abscess above that causes this, because the root of the thigh comes over here.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him who experiences this in the dying, it is that this event is contrary to what has been said before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him who experiences this beforehand, it is that his leg is sound according to its strength; nevertheless, do not bend the knee without pain, and if one wishes to make it walk, it cannot do so until later, and it retains urine, and the ankle swells, and when he tries to stand, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who experiences this afterward, it is that he cannot extend or bend his knee, and one leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the muscle of the thigh sticks to the bone along the sides.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	They must reset this appearance of dislocation if it is an old dislocation that persists according to its nature, as there is no cure; and one must not let him have any pride.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for him whose dislocation is fresh, and it is one of the four types of dislocation, act quickly to reset the joint, bringing it back inside and aligning it correctly, both forward and backward; perhaps then it will return, and no other treatment is needed.
