Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, one must use a strong assistant, extending the leg strongly with two hands or binding it at the knee; another assistant should place his hand above in such a way that he flexes his hands beneath his armpits, then pulls firmly on a strong ligament on the calf; another should hold the head with a ligament; and all at once extend it upward and downward until the patient is lifted from the ground and remains still.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to all three positions, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If it is not, then it is necessary to take care of this appearance. When the dislocation is in the hidden place, it is good that you remind the patient of his healthy side, then tie him to the root of the thigh, and the limb that is detached from the wound, then extend the tie upwards towards the wound and against the force; then ask another helper to grasp the patient's arms, and embrace the large limb of the afflicted thigh, and stretch it in the opposite direction: it will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot hold it in the manner we have said, then it is necessary that you bind both feet of the patient together with a strong, soft cord on their heels and knees, and let the sick leg be extended two fingers longer than the others; then hang it from the top of a post, and let it hang above the ground by two long arms; then command the assistant to embrace the head of the thigh, and have other assistants hanging with the patient, who embrace the thigh, for the joint will now return healthily.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when dislocation is outside, if the patient lies as we have said in the case of gilbosity, then tighten the bandage precisely on the sick leg and also on the foot; then place two hot coals, one at the head and one at the foot, and insert a hot coal between the cuisses of the patient, forming it; and surround him with wet cloths so that he does not hurt himself, then stretch each assistant towards him, and make them put their hands equally on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it does not return, place it on a table and press it as we have said in the previous section, and lay the patient on their healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to stretch the diseased leg forcibly, as I have said; and place the bandage so that the pain does not remain on the sore angle, then press with the other hand and stretch it downward towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is in the joint, it does not suit to extend the patient down or lift him up from the ground, but rather he should remain as his hip was dislocated earlier, just as we have said gently on both hips; and it should be done on his face, and the limb extended as we have said before, and all should press on the joint on the table. And it will be perfect when the patient extends his legs, and they will be even. Then adjust the thighs, and apply the plaster, and wrap a bandage tightly so that the hip does not move; and rest for three or four days, then release him and apply the plaster again; and if you see them to be even, tighten as before, and leave it for three days. Then release it, and make him go gently until the member is healed.
de la dislocation dou genoil	From the dislocation of the knee.
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The patient is dislocated in three ways: internally, externally, and posteriorly; but not anteriorly.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg at the knee, and if he does not release it at the knee, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place his face on your hand, and place his foot on yours. Then take the patient's knee in your palms, and pull gently between your fingers, then bend both sides of the knee joint; and another assistant extends the patient's foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he releases his leg slightly at the knee. And apply a poultice, and raise the leg at the knee, and bind them together firmly for three or four days, then release it; and let not the patient move about, until the member is comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not fully extended, apply strong stretching as we have said in the treatment of the shoulder, as long as it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	On the dislocation of the heel.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is neither completely dislocated nor fully aligned, and it moves both inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and there is tension before the part that is dislocated; the reduction is light, and one should gently extend their hand to it when it is slightly dislocated.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated from all sides, it is necessary that you make the patient lie straight, and hold him by the leg, above the ankle; then take the foot in your right hand, and twice with your left, then stretch it up high, and nicely bring the foot up high; do this twice more, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, begin the work again, for it will return; and if it cannot return in this way, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and insert a firm stick between his thighs, and wrap cloth around him so he does not hurt himself; then have each assistant hold the thigh, and others extend the foot to his hands or to the ankle, that it be held fast with the foot; then stretch each assistant equally, and the stick should remain between the patient's thighs to keep him in place when stretched; then put the mirrors equally on both sides of the dislocation, and another assistant hold the healthy leg from below, and the dislocation will return firmly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is at the right length, he should apply a poultice and compress, forming a strain around it, and fasten the foot to the leg, securing the stirrups behind on the ankle, so that the ligature is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the strain subsides, remove it on the third or fourth day, and let the patient walk for four days; and if he improves further, it is not certain that he will not recover completely.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess forms, it is necessary to calm it, as we have said elsewhere, while it is still healthy.
des dois	Of these two things
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the fingers are dislocated, if they need to be extended without strain, it is a light matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any other part of the foot or leg, it is necessary that you make the patient lie on their back or on a table completely upright, and place your foot on what opens up from the joints, then press with your foot in a forming motion until it returns; and when it is even and nothing opens, place a wooden block under the sole of the foot, then pull it with force, and leave it for three days, then release it; and make them rest until they are healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	From wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation and it needs to be restored, often the patient dies if they are not careful in its treatment; so, do not be presumptuous in the cure, if you are not skilled in the art and have not used it for a long time, nor quick or merciful or tardy. In the beginning, use hot poultices on the abscess, and leave the patient in God's hands, if there is no hope of healing; but when there is hope, now reposition the limb to its place, so that the abscess heats from below; and when the limb is in place, administer soothing poultices on the abscess, and treat the wound as appropriate with desiccated herbs; and if with dislocation there are broken bones and small bones are out of place, reset them, and do what we have said for simple diseases; and beware to enter a path of fear, according to what I have said, because that will move you according to your Creator, and for the knowledge of your arm and body.
Amen	Indeed
